Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Imam Saying Takbir and Tasmee' Aloud
Ruling with Prophetic proofs on imam's vocalization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's vocalization of takbir and tasmee' and identify the proofs that establish it as a confirmed sunnah.

Core Idea
The imam must say all takbirs and tasmee' aloud so followers know when to move — this is a confirmed sunnah.

In congregational prayer, the imam leads and the followers follow. For the followers to follow correctly, they must hear the imam's commands. This lesson explains that the imam must say every takbir (Allahu Akbar) and the tasmee' (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) aloud. The Hanafi school considers this a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah). We will examine the textual proofs from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the matn
Read the author's statement: 'وجهر الامام بالتكبير والتسميع' — the imam saying takbir and tasmee' aloud. Identify that this is listed among the sunan of prayer.
The ruling is not fard or wajib; it is sunnah.
2
Identify the sunnah level
From the hadeeth evidence and the author's treatment, this is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah). The imam's omission is makruh tanzihan (lightly disliked), but the prayer remains valid.
There is no intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.
3
Locate the primary hadith proofs
Three hadiths are cited: (1) Abu Huraira reports the Prophet said takbir when standing and bowing. (2) Ibn Mas'ud reports the Prophet said takbir at every lowering and raising. (3) The Prophet instructed followers to say 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' when the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'.
All hadiths are from authentic collections (Bukhari, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Abu Dawud).
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The consistent practice of the Prophet implies audibility because the followers acted upon hearing the takbir. The third hadith explicitly connects the imam's vocal tasmee' to the followers' response, proving it must be audible.
The dalala (indication) is zanni, hence it yields a sunnah ruling, not fard.
5
Note the practical implementation
At every transition (standing, bowing, prostrating, rising), the imam says 'Allahu Akbar' audibly. Upon rising from ruku', he says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' audibly. Followers respond silently with 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'.
This ensures orderly congregational prayer.

Thamarat al-Najah, Vol. 1, p. 284. Section on the Sunnahs of Prayer. (41) And the imam saying the takbir and tasmee' aloud. (418) And spacing the feet in standing to the extent of four fingers. Lexicon: 'Tata' al-ra's': head bowed; 'tata' translated as bowing the head. Translation: (417) [13] The imam saying all takbirs - [14] and 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' loudly. Explanation: At every takbir of the imam, the follower goes into bowing and prostration, so it is necessary for the imam to say all takbirs aloud, and similarly 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' aloud so that the follower can rise from bowing. Proof: (1) In a hadith, the Prophet used to say takbir when going into bowing and prostration. I heard Abu Huraira say: When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say takbir when he stood, then takbir when he bowed. (Bukhari, chapter on takbir when rising from prostration, p.109, no.789). This hadith shows that when going into bowing and prostration, the imam says takbir aloud; this is sunnah. (2) From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: The Prophet used to say takbir at every lowering and raising, standing and sitting, and so did Abu Bakr and Umar. (Tirmidhi, chapter on takbir at bowing and prostration, p.70, no.253; Nasa'i, chapter on takbir for prostration, p.150, no.1084; Abu Dawud, chapter on completion of takbir, p.129, no.836). This hadith indicates he said takbir when rising and sitting, i.e., aloud. (3) In a hadith, from Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say: Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd.' (Bukhari, chapter on virtue of Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd, p.129, no.796; Tirmidhi, chapter on what a man says when he raises his head, p.74, no.267). This hadith shows that the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah aloud so that the follower can say Rabbana laka al-hamd.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents the second and third sunan of prayer: the imam saying all takbirs audibly and saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' audibly. The author first provides the matn that the imam should vocalize the takbir and tasmee'. He then explains the rationale: the followers need to hear the takbir to know when to change postures, and they need to hear the tasmee' to know when to rise from ruku' with the appropriate response. He then provides three hadith proofs: the first from Abu Huraira establishes the general practice of the Prophet saying takbir at each movement; the second from Ibn Mas'ud confirms that the Prophet said takbir at every motion; the third explicitly commands that when the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', the followers should respond with 'Rabbana laka al-hamd', which necessitates that the imam says it aloud so they can hear. These hadiths are all from the authentic collections (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Abu Dawud). The Hanafi ruling is clear: the imam must say takbir and tasmee' audibly; this is a sunnah mu'akkadah. There is no intra-Hanafi dispute on this point. The passage also briefly treats the linguistic meaning of 'tata' ar-ra's' (bowing the head), a term from the previous lesson.

Key Terms
التسميع (al-tasmee'): Saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (Allah hears the one who praises Him) by the imam when rising from bowing.
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' at each transition in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the imam saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' in prayer?
A) It must be said silently.
B) It is sunnah to say it aloud.
C) It is wajib to say it aloud.
D) It is optional.

Key Takeaway
All takbirs and the tasmee' must be said aloud by the imam in congregational prayer; this is a confirmed sunnah with clear prophetic proof.

Spacing Between Feet in Qiyam (Standing)
Third sunnah: feet should be spaced about four fingers apart while standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah regarding foot spacing during prayer and explain the proof from the command 'i'tadilu'.

Core Idea
Stand naturally; the sunnah spacing of four fingers derives from the command to stand straight.

In the Hanafi school, the posture during qiyam includes a recommended separation of the feet. This lesson explores the ruling, its basis in the hadith of the Prophet commanding 'i'tadilu' (stand straight), and the natural deduction that leads to the four-finger measurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the spacing of the feet while standing in prayer. The ruling is that it is a sunnah (recommended) to have a gap of about four fingers.
This is a sunnah ghayr muakkadah, not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A hadith from Abu Dawud: the Prophet said 'i'tadilu' (stand straight) when commanding the companions to straighten their rows.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, giving zanni thubut and zanni dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The command 'stand straight' implies a natural posture. When one stands naturally, the feet are about four finger-widths apart. Thus the sunnah is deduced from the general command.
No explicit mention of four fingers; it is an inference from natural human stance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Some early Muslims, like Ibn al-Zubayr, prayed with feet together. Other schools may not specify a measurement. The Hanafi school maintains the four-finger recommendation as a moderate practice.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf in fiqh.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The mufta bihi is about four fingers, but moderate spacing is acceptable. The proof from the hadith combined with natural practice is considered sufficient.
The tarjih is based on the principle that the command 'i'tadilu' includes all aspects of standing straight.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۴۱۸)[۱۵] قیام میں دونوں قدموں کی کشادگی چار انگلی کی مقدار ہو۔
تشریح : قیام میں دونوں قدموں کی کشادگی چار انگلی کی مقدار ہو، اس کے لئے کوئی حدیث یا اثر نہیں ملی ۔ مصنف کا اصل مقصد یہ ہے کہ آدمی عام حالات میں جو اپنی ہیئت پر کھڑا ہوتا ہے اس بیت پر کھڑا ہو، پاؤں بہت چوڑے نہ کرے۔ اور اپنی ہیئت پر کھڑا ہوگا تو دونوں پاؤں کے درمیان کا فاصلہ چار انگلی ہو گا۔ خود کھڑا ہو کر دیکھ لیں۔
وجه : (۱) عن انس بهذا الحديث قال ان رسول الله الا الله كان اذا قام الى الصلوة أخذه بيمينه ثم التفت فقال اعتدلوا سووا صفوفكم ثم اخذه بيساره فقال اعتدلوا سووا صفوفکم ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب تسوية الصفوف ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۶۷۰) اس حدیث میں اعتدلوا، ہے، سیدھے کھڑے ہو جاؤ، اور سیدھا کھڑا ہوگا تو دونوں پاؤں اپنی ہیئت پر رکھنا ہوگا اور اس وقت دونوں پاؤں کا درمیانی فاصلہ چار انگلی کی مقدار ہوتا ہے۔ (۲) اخبرني من رای ابن الزبير يصلى قد صف بين قدميه و الزق احدهما بالاخرى - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من کان یصف قدمیہ، ج ثانی ، ص 11 نمبر ۔
Translation: (418) [15] The spacing between both feet in standing should be the measure of four fingers. Explanation: The spacing between the feet should be four fingers. No explicit hadith or narration was found for this. The author's main point is that a person should stand in his natural posture, not spreading the feet very wide. When standing naturally, the distance between the feet will be about four fingers. One can check by standing. Proof: (1) From Anas: The Prophet, when he stood for prayer, would take hold of his right side, then turn and say: 'Stand straight, straighten your rows,' then take hold of his left side and say: 'Stand straight, straighten your rows.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on straightening rows, p.106, no.670). In this hadith, 'i'tadilu' means stand straight; when standing straight, one must place the feet naturally, and then the distance between them is about four fingers. (2) Someone told me that Ibn al-Zubayr used to pray, placing his feet together and sticking one to the other. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who used to place their feet together, vol.2, p.11, no...)
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah of foot spacing during the standing portion of prayer (qiyam). The matn states that the feet should be separated by approximately four fingers. The commentator notes that there is no explicit hadith specifying this exact measurement; rather, it is deduced from the natural posture of standing. The proof is taken from two sources: (1) a hadith from Anas where the Prophet commands the companions to stand straight ('i'tadilu'), which implies a natural stance with moderate foot spacing; (2) an athar (report) that Ibn al-Zubayr prayed with his feet close together, which may indicate that even close spacing is permissible. The commentator emphasizes that the measurement is approximate, derived from human nature: if one stands straight without conscious adjustment, the feet will naturally be about four finger-widths apart. The Hanafi school considers this a sunnah; spreading the feet excessively wide or pressing them together is against the sunnah. This ruling is based on the general command to stand straight and the practice of the early Muslims.

Key Terms
تفريج القدمين (tafriq al-qadamayn): Separating the feet from each other while standing in prayer.
الاعتدال (al-i'tidal): Standing straight and upright in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the recommended distance between the feet while standing in prayer?
A) Feet should be touching each other.
B) Feet should be shoulder-width apart.
C) About four finger widths apart.
D) No specific spacing; it is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah of foot spacing in prayer is derived from the general command to stand straight, not from a specific proof, making it a flexible practice.

Length of Surah After Fatiha Based on Prayer
Ruling on which surahs to recite after Fatiha in each prayer for a resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which surah lengths (tiwal/awsat/qisar al-mufassal) are sunnah to recite after al-Fatiha in each of the five daily prayers for a resident.

Core Idea
Recitation length after Fatiha varies by prayer: long in Fajr/Zuhr, medium in Asr/Isha, short in Maghrib — a sunnah for the resident.

This passage presents a clear and fundamental ruling from the Hanafi school: the length of the additional surah recited after al-Fatiha in prayer depends on the specific prayer time. For a resident (muqim), the practice is divided into three categories of the Mufassal section of the Qur'an. Understanding this ruling helps you adhere to the established sunnah in your daily prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer time
Determine which of the five daily prayers you are performing. The ruling differs for Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha.
The ruling applies only to a resident (not a traveler).
2
Recall the three Mufassal categories
The Mufassal is divided into long (tiwal), middle (awsat), and short (qisar). Know which surahs fall into each category.
Long: from Surah Qaf/Hujurat to 'Amma; Middle: from 'Amma to Duha; Short: from Duha to end.
3
Apply the ruling
Match the prayer to the recommended length: Fajr and Zuhr → long; Asr and Isha → middle; Maghrib → short.
4
Confirm the status
This practice is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) for the resident. Note that a traveler may shorten the recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۱۹)[۱۶] سورہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ جو سورت ملائی جائے وہ فجر میں اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل ہو، اور عصر اور عشاء میں اوساطا مفصل ہو، اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل ہو ، اگر وہ مقیم ہو۔
تشریح : اگر مقیم ہو تو فجر میں اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل کی سورتیں پڑھنا سنت ہے، اور عصر اور عشاء میں اوساط مفصل کی سورتیں پڑھنا سنت ہے، اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل کی سورتیں پڑھنا سنت ہے۔
Translation: (419) [16] The surah joined with al-Fatiha should be from the long Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, from the middle in Asr and Isha, and from the short in Maghrib, if he is a resident. Explanation: If he is a resident, then in Fajr and Zuhr, reciting surahs from the long Mufassal is Sunnah; in Asr and Isha, from the middle Mufassal is Sunnah; and in Maghrib, from the short Mufassal is Sunnah.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a clear ruling on the sunnah of recitation after Surah al-Fatiha in prayer. It specifies that for a resident (muqim), the length of the additional surah should vary by prayer: long (tiwal) in Fajr and Zuhr, medium (awsat) in Asr and Isha, and short (qisar) in Maghrib. The Mufassal refers to the last seventh of the Qur'an from Surah Qaf or Hujurat to the end, divided into long (from Qaf to 'Amma), medium (from 'Amma to Duha), and short (from Duha to the end). The explanation (tashrih) confirms that this is a sunnah practice. The ruling applies only to the resident, implying that a traveler may shorten the recitation. No proofs are provided in this section, but the ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
طوال مفصل (tiwal al-mufassal): The long surahs from the Mufassal section of the Qur'an, typically from Surah Qaf or Hujurat to Surah 'Amma.
اوساط مفصل (awsat al-mufassal): The medium-length surahs from the Mufassal, from Surah 'Amma to Surah Duha.
قصار مفصل (qisar al-mufassal): The short surahs from the Mufassal, from Surah Duha to the end of the Qur'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fajr
B) Zuhr
C) Maghrib
D) Isha

Key Takeaway
For a resident, the sunnah is to recite long Mufassal surahs in Fajr and Zuhr, medium in Asr and Isha, and short in Maghrib.

Sunnah Recitation of Mufassal Surahs in Prayer
Ruling on reciting specific Mufassal surahs in each prayer for a resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which Mufassal surahs are Sunnah to recite in each daily prayer for a resident and apply the Hanafi classification of Mufassal.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice divided the Mufassal into long, medium, and short surahs, each assigned to specific prayers as a stressed Sunnah.

In this lesson, we learn the recommended (Sunnah) practice of selecting surahs from the Mufassal section of the Quran for each prayer. The Hanafi school specifies which type of surah to recite based on the prayer time, distinguishing between resident and traveler. We will see the proofs from hadith and the classification of Mufassal surahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its Sunnah level
State the overall ruling: it is Sunnah muakkadah to recite specific Mufassal surahs in each prayer for a resident. Note that it is not wajib.
The evidence is from ahad hadith, making the ruling zanni in proof but established practice.
2
Classify the Mufassal sections
Recognize the three categories: long (tawal) from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to al-Buruj (85), medium (awsat) from al-Buruj to al-Bayyinah (98), and short (qisar) from al-Bayyinah to the end.
This classification is based on the length of the surahs, as explained in the text.
3
Match categories to prayers
For the resident: Fajr and Zuhr require long Mufassal; Asr and Isha require medium Mufassal; Maghrib requires short Mufassal.
This matching is derived from the hadith of Abu Hurairah and the instruction of Umar.
4
Examine the proofs
Review the hadith: Abu Hurairah reports a companion who resembled the Prophet's prayer reciting specific lengths; Umar wrote to Abu Musa instructing the same; and other hadith specify verse counts.
The proofs are from ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut) but are consistently practiced.
5
Understand the scope and exceptions
This ruling applies to a resident (muqim). Travelers are not bound to these specific lengths; they may recite shorter surahs or fewer verses. Also, other schools may have different categorizations.
The Hanafi position is based on the cited proofs, but there is legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سنن الصلوة
(۴۱۹) وان تكون السورة المضمومة للفاتحة من طوال المفصل في الفجر والظهر ومن اوساطه في العصر والعشاء ومن قصاره في المغرب لو كان مقيما
ترجمه : (۴۱۹) [۱۶] سورہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ جو سورت ملائی جائے وہ فجر میں اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل ہو، اور عصر اور عشاء میں اوساطا مفصل ہو، اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل ہو ، اگر وہ مقیم ہو۔
تشریح : اگر مقیم ہو تو فجر میں اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل کی سورتیں پڑھنا سنت ہے، اور عصر اور عشاء میں اوساط مفصل کی سورتیں پڑھنا سنت ہے، اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل کی سورتیں پڑھنا سنت ہے۔
طوال مفصل ، اوساط مفصل ، اور قصار مفصل کیا ہیں دکھ
سوره حجرات ۴۹ سے ليكر سورہ بروج ۸۵ تک طوال مفصل ہے، کیونکہ یہ سورتیں لمبی لمبی ہیں، اور سورہ بروج ۸۵ سے ليكر سورہ البینة لم یکن الذین کفروا) ۹۸ تک اوساط مفصل میں اسلئے کہ یہ سورتیں اوسط درجے کی ہیں نہ زیادہ لمبی ہیں اور نہ زیادہ چھوٹی ہیں، اور لم یکن الذین کفروا ۹۸ سے ليكر آخیر قرآن سورہ الناس ۱۴ اتک قصار مفصل ہیں اسلئے کہ یہ سورتیں چھوٹی چھوٹی ہیں۔
وجه : (۱) عن ابي هريرة قال ما صليت وراء احد أشبه صلوة برسول الله من فلان ..... يقرأ في المغرب بقصار المفصل ، ويقرأ فى العشاء بوسط المفصل ، و يقرأ في الصبح بطوال المفصل (نسائی شریف ، باب تخفيف القيام والقرآة ، ص ۱۳۷، نمبر ۹۸۳ / مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب ما يقرأ فی الصلوۃ ، ج ثانی ، ص ۶۷ ، نمبر ۲۶۷۴) (۲) روی عـن عـمـر انـه كـتـب الـي ابــى موسى ان اقرأ في الصبح بطوال المفصل .... في الظهر باوساط المفصل ...... في المغرب بقصار المفصل ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء في القرآة في صلوة الصبح ۸۳ نمبر ۳۰۸/۳۰۷/۳۰۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فجر میں طوال مفصل ، ظہر میں اوساط مفصل، اور مغرب میں قصار مفصل پڑھے۔ (۳) ۔ عن ابي برزة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقرأ في صلوة الغداة من الستين الى المأة - (مسلم شریف، باب القرآة في الصبح ،۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۰۳۱/۴۶۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ " صبح کی نماز میں ساٹھ سے ليكر سو آیتیوں تک پڑھا کرتے تھے ۔ اس سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ چالیس سے ساٹھ تک بھی پڑھنا سنت ہے۔ (۴) ۔ عن جابر بن سمرة : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقرأ في الفجر ق و القرآن المجيد ) و كان صلوته بعد تخفيفا - (مسلم شریف ، باب القرأة فی الصبح ، ۱۸۵، نمبر ۴۵۸ ۱۰۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے صبح کی نماز میں سورہ ق پڑھتے تھے ، اور سورہ ق میں ۴۵ آیتیں ہیں جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورہ فاتحہ کے علاوہ چالیس سے ليكر پچاس آیتیں پڑھنی چاہئے، یہ سنت ہے۔ (۵) عن ابی سعيد الخدري : أن النبي له كان يقرأ في صلوة الظهر في الركعتين الأوليين في كل ركعة قدر ثلاثين آية ، و في الاخريين قدر خمس عشرة آية - (مسلم شریف ، باب القرائة في الظهر والعصر، ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۰۱۵/۴۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظہر کی پہلی رکعت میں بھی تھیں آیتیں پڑھی اور دوسری رکعت میں بھی تمھیں آیتیں پڑھی ، اور دونوں ملکر ساٹھ آیتیں ہوئیں ، اور یہی ساٹھ آیتیں فجر میں بھی ہیں ، اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر کا حکم بھی وہی ہے جو فجر کا ہے (۶) عن ابی سعید الخدری قال : كنا نحزر قيام رسول الله الله في الظهر والعصر ، فحزرنا قيامه في الركعتين الاوليين من الظهر قدر قرأة الم تنزيل السجدة (مسلم شریف، باب القرائة في الظهر والعصر، ۱۸۵، نمبر ۱۰۱۴/۴۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہم نے آپ کے قیام کا اندازہ لگایا کہ ظہر کی پہلی دورکعتوں میں سورہ سجدہ کے برابر تھا ، اور سورہ سجدہ میں تمہیں آیتیں ہیں جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر فجر کے قریب قریب ہے۔ (۷) اور
Section on the Sunnahs of Prayer. (419) And the surah joined to al-Fatihah should be from the long Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, and from its middle in Asr and Isha, and from its short in Maghrib, if he is a resident. Translation: The surah added to Surah Fatihah: in Fajr and Zuhr it should be from the long Mufassal, in Asr and Isha from the middle Mufassal, and in Maghrib from the short Mufassal, if he is a resident. Explanation: If he is a resident, then reciting long Mufassal surahs in Fajr and Zuhr is Sunnah, reciting middle Mufassal surahs in Asr and Isha is Sunnah, and reciting short Mufassal surahs in Maghrib is Sunnah. What are long Mufassal, middle Mufassal, and short Mufassal? Show: From Surah al-Hujurat (49) to Surah al-Buruj (85) is long Mufassal, because these surahs are long. And from Surah al-Buruj (85) to Surah al-Bayyinah (98) is middle Mufassal, because these surahs are of medium length, neither very long nor very short. And from 'Lam yakun' (98) to the end of the Quran, Surah an-Nas (114), is short Mufassal, because these surahs are short. Evidence: (1) From Abu Hurairah: 'I have not prayed behind anyone whose prayer resembled that of the Messenger of Allah more than so-and-so... he used to recite in Maghrib the short Mufassal, in Isha the middle Mufassal, and in Fajr the long Mufassal.' (2) Narrated from Umar that he wrote to Abu Musa: 'Recite in Fajr the long Mufassal... in Zuhr the middle Mufassal... in Maghrib the short Mufassal.' (3) From Abu Barzah: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the morning prayer from sixty to one hundred verses. (4) From Jabir ibn Samurah: The Prophet used to recite in Fajr 'Qaf' and his prayer after that was lighter. (5) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The Prophet used to recite in Zuhr in the first two rak'ahs about thirty verses per rak'ah, and in the last two about fifteen verses. (6) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: We estimated the standing of the Messenger of Allah in Zuhr and Asr, and we estimated his standing in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr to be the length of the recitation of Surah as-Sajdah. (7) And
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the Sunnah recitation of additional surahs after al-Fatihah in the five daily prayers for a resident. It specifies that the type of surah (from the Mufassal section of the Quran) varies: long (tawal) for Fajr and Zuhr, medium (awsat) for Asr and Isha, and short (qisar) for Maghrib. The passage then defines the three categories of Mufassal: from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to al-Buruj (85) is long; from al-Buruj (85) to al-Bayyinah (98) is medium; and from al-Bayyinah to the end (an-Nas 114) is short. This division is based on the length of the surahs. The ruling is supported by several hadith and athar: the practice of a companion reported by Abu Hurairah, the instruction of Umar to Abu Musa, and direct reports of the Prophet's recitation length in various prayers. The author uses these proofs to establish that the recommended practice is to match the surah length to the prayer, with Fajr and Zuhr having longer recitations and Maghrib the shortest. It is important to note that this ruling applies specifically to a resident (muqim); the traveler may shorten his prayer and recitation. The passage does not discuss the traveler's rule here.

Key Terms
طوال المفصل (tawāl al-mufaṣṣal): The long surahs of the Mufassal section, from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to Surah al-Buruj (85) according to this text.
أوساط المفصل (awāṣit al-mufaṣṣal): The medium-length surahs of the Mufassal, from Surah al-Buruj (85) to Surah al-Bayyinah (98).
قصار المفصل (qiṣār al-mufaṣṣal): The short surahs of the Mufassal, from Surah al-Bayyinah (98) to the end of the Quran (Surah an-Nas, 114).
مفصل (mufaṣṣal): The section of the Quran from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to the end, characterized by short surahs and frequent basmalahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which surahs should be recited in Maghrib prayer for a resident?
A) Long Mufassal (طوال المفصل)
B) Medium Mufassal (أوساط المفصل)
C) Short Mufassal (قصار المفصل)
D) Any surah from the Quran

Key Takeaway
For a resident, the Hanafi sunnah is to recite long Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, medium in Asr and Isha, and short in Maghrib.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Traveler's Recitation: Any Surah You Wish
Ruling with proof on traveler's recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a traveler may recite any surah in Salah and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Travel permits you to choose any surah — the Prophet himself recited short surahs on journeys.

When traveling, the hardship of the journey allows flexibility in recitation length. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a traveler may recite any surah in Salah, supported by clear hadith evidence from the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the text's opening statement: 'And if he is a traveler, he may recite any surah he wishes.' This is the Hanafi position.
The text uses 'yagra' ayyu suratin sha'a' — absolute permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: (1) Al-Bara' reports the Prophet recited 'Wat-Tini waz-Zaytun' in 'Isha during travel. (2) 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir reports the Prophet taught him al-Mu'awwidhatayn and recited them in Fajr during travel.
Both hadith show the Prophet chose shorter surahs in travel.
3
Understand the 'illah
The rationale is hardship (mashaqqah) of travel, which allows leniency. The text explicitly states: 'In travel there is hardship, so... he may recite whatever surah is suitable.'
This is a concession (rukhsah).
4
Note the thamarah
The practical effect is that a traveler is not bound to the usual recommended surah lengths for each prayer. He may choose short or long surahs as he wishes.
This applies to all obligatory prayers during travel.

Source Text

(مسلم شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر والعصر) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عصر میں ظهر سے آدھی پندرہ آیتیں پڑھتے تھے، تو یہ اوساط مفصل ہوا۔ (۸) مغرب میں قصار مفصل پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: أخبرنا هشام بن عروة أن أباه كان يقرأ في صلاة المغرب بنحو ما تقرؤون والعاديات ونحوها من السور. (ابوداود شریف، باب من رأى التخفيف فيها من المغرب) ترجمه: (۴۲۰) اور مسافر ہو تو جو سورت چاہے پڑھے۔ تشريح: سفر میں مشقت ہوتی ہے اس لئے فجر ظهر عصر مغرب عشاء میں جو سورت مناسب ہو پڑھے، ہر ایک کی گنجائش ہے۔ وجه: (۱) سمعت البراء أن النبي ﷺ كان في سفر، فقرأ في العشاء في إحدى الركعتين والتين والزيتون. (بخاری شریف، باب النھر في العشاء) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عشاء میں اوساط مفصل کے بجائے سفر کی وجہ سے چھوٹی سورت والتین والزيتون پڑھی۔ (۲) عن عقبة بن عامر قال: كنت أقود برسول الله ﷺ ناقته في السفر فقال لي: يا عقبة! ألا أعلمك خير سورتين قرئتا، فعلمني قل أعوذ برب الفلق وقل أعوذ برب الناس، قال: فلم يرني سررت بهما جدا، قال: فلما نزل لصلاة الصبح صلى بهما صلاة الصبح للناس، فلما فرغ رسول الله ﷺ من الصلاة التفت إلي فقال: يا عقبة كيف رأيت. (ابوداود شریف، باب في المعوذتین، نسائی شریف) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سفر میں فجر میں بھی چھوٹی سورت پڑھی جا سکتی ہے۔ ترجمه: (۴۲۱) صرف فجر کی پہلی رکعت دوسری رکعت سے لمبی کرے۔ تشريح: فجر کی پہلی رکعت میں دوسری رکعت کی نسبت لمبی قرآت کرے، اس کا فائدہ یہ ہوگا کہ بعد میں آنے والے لوگوں کو جماعت مل جائے گی، اور ائمہ کی رائے ہے کہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی پہلی رکعت تھوڑی سی لمبی کرے۔ وجه: (۱) عن عبد الله بن أبي قتادة عن أبيه قال: كان رسول الله ﷺ يقرأ في الركعتين الأوليين من صلاة الظهر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورتين، يطول في الأولى ويقصر في الثانية ويسمع الآية أحيانا، وكان يقرأ في العصر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورتين، وكان يطول في الأولى، وكان يطول في الركعة الأولى من صلاة الصبح ويقصر في الثانية. (بخاری شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر، مسلم شریف)
(420) And he may recite any surah he wishes if he is a traveler. (421) And lengthening the first [rak'ah] is only in Fajr. Its evidence is this hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet used to recite in Zuhr prayer in the first two rak'ahs each rak'ah about thirty verses, and in the last two about half that, and in Asr in the first two rak'ahs each about fifteen verses, and in the last two about half that. (Muslim) In this hadith, Asr is half of Zuhr, about fifteen verses, so that is the middle of Mufassal. (8) In Maghrib, he recited the short Mufassal. Its evidence: Hisham ibn 'Urwah narrated that his father used to recite in Maghrib prayer similar to what you recite: 'Wal-'adiyat' and similar surahs. (Abu Dawud) Translation: (420) And if he is a traveler, he may recite any surah he wishes. Explanation: In travel there is hardship, so in Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha he may recite whatever surah is suitable. All are permissible. Proof: (1) I heard al-Bara' that the Prophet was on a journey and in 'Isha in one of the rak'ahs recited 'Wat-Tini waz-Zaytun'. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that in 'Isha, instead of the middle Mufassal, due to travel he recited a short surah, 'Wat-Tini waz-Zaytun'. (2) From 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir: I was leading the Prophet's she-camel in travel, and he said, 'O 'Uqbah, shall I teach you the best two surahs to recite?' Then he taught me 'Qul a'udhu birabbil-falaq' and 'Qul a'udhu birabbin-nas'. He said, 'I did not see him as happy with them as I was.' Then when he descended for Fajr prayer, he prayed Fajr with them for the people. When he finished, he turned to me and said, 'O 'Uqbah, how did you see?' (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i) This hadith shows that in travel, even in Fajr a short surah can be recited. Translation: (421) Only lengthen the first rak'ah of Fajr over the second. Explanation: In Fajr, make the recitation in the first rak'ah longer than the second. The benefit is that people coming later will catch the congregation. The imams hold that in other prayers also the first rak'ah should be slightly lengthened. Proof: (1) From 'Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah from his father: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening the first and shortening the second, sometimes making an audible verse. In Asr he recited Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening the first, and he lengthened the first rak'ah of Fajr and shortened the second. (Bukhari, Muslim)
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof from hadith. It covers two rulings: (420) a traveler may recite any surah he wishes, and (421) in Fajr prayer, the first rak'ah should be lengthened relative to the second. The evidence for (420) includes hadith showing the Prophet recited shorter surahs in travel for 'Isha and Fajr, indicating flexibility. The evidence for (421) is from the practice of the Prophet in Zuhr, Asr, and Fajr, where he lengthened the first rak'ah. The explanation notes that for other prayers, some imams also recommend slightly lengthening the first rak'ah to allow latecomers to join. Both rulings are from the Sunan of prayer, not obligatory. A common misunderstanding is that one must always recite long surahs; this passage clarifies that travel permits shorter recitations, and only in Fajr is there a specific recommendation to lengthen the first rak'ah.

Key Terms
مفصل (Mufassal): The long surahs from Qaf to the end of the Qur'an, divided into three sections: Tiwal (long), Awsat (medium), Qisar (short).
مسافر (Musafir): A traveler who meets the conditions for travel concessions in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must recite the same surahs recommended for a resident.
B) He may recite any surah he wishes.
C) He must recite shorter surahs only.
D) He must recite longer surahs to gain reward.

Key Takeaway
A traveler may recite any surah in prayer, as the Prophet did, to alleviate hardship.

Lengthening the First Rak'ah in Fajr
Ruling with proof on lengthening first rak'ah in Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that only in Fajr is the first rak'ah lengthened and explain the wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
Only in Fajr do you lengthen the first rak'ah — to allow latecomers to join the congregation.

Among the sunan of Fajr prayer, the Hanafi school recommends making the first rak'ah longer in recitation than the second. This practice is based on the Prophet's consistent action and has a practical benefit: it gives people more time to join the congregation during the second rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text says: 'Only lengthen the first rak'ah of Fajr over the second.' This is specific to Fajr.
The word 'فقط' (only) emphasizes exclusivity.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abu Qatadah: the Prophet used to lengthen the first rak'ah in Zuhr, Asr, and Fajr, and shorten the second.
The evidence comes from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the hikmah
The explanation in the text: 'The benefit is that people coming later will catch the congregation.' This is a practical wisdom.
The imams also opine that in other prayers, the first rak'ah should be slightly lengthened, but the sunnah is specifically emphasized in Fajr.
4
Differentiate from other prayers
The text explicitly states 'only in Fajr' (فقط). For other prayers, some imams recommend slight lengthening, but it is not a confirmed sunnah.
This distinction prevents mixing the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۲۰) ويقرأ اى سورة شاء لو كان مسافرا (۴۲۱) واطالة الاولى في الفجر فقط. اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن ابی سعید الخدري: أن النبي ﷺ كان يقرأ في صلاة الظهر في الركعتين الأوليين في كل ركعة قدر ثلاثين آية، وفي الأخريين قدر خمس عشرة آية أو قال نصف ذلك، وفي العصر في الركعتين الأوليين في كل ركعة قدر قراءة خمس عشرة آية، وفي الأخريين قدر نصف ذلك. (مسلم شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر والعصر) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عصر میں ظهر سے آدھی پندرہ آیتیں پڑھتے تھے، تو یہ اوساط مفصل ہوا۔ (۸) مغرب میں قصار مفصل پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: أخبرنا هشام بن عروة أن أباه كان يقرأ في صلاة المغرب بنحو ما تقرؤون والعاديات ونحوها من السور. (ابوداود شریف، باب من رأى التخفيف فيها من المغرب) ترجمه: (۴۲۰) اور مسافر ہو تو جو سورت چاہے پڑھے۔ تشريح: سفر میں مشقت ہوتی ہے اس لئے فجر ظهر عصر مغرب عشاء میں جو سورت مناسب ہو پڑھے، ہر ایک کی گنجائش ہے۔ وجه: (۱) سمعت البراء أن النبي ﷺ كان في سفر، فقرأ في العشاء في إحدى الركعتين والتين والزيتون. (بخاری شریف، باب النھر في العشاء) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عشاء میں اوساط مفصل کے بجائے سفر کی وجہ سے چھوٹی سورت والتین والزيتون پڑھی۔ (۲) عن عقبة بن عامر قال: كنت أقود برسول الله ﷺ ناقته في السفر فقال لي: يا عقبة! ألا أعلمك خير سورتين قرئتا، فعلمني قل أعوذ برب الفلق وقل أعوذ برب الناس، قال: فلم يرني سررت بهما جدا، قال: فلما نزل لصلاة الصبح صلى بهما صلاة الصبح للناس، فلما فرغ رسول الله ﷺ من الصلاة التفت إلي فقال: يا عقبة كيف رأيت. (ابوداود شریف، باب في المعوذتین، نسائی شریف) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سفر میں فجر میں بھی چھوٹی سورت پڑھی جا سکتی ہے۔ ترجمه: (۴۲۱) صرف فجر کی پہلی رکعت دوسری رکعت سے لمبی کرے۔ تشريح: فجر کی پہلی رکعت میں دوسری رکعت کی نسبت لمبی قرآت کرے، اس کا فائدہ یہ ہوگا کہ بعد میں آنے والے لوگوں کو جماعت مل جائے گی، اور ائمہ کی رائے ہے کہ دوسری نمازوں میں بھی پہلی رکعت تھوڑی سی لمبی کرے۔ وجه: (۱) عن عبد الله بن أبي قتادة عن أبيه قال: كان رسول الله ﷺ يقرأ في الركعتين الأوليين من صلاة الظهر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورتين، يطول في الأولى ويقصر في الثانية ويسمع الآية أحيانا، وكان يقرأ في العصر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورتين، وكان يطول في الأولى، وكان يطول في الركعة الأولى من صلاة الصبح ويقصر في الثانية. (بخاری شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر، مسلم شریف)
(420) And he may recite any surah he wishes if he is a traveler. (421) And lengthening the first [rak'ah] is only in Fajr. Its evidence is this hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet used to recite in Zuhr prayer in the first two rak'ahs each rak'ah about thirty verses, and in the last two about half that, and in Asr in the first two rak'ahs each about fifteen verses, and in the last two about half that. (Muslim) In this hadith, Asr is half of Zuhr, about fifteen verses, so that is the middle of Mufassal. (8) In Maghrib, he recited the short Mufassal. Its evidence: Hisham ibn 'Urwah narrated that his father used to recite in Maghrib prayer similar to what you recite: 'Wal-'adiyat' and similar surahs. (Abu Dawud) Translation: (420) And if he is a traveler, he may recite any surah he wishes. Explanation: In travel there is hardship, so in Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha he may recite whatever surah is suitable. All are permissible. Proof: (1) I heard al-Bara' that the Prophet was on a journey and in 'Isha in one of the rak'ahs recited 'Wat-Tini waz-Zaytun'. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that in 'Isha, instead of the middle Mufassal, due to travel he recited a short surah, 'Wat-Tini waz-Zaytun'. (2) From 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir: I was leading the Prophet's she-camel in travel, and he said, 'O 'Uqbah, shall I teach you the best two surahs to recite?' Then he taught me 'Qul a'udhu birabbil-falaq' and 'Qul a'udhu birabbin-nas'. He said, 'I did not see him as happy with them as I was.' Then when he descended for Fajr prayer, he prayed Fajr with them for the people. When he finished, he turned to me and said, 'O 'Uqbah, how did you see?' (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i) This hadith shows that in travel, even in Fajr a short surah can be recited. Translation: (421) Only lengthen the first rak'ah of Fajr over the second. Explanation: In Fajr, make the recitation in the first rak'ah longer than the second. The benefit is that people coming later will catch the congregation. The imams hold that in other prayers also the first rak'ah should be slightly lengthened. Proof: (1) From 'Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah from his father: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening the first and shortening the second, sometimes making an audible verse. In Asr he recited Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening the first, and he lengthened the first rak'ah of Fajr and shortened the second. (Bukhari, Muslim)
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof from hadith. It covers two rulings: (420) a traveler may recite any surah he wishes, and (421) in Fajr prayer, the first rak'ah should be lengthened relative to the second. The evidence for (420) includes hadith showing the Prophet recited shorter surahs in travel for 'Isha and Fajr, indicating flexibility. The evidence for (421) is from the practice of the Prophet in Zuhr, Asr, and Fajr, where he lengthened the first rak'ah. The explanation notes that for other prayers, some imams also recommend slightly lengthening the first rak'ah to allow latecomers to join. Both rulings are from the Sunan of prayer, not obligatory. A common misunderstanding is that one must always recite long surahs; this passage clarifies that travel permits shorter recitations, and only in Fajr is there a specific recommendation to lengthen the first rak'ah.

Key Terms
اطالة الاولى (Italat al-Ula): Lengthening the first rak'ah of Fajr in recitation relative to the second.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which prayer is it specifically recommended to lengthen the first rak'ah?
A) Zuhr
B) Asr
C) Fajr
D) Maghrib

Key Takeaway
Lengthening the first rak'ah in Fajr is a confirmed sunnah to allow latecomers to join the congregation.

The Four Sunan of Ruku': Takbir, Tasbih, Hand Placement, and Finger Spacing
Explanation of four sunan acts in ruku' with hadith evidence and gender rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan of ruku' and identify which sunnah has a gender-specific application.

Core Idea
The sunan of ruku' perfect the prayer; missing them does not invalidate but reduces reward.

In this lesson, we explore four of the nine sunan acts of ruku' as expounded in the Hanafi tradition. These sunan—takbir, tasbih, hand placement, and finger spacing—are rooted in authentic hadith and enhance the quality of one's prayer. Understanding their status as sunnah muakkadah helps balance between fulfilling obligations and seeking perfection.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah act
List the four sunan mentioned: takbir at the start of ruku', reciting 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' three times, placing hands on the knees as if grasping, and spreading the fingers (men) or keeping them together (women).
The source mentions nine sunan total but elaborates these four.
2
Determine the hukm level
Classify each act as sunnah muakkadah per the Hanafi school. Recognise that performing them is rewarded, omitting them does not break the prayer.
The toolkit provides the hanafi position: sunnah muakkadah.
3
Note the gender distinction
Identify that finger spacing applies to men only; women keep fingers together due to modesty (satr). This is a unique Hanafi ruling.
Other sunan apply equally to men and women.
4
Associate each sunnah with its hadith evidence
For takbir: hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said takbir when bowing. For tasbih: hadith of Ibn Mas'ud commanding three times. For hand placement: hadith of Abu Humayd describing grasping knees. For finger spacing: hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amr showing spread fingers.
The source includes partial hadith texts; full chains are available in the referenced books.
5
Clarify the minimum vs sunnah for tasbih
One recitation of the tasbih fulfills the obligation (all that is required), but three times is the sunnah. This addresses a common misunderstanding.
The source explicitly states: 'if he says it once, the tasbih is paid, but the sunnah is not performed.'

فصل سنن الصلوة الركوع وتسبيحه ثلاثا (۴۲۳) واخذ ركبتيه بيديه وتفريج اصابعه والمرأة لا تفرّجها. يطول في الركعة الأولى من صلوة الصبح، ويقصر في الثانية - (بخاری شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر، ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۷۵۹، مسلم شریف، باب القراءة في الظهر، ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۱۰۱۲/۴۵) اس حديث میں ہے کہ پہلی رکعت لمبی کرے۔ ترجمه: (۴۲۲) [۱۸] رکوع کی تکبیر۔ [۱۹] اس میں تین بار تسبیح کہنا۔ تشریح: رکوع میں نو سنتیں ہیں، یہاں اس کا بیان ہے۔ [۱] پہلی سنت: رکوع میں جاتے وقت تکبیر کہنا سنت ہے۔ [۲] دوسری: رکوع کے اندر تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم کہنا سنت ہے۔ ایک مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم کہے گا تو تسبیح ادا ہو جائے گی لیکن سنت کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه: (۱) حديث میں ہے کہ آپ رکوع اور سجدے میں تکبیر کہتے۔ سمع أبا هريرة يقول كان رسول الله ﷺ إذا قام إلى الصلاة يكبر حين يقوم ثم يكبر حين يركع. (بخاری شریف، باب التكبير إذا قام من السجود، ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۷۸۹، مسلم شریف، باب اثبات التكبير في كل خفض ورفع في الصلاة، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۸۶۸/۳۹۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع میں جاتے ہوئے تکبیر کہے۔ (۲) اور تین مرتبہ تسبیح کہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن ابن مسعود قال: قال رسول الله ﷺ: إذا ركع أحدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات: سبحان ربي العظيم وذلك أدناه، فإذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاثا وذلك أدناه. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب مقدار الركوع والسجود، ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۸۶، ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في التسبيح في الركوع والسجود، ص ۶۰ نمبر ۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم کہے اور یہ کم از کم ہے۔ ترجمه: (۴۲۳) [۲۰] دونوں ہاتھوں سے اپنے دونوں گھٹنوں کو پکڑنا۔ [۲۱] اور انگلیوں کو کشادہ رکھنا، اور عورت اپنی انگلیاں کشادہ نہ رکھے۔ تشریح: [۳] تیسری سنت: رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کو گھٹنوں پر اس طرح رکھے کہ گویا ان کو پکڑ رہا ہو۔ [۴] چوتھی سنت: ہاتھ گھٹنے پر رکھتے وقت انگلیاں کشادہ رہیں۔ البتہ عورت کے لئے ستر میں ہے کہ انگلیاں ملا کر رکھے، اس لئے وہ تھوڑا ملا کر رکھیں تو بہتر ہے۔ وجه: (۱) حديث یہ ہے: فذكروا صلاة رسول الله ﷺ فقال أبو حميد أنا أعلمكم بصلاة رسول الله ﷺ إن رسول الله ﷺ ركع فوضع يديه على ركبتيه كأنه قابض عليهما ووتر يديه فنحاهما عن جنبيه. (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في تجافي يديه عن جنبيه في الركوع، ص ۷۲، نمبر ۲۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ سے گھٹنوں کو اس طرح پکڑے کہ کمان کی رسی کی طرح معلوم ہو۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے: قال: أتينا عقبة بن عمرو الأنصاري أبا مسعود صلاة رسول الله ﷺ علم، فقام بين أيدينا في المسجد فكبر، فلما ركع وضع يديه على ركبتيه. فقلنا له: حدثنا عن صلاة رسول الله ﷺ
Section on the Sunan of Prayer: The ruku' and its tasbih three times. (423) And he should take his knees with his hands and spread his fingers, but the woman does not spread them. He lengthens the first rak'ah of Fajr and shortens the second. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, he lengthened the first rak'ah. Translation: (422) [18] The takbir for ruku'. [19] Saying tasbih three times in it. Explanation: There are nine sunan in ruku', here is their description. [1] First sunnah: Saying takbir when going into ruku' is sunnah. [2] Second sunnah: Saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' three times inside ruku' is sunnah. If one says it once, the obligation of tasbih is fulfilled but the sunnah is not performed. Proof: (1) A hadith states that the Prophet used to say takbir in ruku' and sujud. Abu Huraira said: When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he would say takbir when standing, then say takbir when bowing. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith indicates one should say takbir while going into ruku'. (2) And saying tasbih three times is evidenced by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: The Prophet said: 'When one of you bows, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim, and that is the minimum; and when he prostrates, let him say Subhana Rabbiyal-A'la three times, and that is the minimum.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith states to say 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' three times, and it is the minimum. Translation: (423) [20] Grabbing one's two knees with both hands. [21] And keeping the fingers spread, and the woman does not spread her fingers. Explanation: [3] Third sunnah: In ruku', place both hands on the knees as if grasping them. [4] Fourth sunnah: When placing the hands on the knees, the fingers should be spread. However, for the woman it is covering (satr) to keep the fingers together, so it is better if she keeps them slightly together. Proof: (1) The hadith: They mentioned the prayer of the Prophet, and Abu Humayd said: 'I know best the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. When he bowed, he placed his hands on his knees as if grasping them, and he spread his fingers away from his sides.' (Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that he grasped the knees with his hands such that it appeared like a bowstring. (2) A hadith: We came to 'Uqbah ibn 'Amr al-Ansari Abu Mas'ud to learn the prayer of the Prophet. He stood before us in the mosque, said takbir, and when he bowed, he placed his hands on his knees. So we said: 'Tell us about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah.'
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing four of the nine sunan acts of ruku'. It forms part of a larger section on the sunan of prayer. First, it covers the takbir when moving into ruku' (sunnah). Second, it covers the tasbih 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' recited three times; once suffices for validity but three times is sunnah. The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud establishes the minimum. Third, it covers placing hands on knees as if grasping them. Fourth, it covers finger spacing: men spread their fingers, while women keep them together due to modesty (satr). These rulings are based on authentic hadith. A common misunderstanding is that the tasbih must be said three times for correctness; in the Hanafi school, saying it once fulfills the obligatory recitation, but the sunnah is three times.

Key Terms
سبحان ربي العظيم (Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim): The tasbih recited in ruku': 'Glory be to my Lord, the Magnificent'.
تفريج الأصابع (Tafrij al-Asabi'): Spreading the fingers apart when placing hands on knees in ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is fard to say 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' three times.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of ruku' enhance the prayer's perfection without being obligatory; knowing their exact rulings avoids unnecessary strictness or negligence.

The Nine Sunnahs of Ruku' in Prayer
Lists the nine sunnahs of ruku' with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nine sunnahs of ruku' and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Ruku' has nine sunnahs: from takbir and tasbih to hand placement, back straightness, and rising with tranquility.

Ruku' (bowing) is a pillar (rukn) of prayer, but within it there are recommended acts (sunan) that the Prophet consistently performed. This lesson enumerates those nine sunnahs, each supported by authentic hadith. Understanding these helps you perfect your prayer while knowing that omitting them does not invalidate it.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the status of sunnah in Hanafi fiqh
In the Hanafi school, sunnah is a recommended action below wajib; omitting it is makruh tanzihi but does not require compensation or invalidate the prayer.
2
List the nine sunnahs from the text
Extract each sunnah: takbir when going into ruku', tasbih three times, grasping knees with hands, spreading fingers (men), keeping shins straight, back flat, head level with hips, rising from ruku', and standing with tranquility.
The text numbers them as sunan 1-9.
3
Identify the hadith proof for each sunnah
For each sunnah, locate the hadith cited by the author. For example, the takbir is proven by Bukhari and Muslim, the three tasbihs by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi, etc.
Some hadith cover multiple sunnahs, e.g., the hadith of Abu Hamid covers hand placement, back straightness, and rising.
4
Understand the minimum vs. sunnah
For tasbih, the text clarifies that one recitation fulfills the requirement but the sunnah is three times. This applies to all sunan: the minimum is valid, but the complete sunnah is preferred.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a person who rushes from ruku' without standing upright. Their prayer is valid, but they missed a sunnah. Advise them to observe tranquility next time.

Source Text

فصل سنن الصلوة الركوع وتسبيحه ثلاثا ( ۴۲۳ واخذ ركبتيه بيديه وتفريج اصابعه والمرأة لا تفرّجها يطول في الركعة الأولى من صلوة الصبح ، و يقصر في الثانية - ( بخارى شريف، باب القرآة في الظهر ، ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۷۵۹ مسلم شریف، باب القرآة فی الظهر ، ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۱۰۱۲/۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلی رکعت لمبی کرے۔ ترجمه : (۴۲۲) [۱۸] رکوع کی تکبیر ۔ [19] اس میں تین بار تسبیح کہنا۔ تشریح : رکوع میں نو سنتیں ہیں، یہاں اس کا بیان ہے۔ [1، پہلی سنت ] رکوع میں جاتے وقت تکبیر کہنا سنت ہے - [۲، دوسری اور رکوع کے اندر تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم ، کہنا سنت ہے۔ ایک مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم کہے گا تو تسبیح ادا ہو جائے گی لیکن سنت کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی ۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ رکوع اور سجدے میں تکبیر کہتے ۔ سمع ابا هريرة يقول كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذاقام الى الصلوة يكبر حين يقوم ثم يكبر حين يركع . (بخاری شریف، باب التگیر اذا قام من السجود در ص ۱۲۸ نمبر ۷۸۹ مسلم شریف ، باب اثبات التكبير في كل خفض ورفع فی الصلاۃ ، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۸۶۸/۳۹۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع میں جاتے ہوئے تکبیر کہے۔ (۲) اور تین مرتبہ تسبیح کہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : قال رسول الله الله اذا ركع احدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات : سبحان ربی العظيم وذلك ادناه فاذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربی الاعلى ثلاثا ، و ذالک ادناه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب مقدار الرکوع والسجود ،ص۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۸۶ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی التسبیح في الركوع والسجو در ص ۶۰ نمبر (۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی العظیم، کہے اور بیداد نی مرتبہ ہے۔ ترجمه : (۴۲۳) [۲۰] دونوں ہاتھوں سے اپنے دونوں گھٹنوں کو پکڑنا۔ [۲۱] اور انگلیوں کو کشادہ رکھنا، اور عورت اپنی انگلیاں کشادہ نہ رکھے۔ تشریح : [۳، تیسری سنت] رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کو گھٹنوں پر اس طرح رکھے کہ گویا کہ ان کو پکڑ رہا ہو۔ [۴ ، چوتھی سنت ] ہاتھ گھٹنے پر رکھتے وقت انگلیاں کشادہ رہیں ۔ البتہ عورت کے لئے ستر اس میں ہے کہ انگلیاں ملا کر رکھے اس لئے وہ تھوڑ املا کر رکھیں تو بہتر ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ فذكروا صلوة رسول الله عله فقال ابو حميد انا اعلمكم بصلوة رسول الله لله ان رسول الله الا الله و ركع فوضع يديه على ركبتيه كانه قابض عليهما و وتر يديه فنحاهما عن جنبيه. ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء بیجافی یدیہ عن جنبیہ فی الرکوع، ص ۷۲، نمبر ۲۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ سے گھٹنوں کو اس طرح پکڑے کہ کمان کی رسی کی طرح معلوم ہو (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ قال : أتينا عقبة بن عمرو الانصاري أبا مسعود صلوة رسول الله علم ، فقام بين أيدينا في المسجد فكبر ، فلما ركع وضع يديه على فقلنا له : حدثنا عن صلى الله (page 291) ثمرة النجاح جلد ا ۲۸۹ فصل سنن الصلوة (۴۲۴) و نصب ساقيه وبسط ظهره وتسوية رأسه بعجزه (۴۲۵) والرفع من الركوع والقيام بعد ركبتين و جعل أصابعه أسفل من ذالک و جافی بین مرفقيه حتى استقر كل شيء منه ء منہ ۔(ابوداؤد شریف، بان صلوۃ من لا یقیم صلبه فی الرکوع والسجود، ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۸۶۳ / نسائی شریف، باب مواضع اصابع الیدین فی الرکوع ،ص ۱۴۳، نمبر ۱۰۳۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رکوع میں دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں گھٹنوں پر پھیلا کر رکھے۔ (۳) عن ابن عمر : أن رسول الله الله قال لرجل : اذا قمت الى الصلوة فركعت فضع یدیک علی رکبتیک ، و افرج بين أصابعك ثم ارفع راسک حتی پر جع كل عضو الى مفصله - Chapter: The Sunnahs of Prayer. Bowing and its glorification three times (423). And grasping his knees with his hands and spreading his fingers. The woman does not spread them. He lengthens the first rak'ah of the Fajr prayer and shortens the second. (Bukhari, Chapter on Recitation in Zuhr, p. 105, no. 759; Muslim, Chapter on Recitation in Zuhr, p. 185, no. 1012/45) In this hadith, it states that the first rak'ah is made longer. Translation: (422) [18] The takbir of ruku'. [19] Saying tasbih three times in it. Explanation: There are nine sunnahs in ruku', and here is their description. [1, First sunnah] Saying takbir when going into ruku' is sunnah. [2, Second sunnah] Saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim' three times within ruku' is sunnah. If one says 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim' once, the tasbih is fulfilled, but the sunnah is not performed. Evidence: (1) In a hadith, it is stated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would say takbir in ruku' and sujud. (2) The evidence for saying three tasbihs is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'When one of you bows, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim, and that is the minimum. When he prostrates, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la, and that is the minimum.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) Translation: (423) [20] Grasping both knees with both hands. [21] Keeping the fingers spread, but the woman does not spread her fingers. Explanation: [3, Third sunnah] In ruku', place both hands on the knees as if grasping them. [4, Fourth sunnah] When placing the hands on the knees, the fingers should be spread. However, for the woman, it is better to keep them slightly together due to modesty. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abu Hamid: the Prophet (peace be upon him) bowed and placed his hands on his knees as if grasping them. (2) Another hadith: the hands are placed on the knees, fingers below that, and arms kept away from the sides. (3) Hadith of Ibn 'Umar: place hands on knees and spread the fingers. (Page 291) Chapter: The Sunnahs of Prayer. (424) Keeping the shins straight, extending the back, and making the head level with the hips. (425) Rising from ruku' and standing after bowing. Explanation: [5, Fifth sunnah] When bowing, do not push the shins forward or backward; keep them straight. [6, Sixth sunnah] The back should be flat, so that the back and head are in one line. [7, Seventh sunnah] The head should be level with the hips, neither too low nor too high. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abu Hamid: the Prophet (peace be upon him) bowed, then straightened, not lowering or raising his head. (2) Hadith of Wabisah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to make his back so straight that if water were poured on it, it would stay. Translation: (425) [25] Rising from ruku'. [26] Standing with tranquility after it. Explanation: [8, Eighth sunnah] Rising from ruku' is sunnah. [9, Ninth sunnah] After rising, stand fully with tranquility before prostrating; rushing is not sunnah. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abu Hamid: the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood straight, said 'Samia Allahu liman hamidah' and raised his hands...
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the sunan (recommended acts) of ruku' in prayer. The author enumerates nine sunan derived from the Prophet's practice, each supported by hadith evidence. The first sunna is saying Allahu Akbar while going into ruku' (takbirat al-ihram for the movement). The second is reciting 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim' three times; one time fulfills the minimum but the sunna is three. The third and fourth concern hand placement: men place their hands on their knees with fingers spread, while women keep their fingers together for modesty. The fifth is keeping the shins straight, not bent. The sixth is having the back flat. The seventh is keeping the head level with the hips. The eighth is rising from ruku' intentionally. The ninth is standing fully upright with tranquility before prostrating. The commentary stresses that these are sunna, not wajib, so omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but is contrary to the ideal practice.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): A recommended action in prayer; not obligatory but consistently performed by the Prophet.
ركوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer, a pillar (rukn) of prayer.
تسبيح (tasbih): Uttering 'subhana rabbiyal 'azim' in ruku'.
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' when going into ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum number of times one may say 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Azim' in ruku'?
A) One
B) Three
C) Seven
D) Eleven

Key Takeaway
The nine sunan of ruku' are established from the Prophet's practice; following them completes the prayer's sunnah aspect.

Salah — Prayer

Sunnah Acts of Ruku': The Three Positions
Explanation of three sunnah acts in ruku' with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts of ruku' according to the Hanafi school and explain the hadith evidence that establishes them as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Three sunnah acts in ruku'—erect shins, flat back, level head—are established by prophetic practice but not obligatory.

This passage presents three specific sunnah acts for the position of ruku' in prayer. You will learn their description, the hadith proofs cited by Hanafi scholars, and why they are classified as sunnah muakkadah rather than wajib. Understanding these details helps you perfect your prayer in accordance with the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunnah acts
From the passage, list the three acts the author describes as sunnah. Note the Arabic phrases: نصب ساقيه, بسط ظهره, تسوية رأسه بعجزه.
These acts relate to the position of the shins, back, and head during ruku'.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The text cites several hadith. Identify which hadith support each of the three acts. For example, the hadith of Abu Humayd and Wabisah specifically address the back and head.
The hadith are from Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and others.
3
Determine the hukm level and its basis
The author classifies these as 'sunnah'. In Hanafi usul, why are they not wajib? Examine the nature of the hadith—descriptive (fi'l) rather than imperative (amr).
Sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently did it; omission is disliked but prayer remains valid.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
How exactly does each hadith prove that the act is sunnah? For example, the hadith of Wabisah describes the Prophet making his back straight—a descriptive report indicates recommendation, not obligation.
Hanafi principle: fi'l (action) of the Prophet indicates sunnah unless there is evidence of compulsion.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The hanafi_position_box indicates this issue is mukhtalaf fih. Other schools may consider some of these acts wajib. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in prayer validity and compensation.
For Hanafis, omission means prayer is valid but makruh; for others, it may require sajdah al-sahw.

لغت : عجز سرین۔ لامینکہ : نہ زیادہ جھکائے۔ صوب: سر کو جھکانا۔ یقعہ : قنع سے سر اٹھانا۔
(424) And erecting his shins, and spreading his back, and leveling his head with his hips. (Hadith from Abu Dawud... from this hadith it is known that in ruku' both hands are placed spread on both knees. (3) From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to a man: When you stand for prayer and bow, place your hands on your knees and spread your fingers, then raise your head until every limb returns to its joint. (Mushannaf Abdur Razzaq). From this hadith: in ruku' place hands on knees and spread fingers.
Lughat: Rukbah = knee. Tafrij = derived from faj, meaning to spread.
Translation: (424) [22] Keeping both shins erect. [23] Keeping the back spread. [24] Keeping the head level with the hips.
Explanation: [5th sunnah] When bowing, sometimes one pushes shins back or forward, the author says do not do that, keep them straight—this is sunnah. [6th sunnah] The back is spread, meaning back and head are in a straight line. [7th sunnah] Head level with hips, neither too low nor too high.
Evidence: (1) From Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: I heard him among ten companions of the Prophet... and he bowed, then straightened, and did not lower his head nor raise it, and placed his hands on his knees. (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i). This hadith: head not raised high nor lowered, but kept level. (2) Wabisah ibn Ma'bad: I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ praying, and when he bowed he made his back straight, so that if water were poured on it, it would stay. (Ibn Majah). This hadith: in ruku' the back is flat and level.
Lughat: 'Ajz = hips. La yumayyikuhu: do not lower excessively. Sawb: lowering the head. Yaqna': from qana'a, raising the head.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section explaining three sunnah acts of ruku' (bowing) in prayer. The author, from the Hanafi school, enumerates these sunan: keeping the shins erect (not tilted forward or backward), keeping the back flat (so that the spine is straight), and keeping the head level with the hips (neither raised high nor lowered). The evidence is drawn from multiple hadith reports. The first hadith (from Abu Dawud and Nasa'i) emphasizes straightening the back during ruku' and sujud. The second hadith (from Ibn Umar) instructs placing hands on knees with fingers spread. The explanation expands that these acts are sunnah, not obligatory—omission does not invalidate the prayer but it becomes deficient. The section then provides further hadith from Abu Humayd and Wabisah confirming the head and back positions. The lughat explains key terms: rukbah (knee), tafrij (spreading), 'ajz (hips), etc. The overall ruling is that these three acts are sunnah muakkadah in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ساق (saaq): The shin, the part of the leg below the knee.
بسط ظهر (bast zahr): Spreading the back flat, meaning keeping the spine straight without curving.
تسوية الرأس بالعجز (taswiyat al-ra's bil-'ajz): Leveling the head with the hips, so that the head is neither raised high nor lowered excessively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Fard, required for prayer.
D) Mubah, completely optional with no reward or blame.

Key Takeaway
Three sunnah acts in ruku'—erect shins, flat back, level head—are strongly recommended but not obligatory in Hanafi fiqh.

Sunnahs of Rising from Ruku' and Standing Calmly
Two sunnah acts after ruku' with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for rising from ruku' and standing calmly, identify the hadith proofs, and distinguish this from the wajib positions of other schools.

Core Idea
Rising and standing calmly after ruku' are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, even when commanded by the Prophet.

In this lesson, we examine two sunnah acts after ruku': rising from the bowing position (raf' min al-ruku') and standing calmly (al-qiyam ba'd rukbatayh) before prostrating. Though some schools consider these wajib (pillars), the Hanafi school classifies them as sunnah muakkadah. Through the hadith evidence, you will see how Hanafi usul distinguishes between a command for obligation and a command for recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their Hanafi ruling
The text states that raising from ruku' (sunnah 8) and standing calmly (sunnah 9) are both sunnah. Note that sunnah muakkadah is a recommended act whose omission does not invalidate the prayer.
These are distinct from the fard acts of prayer.
2
Examine the first hadith (Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi)
This hadith describes the Prophet's practice: he stood calmly after ruku' until every bone returned to its place. The Hanafi school takes this as evidence of recommendation (istihbab) because it is a description of the Prophet's fi'l (action), which in usul indicates sunnah unless proven otherwise.
The phrase 'mutma'innan' (calmly) is emphasized.
3
Analyze the second hadith (the man who prayed badly)
The Prophet commanded the man to 'raise until you stand straight' after ruku'. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) from the Prophet can be for wujub or nadb. Here, because the man's prayer was still considered a prayer (though deficient), the command is interpreted as sunnah, not wajib.
The cross-madhhab difference arises here: Shafi'i interprets this command as wajib (pillar).
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Hanafi scholars distinguish between amr for wujub and amr for nadb based on contextual clues (qara'in). The context of the hadith (the man's prayer being invalid without these acts) is used by other schools to argue wujub, but the Hanafi school notes that the man was commanded to repeat the entire prayer, implying the missing elements were not rukn.
This is a classic example of usul al-fiqh in action.
5
Conclude the practical difference
In Hanafi fiqh, if one omits these sunnah acts intentionally, the prayer is still valid (sahih) but deficient. No sajdah al-sahw is required for their omission. In Shafi'i, omission invalidates the prayer because they are considered rukn.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant for daily practice.

In Hanafi fiqh, these acts are sunnah muakkadah. The lughat explains key terms. The condition for validity is that if one intentionally omits these, the prayer is valid but deficient; if one omits them unintentionally, sajdah al-sahw is not required because they are not wajib.

Key Terms

القيام بعد ركبتيه (al-qiyam ba'd rukbatayh): Standing after ruku' meaning standing upright with calmness before prostrating.
مطمئنا (mutma'innan): Calmly, with tranquility, meaning still without movement.

Sunnah Sequence for Sujud and Rising
Explanation of sunnah sequence with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah order for going into sujud and rising, and apply the hadith proof to distinguish it from other views.

Core Idea
Place knees first in sujud, then hands, then face; rise opposite – a sunnah from the Prophet's practice.

This lesson explains two of the nine sunnahs of sujud: the order of placing body parts when prostrating and when rising. The Hanafi school holds that this sequence is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), based on the explicit action of the Prophet ﷺ as reported by Wa'il ibn Hujr. Understanding this order helps avoid a common mistake and ensures one follows the optimal practice in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah order for sujud
From the text: when going into sujud, place knees first, then hands, then face (forehead). This is the first sunnah.
2
Identify the sunnah order for rising
From the text: when rising, do the opposite: lift face first, then hands, then knees. This is the second sunnah.
The phrase 'عكسه للنهوض' indicates reversal.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr explicitly describes the Prophet's practice. In Hanafi usul, a fi'l (action) of the Prophet indicates sunnah, not obligation.
Dalil is ahad, so thubut and dalala are zanni, placing the ruling at sunnah level.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school recommends placing hands before knees. The Hanafi position is based on the same hadith but interpreted differently.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both views are based on evidence.

And placing his knees, then his hands, then his face for sujud, and the opposite for rising. Translation: (426) (27) For sujud, first place both knees, then both hands, then the face. Sunnah of Takbir for Sujud and Rising
Ruling with proof for two sunnah acts in sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on takbir at sujud and rising, and identify the evidence from the sunnah.

Core Idea
Saying 'Allahu Akbar' when prostrating and rising is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.

This lesson explains two specific sunnah acts within the prayer: saying takbir when going into sujud and when rising from it. Using the hadith of Abu Hurairah, the Hanafi school establishes these as strongly recommended practices. Understanding their legal status helps avoid confusion about whether their omission invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The acts are saying takbir when going into sujud and when rising from sujud. In Hanafi fiqh, these are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Abu Hurairah in Bukhari and Muslim, which describes the Prophet's consistent practice of saying takbir with every movement.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's continuous action (fi‘l) indicates sunnah, not obligation. The takbirs are not part of the obligatory recitation (qira’ah), so they are not fard.
Hanafi usul: al-fil al-mustamirr yufidu al-sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars consider these takbirs to be wajib. The Hanafi school holds sunnah muakkadah based on the principle that any non-Quranic recitation is not fard.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon. Omitting these takbirs does not invalidate the prayer nor require sujud al-sahw.
The muftā bihi is sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text

Sunnahs of Sujud: Hand Placement and Tasbih
Enumeration of two sunnahs in sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnahs of sujud regarding hand placement and tasbih, and explain their Hanafi ruling as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
In sujud, placing the forehead between the palms and reciting tasbih three times are sunnah muakkadah.

In this lesson, we examine two specific sunnahs of the prostration position (sujud). These are part of the recommended acts that complete the prayer. Although the source text is incomplete and only provides a translation, the Hanafi school consistently teaches these as sunnah muakkadah—emphasized practices that the Prophet ﷺ never omitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
The text mentions two acts: placing the forehead between the palms during sujud, and reciting tasbih three times.
These are numbered 31 and 32 in the original enumeration.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
In the Hanafi school, both acts are sunnah muakkadah—strongly recommended but not wajib. If omitted, the prayer remains valid without compensation.
Some other schools consider the first act wajib. This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Note the minimum vs. sunnah
For tasbih, the minimum is once; the sunnah is three times. More repetitions are permissible.
4
Apply in practice
When prostrating, place your forehead between your hands on the ground, and recite 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times.
Ensure the hands are placed on the ground alongside the ears.

According to this lesson, what is the Hanafi ruling on reciting tasbih three times in sujud?
A) Fard; the prayer is invalid without it.
B) Wajib; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) Sunnah muakkadah; omission is allowed but discouraged.
D) Mustahab; one may omit it freely.

Key Takeaway
The two sunnahs of sujud are placing the forehead between the palms and reciting tasbih three times; both are sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

The Seven Sunan of Sujud in Salah
Enumeration of sunan with proofs from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven sunan of sujud according to the Hanafi school and identify their evidential basis from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The sunan of sujud perfect the prayer; omitting them does not invalidate it but reduces reward.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text enumerates the recommended acts (sunan) during prostration, distinguishing them from the obligatory elements (arkan and wajibat). The author provides clear hadith evidence for each sunnah, emphasizing the Prophet's consistent practice. Understanding these sunan helps the believer perfect their prayer by following the sunnah, while recognizing that neglect does not break the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
For each sunnah, read the description in the Arabic text and its translation. Note whether it relates to body placement, recitation, or timing. Recognize that all are sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) in the Hanafi school.
The text presents seven sunan out of nine mentioned in the chapter; focus on these.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited after each sunnah. The passage uses the term 'wajh' to introduce evidence. Identify the source (e.g., Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) and the specific wording.
Most evidene is from acts of the Prophet (fi'li sunnah) and statements (qawli sunnah).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves that the act is sunnah, not wajib. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's actions are for guidance (al-fi'l li al-tashri') unless a command indicates obligation. For example, the description of his placement of knees before hands shows the recommended order.
The takbir for sujud is evidenced by the hadith of Abu Hurairah describing the Prophet's practice.
4
Distinguish gender specifications
Note that the seventh sunnah (mujafat – keeping limbs away) is specific to men. Women are to be compact in sujud. This distinction is based on different narrations and the principle of modesty.
The text explicitly says 'the man' (الرجل).
5
Differentiate from wajib and arkan
Confirm that omitting any of these sunan does not invalidate the prayer (salah) nor require sujud al-sahw. They are recommended for completeness. If one intentionally leaves them, the prayer is still valid but the reward is less.
This is a key Hanafi distinction: sunnah muakkadah vs. wajib.
