فصل سنن الصلوة

مطمئنا (٤٢٦) ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه للسجود وعكسه للنهوض (٤٢٧) و تكبير السجود وتكبير الرفع منه (٤٢٨) وكون السجود بين كفيه وتسبيحه ثلاثا (٤٢٩) ومجا فاة الرجل بطنه عن فخذيه ومرفقيه عن جنبيه وذراعيه عن الارض

تشريح : يہاں سے سجدے کی 9 نومنتیں بیان کی جارہی ہیں۔ [1، پہلی سنت قومہ سے سجدہ میں جانے لگے تو زمین پر پہلے دونوں گھٹنے رکھے پھر دونوں ہتھیلیاں رکھے، پھر پیشانی رکھے، یہ سنت طریقہ ہے۔ [۲، دوسری سنت ] اور جب اٹھنے لگے تو اس کا الٹا کرے، یعنی پہلے پیشانی زمین سے اٹھائے، پھر دونوں ہتھیلی اٹھائے پھر گھٹنے اٹھائے۔

وجه : (۱) عن وائل بن حجر قال رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا سجد يضع ركبتيه قبل يديه و اذا نهض رفع يديه قبل ركبتيه - ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في وضع الركبتين قبل اليدين في السجود ص ۷۴ نمبر ۲۶۸/ ابوداود شریف ، باب كيف يضع ركبتيه قبل يديه، ص ۱۳۰، نمبر ۸۳۸)

ترجمه : (٤٢٧) [۲۹] سجدہ کی تکبیر - [۳۰] سجدے سے اٹھنے کی تکبیر ۔ تشریح ۳۱ تیسری سنت سجدہ میں جاتے وقت تکبیر کہنا۔ [۴ چوتھی سنت ] اور سجدہ سے سراٹھاتے وقت بھی اللہ اکبر کہنا سنت ہے

وجه:(۱) سمع أبا هريرة يقول كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام الى الصلوة .... ثم يكبر حين يهوى ثم يكبر حين يرفع رأسه، ثم يكبر حين يسجد ثم يكبر حين يرفع رأسه ثم يفعل ذالك في الصلاة كلها حتى يقضيها. (بخاری شریف، باب التكبير اذا قام من السجود ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۷۸۹ و مسلم شریف ، باب اثبات التكبير في كل خفض ورفع في الصلاۃ ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۸۶۸/۳۹۲)

ترجمه : (٤٢٨) [۳۱] سجدہ دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان کرنا۔ [۳۲] سجدہ میں تین بار تسبیح کہنا۔

تشریح : [ ۵ پانچویں سنت ] سجدہ دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان کرے۔ 11 چھٹی سنت سجدے میں تین مرتبہ تسبیح پڑھے۔

وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ قلت للبراء بن عازب اين كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يضع وجهه اذا سجد؟ فقال بين كفيه ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء این وضع الرجل وجهه اذا اسجد ، ص ۷۵ نمبر ۱۲۷۱ مسلم شریف ، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری بعد تكبيرة الاحترام ، الخ ص۱۷۰، نمبر ۸۹۶/۴۰۱ ) (۲) عن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن ابيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما سجد وضع جبهته بين كفيه وجافي عن ابطيه. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب افتتاح الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۱۶ نمبر ۷۳۶) (۳) اور تین مرتبہ تسبیح کہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا ركع احدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات : سبحان ربی العظيم وذلك ادناه فاذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربی الاعلى ثلاثا ، و ذالک ادناه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب مقدار الرکوع والسجود ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۱۸۸۶ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی التسبیح فی الرکوع والسجود ص ۶۰ نمبر ۲۶۱)

ترجمه : (٤٢٩) (۳۳) مرد پیٹ کو ران سے اور کہنی کو پہلو سے اور ہاتھ کوزمین سے علیحدہ رکھے۔

تشریح : [ ساتویں سنت ] مرد جب سجدے میں جائے تو پیٹ کو رانوں سے علیحدہ رکھے، اور دونوں کہنیوں کو پہلوؤں سے علیحدہ رکھے، اور کلائی سے اوپر کا حصہ زمین سے اونچار کھے ، زمین سے ملا کر نہ رکھے۔ یہ سنت ہے۔

وجه : (1) عن البراء قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا سجدت فضع کفیک وارفع مرفقیک، وفی حدیث آخر ، اذا صـلـي فـرج بين يديه حتى يبدو بياض ابطيه. (مسلم شریف، باب الاعتدال في السجو دو وضع الكفين على الارض، ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۱۰۴/۴۹۵/ ۱۱۰۵ار بخاری شریف ، باب یبدی ضبعیه و یجانی فی السجودص ،۱۳۱، نمبر ۸۰۷) (۲) عن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن ابيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما سجد وضع جبهته بيــن كـفيـه وجـافي عن ابطيه. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب افتتاح الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۱۶، نمبر ۷۳۶ ) (۳) عن انس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اعتدلوا في السجود و لا يبسط أحــدكـم ذراعيه انبساط الكلب ـ (مسلم شریف، باب الاعتدال في السجو دو وضع الکفین علی الارض ،ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۱۰۲٫۴۹۳)

لغت : نهوض: اٹھنا۔ مجافاۃ: الگ رہنا۔ فخذ : زران - جنب : پہلو۔ ذراعیہ: ذراع کی تثنیہ ہے، کلائی سے لیکر کہنی تک کے حصے کو ذراع کہتے ہیں۔ یہاں کلائی سے اوپر کا حصہ مراد ہے۔
Chapter: The Sunan of Prayer

With tranquility (426), and placing his knees, then his hands, then his face for prostration, and the opposite for rising (427), and the takbir for prostration and the takbir for rising from it (428), and that the prostration be between his palms, and his tasbih three times (429), and the man keeping his belly away from his thighs, his elbows from his sides, and his forearms from the ground.

Explanation: Here, nine sunan of prostration are being explained. [1, First Sunnah] When going from standing to prostration, first place both knees on the ground, then both palms, then the forehead – this is the sunnah method. [2, Second Sunnah] And when rising, do the opposite: first lift the forehead from the ground, then both palms, then both knees.

Evidence: (1) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he prostrated, he placed his knees before his hands, and when he rose, he raised his hands before his knees. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi wad' al-rukbatayn qabl al-yadayn fi al-sujud, p.74, no.268; Abu Dawud, Bab kayfa yada'u rukbatayhi qabl yadayhi, p.130, no.838)

Translation (427): [29] The takbir for prostration – [30] The takbir for rising from prostration.
Explanation: [3, Third Sunnah] To say takbir when going into prostration. [4, Fourth Sunnah] And to say Allahu Akbar when lifting the head from prostration is sunnah.

Evidence: (1) Abu Hurairah heard: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to say takbir when he went down, then say takbir when he raised his head, then say takbir when he prostrated, then say takbir when he raised his head, and he would do that throughout the entire prayer until he finished it. (Bukhari, Bab al-takbir idha qama min al-sujud, p.138, no.789; Muslim, Bab ithbat al-takbir fi kull khafd wa raf' fi al-salah, p.166, no.868/392)

Translation (428): [31] To make prostration between the two palms. [32] To recite tasbih three times in prostration.

Explanation: [5, Fifth Sunnah] Perform prostration between the two palms. [6, Sixth Sunnah] Recite tasbih three times in prostration.

Evidence: (1) A hadith: I asked al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: Where did the Prophet (peace be upon him) place his face when he prostrated? He said: Between his palms. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a ayna yada'u al-rajul wajhahu idha sajada, p.75, no.1271; Muslim, Bab wad' al-yad al-yumna 'ala al-yusra ba'd takbirat al-ihram, etc., p.170, no.896/401) (2) From 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him): When he prostrated, he placed his forehead between his palms and kept his armpits away. (Abu Dawud, Bab iftitah al-salah, p.116, no.736) (3) And reciting tasbih three times – its evidence is this hadith: From Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When one of you bows, let him say three times: 'Subhana Rabbiyal 'Adhim' – that is the minimum; and when he prostrates, let him say three times: 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' – that is the minimum. (Abu Dawud, Bab miqdar al-rukuk wa al-sujud, p.136, no.1886; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-tasbih fi al-rukuk wa al-sujud, p.60, no.261)

Translation (429): (33) The man keeps his belly away from his thighs, his elbows from his sides, and his hands (forearms) from the ground.

Explanation: [7, Seventh Sunnah] When a man goes into prostration, he should keep his belly away from his thighs, keep both elbows away from his sides, and keep the part above the wrist raised from the ground – do not place it on the ground. This is sunnah.

Evidence: (1) From al-Bara': The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When you prostrate, place your palms and raise your elbows. In another hadith: When he prayed, he would spread his arms so that the whiteness of his armpits appeared. (Muslim, Bab al-i'tidal fi al-sujud wa wad' al-kaffayn 'ala al-ard, p.203, no.1104/495/1105; Bukhari, Bab yubdi dhab'ayhi wa yujani fi al-sujud, p.131, no.807) (2) From 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him): When he prostrated, he placed his forehead between his palms and kept his armpits away. (Abu Dawud, Bab iftitah al-salah, p.116, no.736) (3) From Anas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Be moderate in prostration and do not spread your forearms like a dog spreads its paws. (Muslim, Bab al-i'tidal fi al-sujud wa wad' al-kaffayn 'ala al-ard, p.203, no.1102/493)

Vocabulary: Nahud: rising. Mujafah: keeping away. Fakhidh: thigh. Janb: side. Dhira'ayn: dual of dhira' – the part from wrist to elbow; here it means the part above the wrist.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the sunan (recommended acts) of prostration (sujud) in prayer, as derived from authentic hadith. The text enumerates seven sunan (out of nine mentioned) with their evidences. The first sunnah is the order of placing body parts when going into sujud: knees first, then hands, then face. The second is the reverse when rising: face, then hands, then knees. The evidence is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr. The third and fourth sunan are the takbir when lowering into sujud and when rising from it, supported by the hadith of Abu Hurairah. The fifth sunnah is that the prostration is performed between the palms, and the sixth is reciting 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times, with the minimum being three (though more is better). The seventh sunnah, specific to men, is to keep the belly away from the thighs, elbows away from the sides, and forearms raised off the ground, in contrast to women who are advised to be more compact. All these are sunnah, not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but reduces its reward. The author uses the term 'sunnah' as defined in the Hanafi school, meaning an act that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, but which is not wajib or fard.

Key Terms
سجدہ (sajdah): Prostration – the act of placing the forehead on the ground in prayer.
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' when moving into and out of prostration.
تسبیح (tasbih): Glorification of Allah, specifically 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in sujud.
مجافاۃ (mujafat): Keeping the limbs away from the body during prostration (for men).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sunnah order for a man when rising from prostration?
A) Lift forehead, then palms, then knees.
B) Lift palms, then knees, then forehead.
C) Lift knees, then palms, then forehead.
D) Lift forehead, then knees, then palms.

Key Takeaway
The seven sunan of sujud are confirmed recommended practices; following them perfects the prayer, but omitting them does not invalidate it.

Men's Sunnahs in Sajdah: Palms, Tasbih, and Mujafaat
Describes three sunnahs for men in sajdah with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts for men in sajdah and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
In sajdah, a man places his forehead between his palms, recites tasbih three times, and keeps his body parts separated.

This lesson examines three specific sunnah acts for men during sajdah (prostration) as taught by the Prophet ﷺ and preserved in the Hanafi school. We will explore the textual evidence from authentic hadith and the precise legal manner of performing these acts. Understanding these sunnahs helps perfect one’s prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunnahs
Locate the three acts listed: placing forehead between palms, saying tasbih three times, and mujafaat (separation of body parts).
These are numbered as the 5th, 6th, and 7th sunnahs of sajdah in the commentary.
2
Locate the hadith evidence for each
For each sunnah, find the hadith cited. Note the narrators and sources (e.g., al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, Ibn Mas'ud, Anas).
The hadith are from Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Bukhari.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each hadith proves the sunnah. For example, 'between his palms' directly indicates placement of the forehead.
The Hanafi school treats these as sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.
4
Note the gender distinction
Recognize that mujafaat is specific to men; women are to perform takhaffud (drawing limbs close).
This is a key differentiator in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Recognize the sunnah level
These acts are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah). Their omission does not invalidate prayer but reduces perfection.
The author uses multiple hadith to stress their importance.

وكون السجود بين كفيه وتسبيحه ثلاثا ( (٤٢٩) ومجا فاة الرجل بطنه عن فخذيه ومرفقيه عن جنبيه وذراعيه عن الارض (٤٣٠) تشريح : [ ٥ پانچویں سنت ] سجدہ دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان کرے۔ 11 چھٹی سنت سجدے میں تین مرتبہ تسبیح پڑھے۔ صلى الله وجه : (١) حدیث میں ہے۔ قلت للبراء بن عازب اين كان النبي عل يضع وجهه اذا سجد؟ فقال بين كفيه ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء این وضع الرجل وجهه اذا اسجد ، ص ٧٥ نمبر ١٢٧١ مسلم شریف ، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری بعد تكبيرة الاحترام ، الخ ص١٧٠، نمبر ٨٩٦/٤٠١ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سجدے کے وقت چہرے کو دونوں ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان رکھے۔ (٢) صلى الله عن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن ابيه عن النبي عله فلما سجد وضع جبهته بين كفيه وجافي عن ابطيه. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب افتتاح الصلوۃ ، ص ١١٦ نمبر ٧٣٦) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ کے وقت چہرہ ہتھیلیوں کے درمیان رکھے۔ (٣) اور تین مرتبہ تسبیح کہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن مسعود قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا ركع صلى الله احدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات : سبحان ربی العظيم وذلك ادناه فاذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربی الاعلى ثلاثا ، و ذالک ادناه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب مقدار الرکوع والسجود ص ١٣٦، نمبر ١٨٨٦ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی التسبیح فی الرکوع والسجو د ص ٦٠ نمبر ٢٦١) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین مرتبہ سبحان ربی الاعلی ، کہے یہ ادنی مرتبہ ہے۔ ترجمه : (٤٢٩) (٣٣) مرد پیٹ کو ران سے اور کہنی کو پہلو سے اور ہاتھ کوزمین سے علیحدہ رکھے۔ تشريح : [ ساتویں سنت ] مرد جب سجدے میں جائے تو پیٹ کو رانوں سے علیحدہ رکھے، اور دونوں کہنیوں کو پہلوؤں سے علیحدہ رکھے، اور کلائی سے اوپر کا حصہ زمین سے اونچار کھے ، زمین سے ملا کر نہ رکھے۔ یہ سنت ہے۔ وجه : (1) عن البراء قال قال رسول الله الله اذا سجدت فضع کفیک وارفع مرفقیک، وفی حدیث آخر ، اذا صـلـي فـرج بين يديه حتى يبدو بیاض ابطيه. (مسلم شریف، باب الاعتدال في السجو دو وضع الكفين على الارض، ص ٢٠٣، نمبر ١١٠٤/٤٩٥/ ١١٠٥ار بخاری شریف ، باب یبدی ضبعیه و یجانی فی السجودص ،١٣١، نمبر ٨٠٧) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کہنیوں کو اونچارکھے اور پہلو سے الگ رکھے۔ (٢) عن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن ابيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما سجد وضع صلى الله صلى الله جبهته بيــن كـفيـه وجـافي عن ابطيه. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب افتتاح الصلوۃ ، ص ١١٦، نمبر ٧٣٦ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہتھیلیوں سے پہلوؤں کو الگ رکھے۔ (٣) عن انس قال قال رسول الله له اعتدلوا في السجود و لا يبسط أحــدكـم ذراعيه انبساط الكلب ـ (مسلم شریف، باب الاعتدال في السجو دو وضع الکفین علی الارض ،ص ٢٠٣، نمبر ١١٠٢·٤٩٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کتے کی طرح ہاتھ کو زمین پر نہ بچھائے بلکہ اس کو اونچار کھے۔ لغت : نهوض: اٹھنا۔ مجافاۃ: الگ رہنا۔ فخذ : زران - جنب : پہلو۔ ذراعیہ: ذراع کی تثنیہ ہے، کلائی سے لیکر کہنی تک کے حصے کو ذراع کہتے ہیں۔ یہاں کلائی سے اوپر کا حصہ مراد ہے۔
And the prostration between his palms, and his tasbih three times, and the man's separation of his belly from his thighs, his elbows from his sides, and his forearms from the ground. Commentary: [5th sunnah] He should prostrate between his two palms. [6th sunnah] He should recite tasbih three times in prostration. Evidence: (1) In a hadith: I asked al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, 'Where would the Prophet place his face when he prostrated?' He said, 'Between his palms.' ... (2) ... (3) ... Translation: (429) (33) The man keeps his belly away from his thighs, his elbows from his sides, and his hands from the ground. Commentary: [7th sunnah] When a man goes into prostration, he should keep his belly away from his thighs, both elbows away from his sides, and the part above the wrist raised from the ground, not placing it on the ground. This is sunnah. Evidence: (1) ... (2) ... (3) ... Glossary: ...
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering three sunnah acts for men in sajdah. The author first lists the rulings concisely: (1) placing the forehead between the palms, (2) saying 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times, and (3) the mujafaat (separation) of the belly from thighs, elbows from sides, and forearms from the ground. Then the commentary explains each as the 5th, 6th, and 7th sunnahs of sajdah. For the first two, hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib and Ibn Mas'ud are cited showing that the Prophet placed his forehead between his palms and instructed tasbih three times as the minimum. For the mujafaat, hadith from al-Bara', 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il, and Anas are quoted showing the Prophet raised his elbows, kept them away from his sides, and forbade spreading arms like a dog. The glossary defines key terms: 'mujafaat' means separation, 'fakhdh' is thigh, 'janb' is side, and 'dhira'' is the forearm from wrist to elbow. These sunnahs distinguish men's posture from women's, as will be explained next.

Key Terms
مجافاة (mujafaat): The act of keeping body parts separated; here, the man keeping his belly away from thighs, elbows from sides, and forearms from the ground during sajdah.
تسبيح (tasbih): The utterance of 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' (Glory to my Lord, the Most High) at least three times during sajdah.
ذراع (dhira'): The forearm from wrist to elbow; in this context, the part above the wrist should be raised off the ground during sajdah for men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three times
C) Five times
D) Seven times

Key Takeaway
Three sunnah acts for men in sajdah: placing forehead between palms, reciting tasbih three times, and separating body parts (mujafaat).

Qawmah and Jalsah: Sunnah Postures in Prayer
Describes qawmah and jalsah as sunnah acts in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qawmah and jalsah, explain the dalil, and distinguish the sunnah status from fard/wajib.

Core Idea
Qawmah and jalsah are sunnah muakkadah; omitting them does not invalidate prayer but diminishes its perfection.

In the Hanafi school, the postures of qawmah (standing after ruku) and jalsah (sitting between prostrations) are considered sunnah muakkadah—strongly recommended but not obligatory. The text cites the famous hadith of the man who prayed improperly, where the Prophet instructed tranquility (tuma'ninah) in each posture. Understanding why Hanafis classify these as sunnah rather than wajib is key to grasping the school's method of weighting proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the postures and ruling
From the text, qawmah is the standing after ruku, jalsah is the sitting between sajdahs. The text explicitly says 'it is sunnah'. Note that this is the 9th and 10th sunnah of sajdah.
2
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of the man who prayed improperly includes commands for each posture with tuma'ninah. The addition from Abu Dawud says 'if you do this, your prayer is complete'—implying these are integral. But Hanafi usul classifies this as sunnah, not wajib.
Look at the Hanafi interpretation: the Prophet did not order the man to repeat when he omitted these, only taught them for completeness.
3
Distinguish from other schools
Shafi'is consider tuma'ninah in these postures as wajib. The Hanafi position is based on the fact that the command is for perfection (tamam) not validity (sihha).
Cross-madhhab: note the practical difference—omission requires sajdah sahw for Shafi'is; Hanafis consider it makruh without compensation.
4
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario where someone omits qawmah or jalsah, the prayer is valid but less perfect. The mufta bihi is sunnah muakkadah.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad said wajib, but the relied-upon view is sunnah.

Source Text

(ابوداؤد شریف، باب صلوۃ من لا یتقیم صلبه فی الرکوع والسجود، ص ١٣٢، نمبر ٨٥٦) اس حدیث میں
And qawmah and jalsah between the two prostrations. Translation: (431) [35] Qawmah. [36] Jalsah between the two prostrations. Commentary: [9th sunnah] When he stands up from ruku, he should stand with tranquility; this is called qawmah; it is sunnah. [10th sunnah] He should sit with tranquility between the two prostrations; this is called jalsah; it is also sunnah. These are the ten sunnahs of sajdah. Then evidence: (1) ... hadith ... (2) In Abu Dawud it adds: 'If you do this, your prayer is complete; and whatever you omit from it, you have only diminished from your prayer.'
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents the 9th and 10th sunnahs of sajdah: qawmah (standing after ruku with tranquility) and jalsah (sitting between the two sajdahs with tranquility). The commentary notes that these are sunnah, not wajib. The text cites the famous hadith of the man who prayed improperly; the Prophet instructed him to perform each posture with tranquility (tuma'ninah). The addition from Abu Dawud emphasizes that completion of the prayer depends on fulfilling these elements. The passage concludes stating these complete the ten sunnahs of sajdah. This ruling is standard in the Hanafi school; qawmah and jalsah are considered sunnah, not fard or wajib, but their omission diminishes the prayer.

Key Terms
قومة (qawmah): The standing posture after rising from ruku, performed with tranquility (tuma'ninah).
جلسة (jalsah): The sitting posture between the two sajdahs, performed with tranquility.
اطمئنان (tuma'ninah): Tranquility or calmness; remaining still for a moment in each posture.

Woman's Posture in Sajdah: A Stressed Sunnah for Modesty
Hadith-based ruling on women's sajdah posture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's posture in sajdah and identify its proof from hadith.

Core Idea
A woman prostrates compactly, sticking her belly to her thighs, for greater modesty — this is a stressed sunnah.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah explains the eighth sunnah of salah: the woman's posture in prostration. While men are commanded to spread out, women are to lower and compact themselves. This distinction is based on explicit Prophetic commands and has roots in modesty. We will examine the ruling, its evidence, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the woman's posture during sajdah: she should shrink and stick her belly to her thighs. The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah (stressed sunnah), as indicated by the Urdu commentary calling it the eighth sunnah.
Sunnah muakkadah is a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three proofs: (1) a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet commanded men to spread out and women to lower themselves in sajdah; (2) a hadith from Ibn Umar stating the woman should stick her belly to her thighs as it is more concealing; (3) athar from Ali and Ibn Abbas confirming the same.
The primary evidence is the hadith in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command (يأمر) in the hadith indicates a recommended act (sunnah), not an obligation, because other proofs allow women to prostrate like men if needed. The act of sticking the belly to the thighs is derived from the word 'taltasiq' (تلتصق) in the Ibn Umar hadith.
Hanafi usul: al-amr indicates wujub unless there is a qarinah, here the qarinah is that the same act can be done differently.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not differentiate between men and women in sajdah posture; they hold that women should also spread out slightly, but less than men. The Hanafi position is based on the explicit command tailored to women's modesty.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different interpretations of the same hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi mufta bihi position is that women should adopt the compact posture. It is considered a sunnah muakkadah, and the evidence from multiple narrations supports it. Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., works of fatawa mutakhkhirin) uphold this as the relied-upon practice.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin, indicating it is well-established in later fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(430) وانخفاظ المرأة ولزقها بطنها بفخذيها
ترجمه : (430) [34] عورت سکڑے اور پیٹ کوران سے ملا دے۔
تشریح : [ 8 آٹھویں سنت ] عورت ران کو پیٹ اور پہلو سے ملائے اور ذرا سکڑ کرسجدہ کرے۔
وجه : (ا) عن ابي سعيد الخدري صاحب رسول الله عن رسول الله انه قال خير صفوف الرجال الاول و خير صفوف النساء الصف الاخر و كان يأمر الرجال ان يتجافوا في سجودهم و يأمر النساء ينخفضن في سجودهن - ( سنن بيھقي ، باب ما يستحب للمرأة من ترك التجافي في الركوع والسجود، ج ثانی، ص 1314 نمبر 3198)۔ (2) عن عبد الله ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله اذا جلست المرأة في الصلوة وضعت فخذها على فخذها الاخرى واذا سجدت الصقت بطنها في فخذها كأستر ما يكون لها ۔ (سنن بيھقي ، باب ما يستحب للمرأة من ترك التجافي في الركوع والسجود، ج ثانی ، ص 1314، نمبر 3199) (3) اثر میں ہے۔ عن على قال : اذا سجدت المرأة فلتحتفر و لتضم فخذيها (2) عن ابن عباس أنه سئل عن صلوة المرأة فقال : تجتمع و تحتفر (مصنف ابن ابي شية ، المرأة كيف تكون في سجودها ، ج اول ص 242، نمبر2778/2777) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت سجدے کے اندر سکڑ کر رہے اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے ملا دے تاکہ زیادہ سے زیادہ ستر ہو سکے ، یہی اسکے لئے بہتر ہے۔
لغت انخفض : سکڑنا۔ لزق: چپکنا۔ فخذ : ران۔
(430) And the lowering of the woman and her sticking her belly to her thighs. Translation: (430) [34] The woman shrinks and sticks her belly to her thighs. Explanation: [8th sunnah] The woman brings her thighs to her belly and sides and prostrates while somewhat shrinking. Proof: (1) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet said: The best rows of men are the first, and the best rows of women are the last, and he used to command men to spread out in their prostration and command women to lower themselves in their prostration. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is recommended for women to avoid spreading in bowing and prostration, vol. 2, p. 1314, no. 3198). (2) From Abdullah ibn Umar: The Prophet said: When a woman sits in prayer, she places one thigh on the other, and when she prostrates, she sticks her belly to her thighs, as it is more concealing for her. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, same chapter, p. 1314, no. 3199). (3) There is an athar: From Ali: When a woman prostrates, she should draw herself together and join her thighs. (2) From Ibn Abbas that he was asked about a woman's prayer, and he said: She should gather herself and draw together. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on how a woman should be in her prostration, vol. 1, p. 242, nos. 2777/2778). From this hadith and athar, it is learned that the woman should shrink in prostration and stick her belly to her thighs so that more covering is achieved; this is better for her. Vocabulary: انخفض: to shrink. لزق: to stick. فخذ: thigh.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage explains the eighth sunnah of prostration: the woman's posture. The Arabic matn states two actions: lowering (انخفاظ) and sticking (لزق) the belly to the thighs. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the woman should bring her thighs to her belly and sides and prostrate in a compact manner. The evidence includes three proofs: (1) a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing that the Prophet commanded women to lower themselves in sajdah while men spread out; (2) a hadith from Ibn Umar emphasizing that this posture is more concealing; (3) athar from Ali and Ibn Abbas confirming the same. The lesson is that women are to perform sajdah in a compact posture for modesty, unlike men who spread out.

Key Terms
انخفاظ (inkhifāḍ): Lowering or shrinking of the body during prostration, specifically for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the recommended posture for a woman in sajdah?
A) Spreading her arms like men
B) Sticking her belly to her thighs and shrinking
C) Raising her back high
D) Placing her forehead on the ground without any specific posture

Key Takeaway
A woman's sajdah posture is sunnah muakkadah: she should be compact, sticking her belly to her thighs, for modesty.

Placing Hands on Thighs Between Sajdahs (Eleventh Sunnah)
Position of hands during the sitting between two prostrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the position of the hands during the sitting between the two prostrations and identify the hadith proof for this sunnah.

Core Idea
The Prophet placed his hands on his thighs between sajdahs—follow his practice for complete prayer.

This lesson covers the eleventh sunnah of salah: placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah). Although a small detail, following the Prophet's exact posture brings the prayer closer to his sunnah and perfects its form. The source passage provides both the ruling and the hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? Placing hands on thighs during the sitting between two sajdahs. What is the ruling? Sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's consistent practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Asim ibn Kulayb describes the Prophet's posture: he placed his left hand on his left thigh and right hand on his right thigh, clenching fingers except the index finger.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Nasa'i, classified as ahad.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action is a model for the ummah. His consistent practice indicates recommendation (sunnah) rather than obligation, as there is no command with implied compulsion.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates sunnah unless proven otherwise.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (difference)
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) recommend placing hands on the knees instead. The Hanafi position relies on the hadith above.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions have evidence.
5
Apply the ruling
When performing salah, deliberately place both hands on your thighs during the sitting between sajdahs, as well as during tashahhud.
This small action earns reward and perfects the prayer.

ترجمه : (432) [37] دو سجدوں کے درمیان دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں رانوں پر رکھے ، جیسے تشہد میں رکھتے ہیں۔ تشریح : دو سجدوں کے درمیان بیٹھے تو دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں رانوں پر رکھے ، جیسے تشہد کے وقت دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں رانوں پر رکھتے ہیں۔ وجه : (ا) عاصم بن كليب الجرمي عن ابيه عن جده قال دخلت على النبى وهو يصلى وقد وضع يده اليسرى على فخذه اليسرى ووضع يده اليمنى على فخذه اليمنى وقبض اصابعه وبسط السبابة_ ترمذي شریف ، باب ابواب الدعاء، كتاب الدعوات، ص 817 نمبر 3587 نسائي شریف ، باب قبض الحنين من اصابع اليد اليمنى وعقد الوسطى، ص42 نمبر 1269) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جلسہ یا تشہد میں بیٹھے تو دائیں ہاتھ کو دائیں ران پر اور بائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ران پر رکھے۔
Translation: (432) [37] Place both hands on both thighs between the two prostrations, like in tashahhud. Explanation: When sitting between the two prostrations, place both hands on both thighs, as one places both hands on both thighs during tashahhud. Proof: (1) Asim ibn Kulayb al-Jarmi from his father from his grandfather said: I entered upon the Prophet while he was praying, and he had placed his left hand on his left thigh and his right hand on his right thigh, and he clenched his fingers and extended his index finger. (Tirmidhi, chapter on chapters of supplication, book of supplications, p. 817 no. 3587; Nasa'i, chapter on grasping the fingers of the right hand and bending the middle finger, p. 42 no. 1269). In this hadith, it is mentioned that when sitting in jalsah or tashahhud, one should place the right hand on the right thigh and the left hand on the left thigh.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage explains the eleventh sunnah: placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah), just as in tashahhud. The Urdu commentary reiterates the same. The proof is a hadith from Asim ibn Kulayb describing the Prophet's posture in prayer: both hands on respective thighs, with fingers clenched and index finger extended. This sunnah applies to both jalsah and tashahhud.

Key Terms
وضع اليدين (waḍʿ al-yadayn): Placing hands on thighs during sitting postures in prayer.

Sitting Posture: Iftirash for Men, Tawarruk for Women
Description of sitting postures in jalsah and tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the sunnah sitting postures for men (iftirash) and women (tawarruk) in prayer, and cite the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Men sit on the left foot, right erect; women sit on both feet to the right — both sunnah muakkadah.

The twelfth sunnah of salah concerns the sitting posture in jalsah and tashahhud. This passage details the specific postures prescribed for men and women, supported by authentic hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi and Wa'il ibn Hujr. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly performing the prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sunnah acts
Recognise that the passage prescribes iftirash for men and tawarruk for women as sunnah muakkadah.
Iftirash: spread left foot, right foot erect. Tawarruk: both feet to the right, sit on buttocks.
2
Examine the proofs for iftirash
Look at the hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi (first two rak'ahs) and Wa'il ibn Hujr (tashahhud) that describe the Prophet sitting on his left foot and erecting the right.
These are ahad ahadith, but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Examine the proof for tawarruk
Review the hadith of Abu Humaid describing the Prophet's tawarruk in the last sitting, which the Hanafis apply specifically to women.
Hanafis specify tawarruk for women based on modesty, though the hadith is general.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Understand that Shafi'is apply tawarruk to men in the last sitting, while Hanafis restrict it to women.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its own proof.

Source Text

ترجمه : (433) [38] بائیں پاؤں کو بچھانا اور داہنے کو کھڑا رکھنا۔ [39] عورت سرین پر بیٹھے۔
تشریح : مرد جلسہ میں یا تشہد میں بیٹھے تو دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا رکھے اور بائیں پاؤں بچھائے اور اس پر بیٹھے۔
وجه : (1) فقال ابو حميد الساعدي .... فاذا جلس في الركعتين جلس على رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمنى واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته ( بخاری شریف ، باب سنة الجلوس في التشهد، ص134، نمبر 828 مسلم شریف ، باب ما تجمع صفته الصلوة وما تفتح به ص 205، نمبر 10/498)

( ابوداؤد شریف، باب من ذكر التورك في الرابعة، ص 146 نمبر 1963 مسلم شریف ، باب صفته الجلوس في الصلوة وكيفية وضع اليدين على الفخذين، ص 235 نمبر 1307/579) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں تورک مسنون ہے ، حنفیہ نے اس کو عورت کے بارے خاص کر لیا۔ (2) فقال ابو حميد الساعدي..... واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الأخرى وقعد على مقعدته - (بخاری شریف، باب سنة الجلوس في التشهد
Translation: (433) [38] Spreading the left foot and keeping the right upright. [39] The woman sits on her buttocks. Explanation: When a man sits in jalsah or tashahhud, he should keep the right foot upright and spread the left foot and sit on it. Proof: (1) Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi said: ... when he sat in the two rak'ahs, he sat on his left foot and erected the right; and when he sat in the last rak'ah, he put forward his left foot, erected the other, and sat on his buttocks. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on the sunnah of sitting in tashahhud, p. 134 no. 828; Sahih Muslim, chapter on the complete description of prayer and what it begins with, p. 205 no. 10/498). (2) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: I came to Madinah and said, 'I will look at the prayer of the Messenger of Allah.' When he sat for tashahhud, he spread his left foot and placed his left hand on his left thigh and erected his right foot. (Tirmidhi, chapter on how to sit in tashahhud, p. 79 no. 292). In this hadith, it is stated that he erected the right foot and spread the left. Explanation: For the woman, she does tawarruk in tashahhud, i.e., she puts both feet to the right side and sits on her buttocks. Proof: (1) From Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi: ... until when he performed the prostration in which there is the taslim, he moved his left foot back and sat in tawarruk on his left side. (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on mentioning tawarruk in the fourth, p. 146 no. 1963; Muslim, chapter on the description of sitting in prayer and how to place the hands on the thighs, p. 235 no. 1307/579). From this hadith, it is established that tawarruk is sunnah in the last sitting; the Hanafis have specified it for women. (2) Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi said: ... and when he sat in the last rak'ah, he put forward his left foot, erected the other, and sat on his buttocks. (Bukhari, chapter on the sunnah of sitting in tashahhud).
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage explains the twelfth sunnah: the sitting posture for men and women. For men, in both jalsah and tashahhud, the sunnah is iftirash: sitting on the spread left foot with the right foot erect. Two hadith are cited: from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi (in the first two rak'ahs) and from Wa'il ibn Hujr (in tashahhud). For women, the sunnah is tawarruk: sitting on the buttocks with both feet to the right side. The proof is from a hadith of Abu Humaid describing the Prophet's tawarruk in the last sitting, which Hanafis apply specifically to women. The commentary notes that Hanafis have specified tawarruk for women, while the general sunnah for men is iftirash.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirāsh): Sitting on the spread left foot with the right foot erect.
تورك (tawarruk): Sitting on the buttocks with both feet to the right side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tawarruk on the left side
B) Iftirash: left foot spread, right foot erect
C) Kneeling on both knees
D) Sitting cross-legged

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes iftirash for men and tawarruk for women in all sittings, based on hadith and consideration of modesty.

Placing Hands on Thighs Between Prostrations
Ruling on sunnah hand placement between sajdahs with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling (sunnah muakkadah) for hand placement between sajdahs and cite the proof from the hadith of 'Asim ibn Kulayb.

Core Idea
Placing hands on thighs between sajdahs is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.

This lesson clarifies a common point of sunnah in prayer: where to place your hands when sitting between the two prostrations. The Hanafi school considers this an emphasized sunnah based on the Prophet's practice. Let's examine the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing both hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah). The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
Sunnah muakkadah is an emphasized sunnah; omitting it is disliked but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of 'Asim ibn Kulayb, which describes the Prophet's hand placement during prayer.
This is a hadith ahad (single-chain narration), which is zanni in transmission but accepted for establishing sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit description of the Prophet's action indicates that this is a sunnah act; emulating his actions in prayer is recommended.
The hadith states: 'He placed his left hand on his left thigh and his right hand on his right thigh.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools consider it only mustahabb (recommended) or do not specify, but the Hanafi school emphasizes it as muakkadah due to consistency of practice.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the validity of prayer.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because it is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith and the practice of the early Muslims. It is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is sunnah muakkadah.

ترجمه : (۴۳۲) [۳۷] دو سجدوں کے درمیان دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں رانوں پر رکھے ، جیسے تشہد میں رکھتے ہیں۔ تشریح : دو سجدوں کے درمیان بیٹھے تو دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں رانوں پر رکھے ، جیسے تشہد کے وقت دونوں ہاتھوں کو دونوں رانوں پر رکھتے ہیں۔ وجه : (ا) عاصم بن كليب الجرمي عن ابيه عن جده قال دخلت على النبى عـ ا وهو يصلى وقد وضع يده اليسرى عـلـى فـخـذه اليسرى ووضع يده اليمنى على فخذه اليمنى وقبض اصابعه وبسط السبابة_ صلى الله مندی شریف ، باب ابواب الدعاء، کتاب الدعوات، ص ۸۱۷ نمبر ۳۵۸۷ رنسائی شریف ، باب قبض الحنين من اصابع اليد الیمنی وعقد الوسطی ، ص۴۲ نمبر ۱۲۶۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جلسہ یا تشہد میں بیٹھے تو دائیں ہاتھ کو دائیں ران پر اور بائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ران پر رکھے۔
Section: Sunnah of prayer. (432) And placing the two hands on the two thighs between the two prostrations like the state of tashahhud. (433) And spreading [the left] foot... Translation: (432) [37] Between the two prostrations, he should place both hands on both thighs, just as he places them in tashahhud. Explanation: When sitting between the two prostrations, he places both hands on both thighs, like at the time of tashahhud. Evidence: (1) 'Asim ibn Kulayb al-Jarmi from his father from his grandfather: 'I entered upon the Prophet ﷺ while he was praying, and he had placed his left hand on his left thigh and his right hand on his right thigh, and he clenched his fingers and extended the index finger.'

Commentary
This passage clarifies the sunnah placement of hands during the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah). According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah to place both hands on the thighs, palms down, with fingers spread, similar to the tashahhud position. The proof is the hadith from 'Asim ibn Kulayb, which describes the Prophet's hand placement during prayer. The text emphasizes that this is sunnah, not wajib, and failure to do so does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
سنن الصلوة (sunan al-salah): Acts recommended (sunnah) in prayer, distinct from obligatory (fard) and necessary (wajib) elements.
تعدیل ارکان (ta'dil al-arkan): Performing the pillars of prayer with calmness and deliberation, not hurriedly.

Finger Gesture During Tashahhud
Ruling on raising the index finger during tashahhud in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the index finger gesture in tashahhud and identify the supporting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Raise the index finger once at 'la ilaha', lower at 'illa Allah' — a sunnah act, not wajib.

In this lesson, we examine the sunnah practice of pointing with the index finger during the tashahhud in prayer. The Hanafi school holds this as a sunnah muakkadah based on several authentic hadith. Understanding the correct method and its evidentiary basis is important for proper performance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
The sunnah is to raise the index finger once at 'la ilaha' and lower at 'illa Allah'. This is a sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Identify the primary hadith evidence
The passage cites multiple hadith, including from Wa'il ibn Hujr, 'Asim ibn Kulayb, and Ibn Umar. Identify each and note what they say about the finger gesture.
The hadith describe making a ring with thumb and middle finger and pointing with the index finger.
3
Analyze the juridical link
How does the prophetic action prove the sunnah? The explicit description of pointing indicates it is a recommended act.
The dalala is qati: the action clearly indicates the sunnah.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
While Hanafis consider it sunnah, other schools may view it differently. The passage notes that some consider it mustahabb or even bid'ah.
This is an ikhtilaf that does not affect the Hanafi position.
5
Determine the operative ruling
The mufta bihi is the one gesture at the testimony. The passage also clarifies that no hadith was found for exactly raising at 'la' and lowering at 'illa', but it is derived from practice.
The timing is based on scholarly interpretation of the combined evidence.

تشریح : تحیات میں تشہد پڑھتے وقت جب لا الہ پر پہونچے تو شہادت کی انگلی کو اٹھائے اورالا اللہ پر نیچے کردے ،شروع تحیات سے انگلی سے بار بار اشارہ کرتا رہے ایسا نہ کرے۔
وجه : (۱) عن وائل بن حجر قال ... ثم جلس فافترش رجله اليسرى ووضع يده اليسرى على فخذه اليسرى وحـد مـرفـقـه الايمن على فخذه اليمنى وقبض ثنتين و حلق حلقة ورأيته يقول هكذا وحلق بشر الابهام والوسطى واشار بالسبابة (ابوداؤد شريف، باب کیف الجلوس في التشهد ، ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۹۵۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ انگوٹھے اور درمیان کی انگلی سے حلقہ بنائے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے اشارہ کرے (۳) عاصم بن كليب الجرمي عن ابيه عن صلى الله جده قال دخلت على النبي علم وهو يصلى وقد وضع يده اليسرى على فخذه اليسرى ووضع يده اليمنى على فخذه اليمنى وقبض اصابعه وبسط السبابة ( ترمذی شریف، باب ابواب الدعاء ج ثانی ص ۸۱۷ نمبر ۱۳۵۸۷ نسائی شریف ، باب قبض النتین من اصابع الید الیمنی وعقد الوسطی، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر ۱۲۶۹) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ حلقہ بنائے اور شہادت کی انگلی سے اشارہ کرے۔ (۴) صرف ایک مرتبہ اشارہ کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔عن عبد الله انه ذكر ان النبي الله كان يشير باصبعه اذا دعا لا يحر كھا ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب من روی اندا شار بھا ولم بحر كھا، ج ثانی ص ۱۸۹ نمبر ۲۷۸۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بار بار حرکت نہیں کرتے تھے صرف ایک بار شارہ کرتے تھے (۵) عـن ابـن عـمـر انـه رای رجلا يـحـرك الـحصا..... قال فوضع يده اليمنى على فخذه و اشار باصبعه التي تلى الابهام في القبلة و رمى ببصره اليها او نحوها ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله الا الله يصنع - (سنن بیہقی ، باب الاشارة بالمسمية الى القبلة ، ج ثانی ،ص۱۹۰، نمبر ۲۷۸۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قبلہ کی طرف ایک مرتبہ اشارہ فرمایا۔
لا الہ الا اللہ کے وقت اشارہ کرے۔ لا کے وقت انگلی کھڑی کرے اور الا اللہ کے وقت گرائے اس کی حدیث نہیں ملی۔
(434) [40] In the correct narration, at the time of shahadah, he should point with the index finger. At 'la ilaha' he should raise it, and at 'illa Allah' he should put it down. Explanation: When reciting the tashahhud, upon reaching 'la ilaha', he should raise the index finger, and at 'illa Allah', put it down. He should not keep moving the finger from the beginning. Evidence: (1) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: '...then he sat, spread his left foot, placed his left hand on his left thigh, placed his right elbow on his right thigh, clasped two fingers, made a ring, and I saw him saying thus, and he made a ring with thumb and middle finger and pointed with the index finger.' (3) 'Asim ibn Kulayb: '...he clenched his fingers and extended the index finger.' (4) Only one gesture: 'The Prophet would point with his finger when supplicating and not move it.' (5) 'Ibn Umar saw a man moving pebbles... he placed his right hand on his thigh and pointed with his finger towards the qiblah, fixed his sight on it, and said: Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah do.' He should point at the time of 'la ilaha illa Allah', raising at 'la' and lowering at 'illa Allah'; no hadith was found for this.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage addresses the sunnah of using the index finger (al-musabbihah) during tashahhud. According to the Hanafi school, the sunnah is to raise the index finger once when reciting 'la ilaha' and lower it at 'illa Allah'. The finger is not to be moved repeatedly. The evidence includes several hadith describing the Prophet's practice: making a ring with thumb and middle finger, extending the index finger, and pointing towards the qiblah. Some narrations indicate a single gesture without motion. The author notes that no specific hadith was found for the exact timing of raising and lowering at 'la ilaha illa Allah', but it is derived from practice.

Key Terms
المسبحة (al-musabbihah): The index finger, specifically used to point during tashahhud as a sunnah gesture.
الاشارة (al-isharah): The act of pointing with the finger during tashahhud, done once at the testimony of faith.

Reciting Surah Fatiha in Later Rak'ahs
Ruling on reciting Surah Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Surah Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of fard prayer, cite the primary proof, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i school by identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Reciting Fatiha in later rak'ahs is sunnah, not fard; omitting it does not invalidate prayer.

This passage addresses one of the well-known differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether reciting Surah Fatiha in the third and fourth rak'ahs of fard prayer is obligatory or merely recommended. The author presents the Hanafi view that it is sunnah, supported by the Prophet's ﷺ practice, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position that it is a fard pillar. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps clarify the structure of prayer obligations across madhahib.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling in the passage: In the third and fourth rak'ahs of fard, reciting Surah Fatiha is sunnah. If one recites nothing, the prayer is still valid.
The text explicitly says 'reciting Surah Fatiha is sunnah'.
2
Identify the opposing school and its claim
The passage mentions 'other imams' – referring to Imam al-Shafi'i – who hold that reciting Fatiha in every rak'ah is fard (obligatory).
This is the core of the inter-madhhab dispute.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the two hadith cited: (1) The Prophet ﷺ recited only Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr (hadith of Abu Qatada). (2) Sa'd's practice of shortening in the last two rak'ahs was approved by Umar. Both show the sunnah is to recite only Fatiha.
The Hanafi dalil is explicit practice (fi'l) of the Prophet.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school relies on general commands to recite Fatiha. The Hanafi response is that those commands are specified (takhsis) by the Prophet's actual practice in later rak'ahs, which indicates a lower level of obligation.
This is a usul al-fiqh argument: amm becomes khass by sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In the Hanafi school, omitting Fatiha in later rak'ahs does not require sajdah sahw or invalidate prayer. In the Shafi'i school, the prayer would be invalid if Fatiha is omitted intentionally or forgotten.
This difference directly affects the worshipper's practice and the ruling on compensation.

Reciting Durood in the Final Sitting
Ruling on reciting durood in final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting durood in the final sitting and explain the evidence from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Durood in prayer is sunnah; the fard is fulfilled by reciting it once in a lifetime outside prayer.

In the Hanafi school, the act of sending blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ during the final sitting of salah is considered a recommended sunnah, not an obligatory component. This lesson clarifies the ruling, its proof from the Quran and Sunnah, and distinguishes the fard obligation from the sunnah practice within prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules about reciting durood in prayer. The act is reciting salutations upon the Prophet ﷺ in the final sitting (al-qa'dah al-akhirah). The ruling is that it is sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
Sunnah muakkadah is a confirmed recommended act, omission of which is disliked but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the main proof cited: Quran 33:56, which commands believers to send blessings upon the Prophet. The text explains that this command establishes the fard obligation to recite durood once in a lifetime, not repeatedly in every prayer.
The Hanafi usul principle: a general command (amr) indicates obligation, but the obligation can be fulfilled by a single instance.
3
Analyze the application within prayer
Understand why reciting durood in prayer is only sunnah: the fard is already discharged by a single recitation outside prayer. Within salah, it is a sunnah act that enhances the prayer but is not required for validity.
This distinction is based on the fact that the command in the verse is general (amm) and not repeated for each prayer.
4
Consider the hadith evidence
The passage begins to cite the hadith of Ka'b ibn Ujra, which teaches the specific wording for sending blessings. Even though the text is cut off, the hadith reinforces the recommended practice in prayer.
The hadith shows that the Companions asked how to send blessings, and the Prophet taught the formula, implying it is a meritorious act.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider reciting durood in the final sitting as a pillar (rukn) or wajib. The Hanafi view is that it is sunnah, which is a point of legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical consequence: if omitted in the Hanafi school, the prayer remains valid but is deficient; in the Shafi'i school, the prayer would require repetition.

Reciting Fatihah in the Latter Two Rak'ahs
States the sunnah of reciting Fatihah in third and fourth rak'ahs with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Fatihah in the third and fourth rak'ahs and explain the dalil.

Core Idea
Reciting Fatihah in the latter two rak'ahs is sunnah, not fard; omission is valid.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on reciting Surah al-Fatihah during the third and fourth rak'ahs of a fard prayer. The school distinguishes between the first two rak'ahs, where Fatihah is fard, and the latter two, where it is sunnah. We will look at the textual proofs and the reasoning behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in the third and fourth rak'ahs of a fard prayer. The Hanafi school rules it as sunnah (recommended), not fard (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: (1) the hadith from Abu Qatada showing the Prophet recited only Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs of Zuhr, and (2) the athar from Jabir ibn Samura where Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas says he shortens the last two rak'ahs following the Prophet's practice.
Both are from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet's actual practice (fi'l). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l indicates sunnah unless there is evidence raising it to wujub. Since there is no command for Fatihah in the latter rak'ahs, it remains sunnah.
This distinguishes between the first two rak'ahs where there is a command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text mentions that other imams (especially Imam al-Shafi'i) consider reciting Fatihah in every rak'ah as fard. Their proof includes general hadith like 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatihah' applied absolutely.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school restricts the general command to the first two rak'ahs based on the specific practice (fi'l) of the Prophet. This is a valid specification (takhsis) of the general by the specific sunnah.
The mufta bihi is the sunnah ruling: reciting Fatihah in latter rak'ahs is recommended but not obligatory.

Chapter on the Sunnas of Prayer: He raises it at negation and places it at affirmation (435). The term salat lexically: the thing with which tasbih is recited, meaning the index finger of the right hand, because with it tasbih is recited. Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof type. It states the Hanafi ruling that reciting Surah Fatihah in the third and fourth rak'ahs of a fard prayer is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory. If one omits it entirely, the prayer is still valid, but reciting it is better. The text notes that other imams (like al-Shafi'i) consider it fard. The author then provides two hadith proofs: the first from Abu Qatada showing the Prophet would recite only Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs, and the second from Jabir ibn Samura indicating shortening of the last two rak'ahs, understood as reciting only Fatihah. The Arabic heading 'يرفعها عند النفى' refers to a different sunnah (raising the finger in tashahhud), but the author's commentary reinterprets it or there is a numbering overlap. Focus is on the Fatihah ruling.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; omission is not sinful but meritorious to perform.
فاتحة (fatihah): The opening chapter of the Quran (Surah al-Fatihah), recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the Hanafi ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the third and fourth rak'ahs of a fard prayer?

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reciting Fatihah in the third and fourth rak'ahs is sunnah, not fard; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

Sending Blessings on the Prophet in the Final Sitting
States the sunnah of sending blessings in the final tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting durud in the final sitting and explain the evidence from Quran and Hadith that supports it as sunnah.

Core Idea
Sending blessings on the Prophet in the final sitting is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

This passage clarifies the ruling on reciting blessings (durud) upon the Prophet Muhammad in the final sitting of prayer. While the Quran commands sending blessings in general terms, the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice and specific hadiths, considers it sunnah in the context of prayer. Understanding this distinction is key to proper prayer performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses reciting durud upon the Prophet in the final sitting of prayer. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Examine the primary evidence
The Quranic verse (33:56) commands blessings, but the Hanafi school interprets it as general obligation; the specific context of prayer is governed by the Prophet's practice.
Also consider the hadiths: Ka'b ibn 'Ujra and Fadala ibn 'Ubayd.
3
Understand why it is sunnah, not fard
Although the verse's command is general (thubut qati, dalala zanni), the lack of evidence that the Prophet made it obligatory in prayer reduces it to sunnah.
The imperative form does not automatically make it fard in every context.
4
Note the practical implication
Omitting durud in the final sitting does not invalidate the prayer nor require compensation; it only diminishes the reward.
This distinguishes sunnah from fard/wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (٤٣٦) [٤٢] اخیر قعدہ میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھنا۔ تشریح : قعدہ اولی میں صرف تشہد پڑھ کر اٹھ جائے لیکن دور کعت کے بعد قعدہ اخیرہ ہو یا تین رکعت کے بعد یا چار رکعت کے بعد قعدہ آخیرہ ہو تو اس میں تشہد کے بعد درود شریف بھی پڑھے ، اور بعد میں قرآن وحدیث کے الفاظ سے اپنے لئے دعا بھی کرے، پھر سلام پھیرے۔ وجه (۱) نماز میں درود شریف سنت ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ ان الله و ملئكته يصلون على النبي يا أيها الذين آمنوا صلوا عليه وسلموا تسليما - ( آیت ۵۶ سورۃ الاحزاب ۳۳) اس آیت سے زندگی میں ایک مرتبہ درود پڑھنا فرض ہے اور نماز میں پڑھنا سنت ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔عـن كـعـب بـن عـجـرة . فقلنا قد عرفنا كيف نسلم علیک فکیف نــصــلــی علیک؟ قال قولوا اللهم صل على محمد الخ ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی النبی بعد التشهد ، ص ۱۷۳، نمبر ۹۰۸/۴۰۶ را بود و د شریف، باب الصلو علی النبی بعد التشہد، ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۹۷۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کے بعد حضور پر درود پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ (۳) انه سمع فضالة ابن عبيد يقول : سمع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم رجلا يدعو في صلوته فلم يصل على النبي الله فقال النبي علم : عجل هذا ، ثم دعاه ، فقال له أو لغيره : اذا صلى أحدكم فليبدأ بتحميدالله و الثناء عليه ، ثم ليصل على النبى الله ثم ليدع بعد ما شاء ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب في ايجاب الدعاء بتقديم الحمد والثناء والصلوة على النبي قبلہ، ص ۷۹۴، نمبر ۷ ۳۴۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تشہد کے بعد درود شریف پڑھے۔
Translation: (436) [42] Reciting blessings (durud) on the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the final sitting. Explanation: In the first sitting, one should recite only tashahhud and then stand up. But in the final sitting, whether after two rak'ahs, three, or four, one should recite tashahhud then also durud, and then make a supplication from Quran and hadith, then give salam. Proof: (1) The evidence that durud in prayer is sunnah is the verse: 'Indeed Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet. O you who believe, send blessings upon him and salute him with a worthy salutation.' (33:56) From this verse, sending blessings once in a lifetime is fard, and in prayer it is sunnah. (2) Hadith from Ka'b ibn 'Ujra: We said, 'We know how to greet you, but how do we send blessings?' He said: 'Say: O Allah send blessings upon Muhammad...' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that after tashahhud, one should send blessings on the Prophet. (3) He heard Fadala ibn 'Ubayd say: The Prophet heard a man making supplication in his prayer without sending blessings on the Prophet, so he said: 'This one hastened.' Then he called him and said: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with praise of Allah and exaltation, then send blessings on the Prophet, then make the supplication he wishes.' (Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that one should send blessings after tashahhud.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This ruling-with-proof passage discusses the sunnah of reciting durud (salutations) upon the Prophet in the final sitting of prayer. The author explains that in the first sitting, only tashahhud is recited, but in the final sitting, one should recite tashahhud, then durud, then a supplication from Quran/hadith, then salam. Three proofs are given: the Quranic verse (33:56) which makes sending blessings fard in general but sunnah in prayer; the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujra teaching the wording of durud; and the hadith of Fadala emphasizing that supplication should be preceded by praise and blessings. The Hanafi school holds this as sunnah, not fard, though some other schools may consider it wajib or fard.

Key Terms
درود (durud): Salutations and blessings sent upon the Prophet Muhammad, typically 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'.
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony recited in the sitting position of prayer, beginning with 'At-tahiyyatu lillahi'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting durud (blessings on the Prophet) in the final sitting?
A) It is fard (obligatory) and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is sunnah (recommended) and omitting it does not invalidate.
C) It is wajib and requires sajdah al-sahw if omitted.
D) It is makruh to recite it.

Key Takeaway
Reciting blessings on the Prophet in the final sitting is a recommended sunnah; omitting it does not affect the validity of the prayer.

Supplication Resembling Quran and Hadith, Not Human Speech
States that supplication in prayer must be in words resembling Quran and hadith, not human speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication in prayer, identify the proof from hadith, and apply the distinction between permissible and invalid supplications.

Core Idea
Supplication in prayer must resemble Quran and hadith; human speech invalidates it.

In this passage, the author clarifies a critical boundary: what kind of supplication (du'a) is valid during prayer. The Hanafi school draws a sharp line between permitted phrases from Quran and hadith and forbidden human speech (kalam al-nas). This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on supplication in prayer
Identify the core ruling: supplications must resemble Quran and hadith; using human speech (kalam al-nas) invalidates the prayer.
2
Identify the primary hadith proof
Locate the hadith of Mu'awiya ibn Hakam in the source: 'This prayer does not allow any human speech; it is only tasbih, takbir, and recitation of Quran.'
Sahih Muslim
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition of 'kalam al-nas' indicates that any utterance resembling ordinary conversation is invalid, including supplications not derived from Quran or hadith.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow any lawful supplication in any language, but Hanafi restricts to Quran/hadith phrasing to maintain the sanctity of prayer.
Mukhtalaf fih
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider a person who says in prayer: 'O Allah, help me pass this test.' Determine whether this resembles human speech and thus invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (٤٣٧) [٤٣] الفاظ قرآن وحدیث کے مشابہ دعا کرنا ، کلام الناس کے مشابہ نہیں۔
4: (۱) انسانی کلام کی دعا کرے گا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے ایسی دعانہ کرے جو انسانی کلام کے مشابہ ہو۔اس حدیث میں اسکا اشارہ ہے۔عن معاوية بن الحکم السلمي قال : بينا أنا اصلى مع رسول الله الله .... قال : ان هذه الصلوة لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس ، انما هو التسبيح و التكبير وقراءة القرآن (مسلم شریف باب تحريم الكلام في الصلوة و نسخ ما كان من اباحتہ ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۱۹۹/۵۳۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں کلام الناس نہ کرے۔ (۲) عن عبد الله قال اذا كنا مع النبي الله في الصلوة ... ثم ليتخير من الدعاء اعجبه اليه فيدعو . (بخارى شریف ، باب ما تخير من الدعاء بعد التشهد وليس بواجب، ص ۱۱۵ نمبر ۸۳۵ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب التشهد ،ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۹۶۸) (۳) عن عائشة زوج النبى الله الله اخبرته ان رسول الله الا الله كان يدعو في الصلوة اللهم انی اعوذبک من عذاب القبر ، الخ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الدعاء قبل السلام ص ۱۱۵ نمبر ۸۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سلام سے پہلے حدیث میں منقول دعائیں کرنی چاہئے۔
Translation: (437) [43] Supplicating with words resembling the Quran and hadith, not resembling human speech. (1) If one supplicates with human speech, the prayer becomes invalid. Therefore, one should not make a supplication that resembles human speech. There is an indication of this in the hadith from Mu'awiya ibn al-Hakam al-Sulami: 'While I was praying with the Messenger of Allah... he said: This prayer does not allow any human speech; it is only tasbih, takbir, and recitation of Quran.' (Muslim) This hadith shows one should not speak human speech in prayer. (2) From Abdullah: 'When we were with the Prophet in prayer... then let him choose the supplication that pleases him most and supplicate.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) (3) From Aisha that the Prophet used to supplicate in prayer: 'O Allah, I seek refuge in You from the punishment of the grave...' (Bukhari) This hadith shows that before salam, one should make supplications transmitted in hadith.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This ruling-with-proof passage concerns the nature of supplications (du'a) in prayer. According to the Hanafi school, one must avoid supplications that resemble human speech (kalam al-nas), as that would invalidate the prayer. Instead, supplications should be derived from the Quran or hadith or use similar phrasing. The author provides three hadith proofs: the first from Mu'awiya ibn Hakam establishes that prayer is sanctified from human speech; the second shows that the Prophet taught generic supplication after tashahhud; the third gives an example of the Prophet's own supplication. The ruling ensures that prayer remains distinct from ordinary conversation.

Key Terms
كلام الناس (kalam al-nas): Human speech that is customary between people, such as everyday conversation.
دعاء (du'a): Supplication made to Allah, especially in prayer after tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of supplication invalidates the prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) A supplication that is not from the Quran or hadith.
B) A supplication that resembles human speech (kalam al-nas).
C) A supplication in a language other than Arabic.
D) A supplication that asks for worldly things.

Key Takeaway
Supplication in prayer must avoid ordinary human speech; only phrases from Quran or hadith or similarly sanctified wording are valid.

Turning the Face During Salam: Wajib and Sunnah
Ruling on the salam method and its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the salam and distinguish between the wajib (one utterance) and the Sunnah (two utterances with turning).

Core Idea
One salam is wajib to exit the prayer; two salams with turning is Sunnah muakkadah.

The final salutation (salam) is the act that exits one from the state of prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the minimum obligation and the preferred method. This lesson examines that distinction and the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act discussed is the salam at the end of prayer: saying 'assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to exit.
The first utterance is wajib; the second and the turning are Sunnah.
2
Distinguish wajib from Sunnah
The passage explicitly states: 'saying one salam is wajib in itself' but two salams with turning is Sunnah.
This distinction is crucial for validity.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice: he would say two salams, turning right then left.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The description 'kana yusallim' (he used to say salam) indicates a continuous practice, which in Hanafi usul is evidence for Sunnah, not obligation.
Thus, the turning and second salam are recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۳۸) [۴۴] دونوں سلاموں میں دانے پھر بائیں طرف منھ پھیرنا۔ تشریح : بنفسہ ایک سلام کرنا واجب ہے۔ لیکن دو سلام کرے، اور پہلے سلام میں دائیں طرف منہ کرے اور دوسرے سلام سے بائیں طرف منہ کرے یہ سنت ہے۔ وجه (۱) عن عبد الله ان النبي علم كان يسلم عن يمينه وعن شماله حتى يرى بياض خده، السلام عليكم ورحمة الله ، السلام عليكم ورحمة الله (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی السلام ، ص ۱۵۱ نمبر ۹۹۶ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی التسلیم فی الصلوۃ ص ۷۹، نمبر ۲۹۵) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ سلام پھیرنا چاہئے اس طرح کہ کنارے والوں کو گال نظر آنے لگے۔
Translation: (438) [44] Turning the face right then left in the two salutations. Explanation: Saying one salam is obligatory in itself. But if he says two salams, and in the first salam he turns his face right and in the second salam he turns left, this is Sunnah. Evidence (1): From Abdullah [ibn Umar] that the Prophet used to say salam to his right and to his left until the whiteness of his cheek could be seen, 'Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah, peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on salam, p. 151, no. 996 / Tirmidhi, chapter on salam in prayer, p. 79, no. 295) This hadith establishes that one should turn when saying salam such that the people at the sides can see his cheek.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage discusses the method of the final salutation (salam) in prayer. The author states that saying one salam (the first) is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. However, performing two salams – first to the right and second to the left – is Sunnah. The proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice: he would say 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' turning his face so that the whiteness of his cheek was visible to those beside him. This establishes the recommendation of turning and saying two salams. The Urdu commentary explains the distinction: one salam is sufficient for validity (wajib), but two salams with turning is the recommended practice (Sunnah).

Key Terms
تسلیمة (taslimah): One utterance of 'assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' at the end of prayer
التفات (iltifat): Turning the face to the side during salam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum necessary (wajib) for the salam in prayer?
A) Two salams with turning
B) One salam without turning
C) One salam with turning
D) Two salams without turning

Key Takeaway
One salam is wajib to exit prayer; two salams with turning is Sunnah and follows the Prophet's practice.

Imam's Intention in Salam: Men, Angels, and Righteous Jinn
Ruling with proof on the imam's intention in salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of beings the imam should intend in salam and evaluate the evidence from the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah.

Core Idea
The imam's salam intention includes male followers, angels, and righteous jinn — a practice rooted in hadith.

When an imam makes the final salam, his intention is not limited to the human congregation. The Hanafi school teaches that the imam should also intend the guardian angels and the righteous jinn, who are present during prayer. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (the imam's intention in the final salam) and the hukm level (sunnah).
The ruling is recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah (Muslim, Abu Dawud).
The hadith instructs saying salam to 'your brother' on the right and left.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith supports the ruling: the word 'brother' implies an intended recipient; the imam should intend all those present, including angels and jinn based on other evidences.
The Hanafi interpretation extends the intention to unseen beings.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference among Hanafi narrations regarding including righteous jinn. The asahh (most correct) view includes them.
The text presents inclusion of jinn as the preferred position.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is to intend male followers, guardian angels, and righteous jinn.
This is based on the asahh narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۳۹) [۴۵] امام دونوں سلام کرتے وقت مردوں کی نیت کرے اور نگہبان فرشتوں کی نیت کرے، اور نیک جن کی نیت کرے اصح روایت میں۔ تشریح : امام دونوں سلام کرتے وقت جو مرد مقتدی ہیں ان کی نیت کرے، عورت کی نیت نہ کرے، کیونکہ اس میں فتنہ ہے، اور حفاظت کرنے والے جو فرشتے ہیں ان کی نیت کرے، اور اصح روایت یہ ہے کہ نیک جن کی بھی نیت کرے، کیونکہ نماز میں وہ بھی حاضر ہوتے ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن سمرة .... انما يكفى احدكم أن يضع يده على فخذه ، ثم يسلم على أخيه من على يمينه و شماله - (مسلم شریف، باب الامر بالسكون في الصلوة وانهى عن الاشارة باليد، ص ۱۸۱، نمبر ۴۳۱ ۹۷۰ر ابوداود شریف ، باب فی السلام ص ۱۵۲ نمبر ۹۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سلام میں دائیں اور بائیں جانب مقتدی کی نیت کرے۔ اور یہ سب لوگ امام کے مقتدی ہیں اس لئے ان سبھوں کی نیت کرے۔
Translation: (439) [45] The imam should intend men, guardian angels, and righteous jinn in the two salams, according to the most correct narration. Explanation: The imam, when making the two salams, should intend the male followers (muqtadis) – not women, because there is fitna in that – and he should intend the guardian angels, and the most correct narration is that he should also intend the righteous jinn, because they are also present in the prayer. Evidence (1): In the hadith, from Jabir ibn Samurah... 'It is sufficient for one of you to place his hand on his thigh, then say salam to his brother on his right and left.' (Muslim, chapter on command of stillness in prayer, p. 181, no. 431/970r; Abu Dawud, chapter on salam, p. 152, no. 998) This hadith indicates that in salam, he should intend the muqtadis on his right and left. And all these people are the imam's muqtadis, so he should intend all of them.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage addresses the imam's intention when performing the final salam. The author states that the imam should intend three categories: male followers (not female due to fitna), guardian angels (hafazah), and, according to the most correct (asahh) narration, righteous jinn. The reasoning is that jinn may also be present during prayer. The proof is from the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah, which mentions saying salam to 'your brother on your right and left' – implying the intention is for those present, including jinn. The Urdu commentary highlights the exclusion of women to avoid fitna; this reflects a conservative legal caution. The key point is that the imam's intention in salam is not just for the human congregation but also for unseen beings.

Key Terms
رجال (rijal): Male followers (muqtadis) of the imam
حفظة (hafazah): Guardian angels who record deeds and are present during prayer
صالح الجن (salih al-jinn): Righteous jinn who attend the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct narration (asahh), whom should the imam intend when making salam?
A) Only the male followers
B) Male followers and guardian angels only
C) Male followers, guardian angels, and righteous jinn
D) All followers including women and jinn

Key Takeaway
The imam's salam intention is a sunnah that extends to male followers, guardian angels, and righteous jinn, based on the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah.

Follower's Intention in Salam: Imam, Congregation, Angels, and Jinn
Ruling on follower's intention in salam: imam, congregation, angels, jinn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the persons the follower should intend in the final salam and apply the rule for intending the imam based on his position.

Core Idea
The follower intends the imam, congregation, angels, and jinn in salam; direction follows the imam's position.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah details the recommended intention (niyyah) of the follower (muqtadi) during the final salam of congregational prayer. The Hanafi school, based on prophetic hadith and the practice of the early generations, holds that the follower should intend to return the salam to the imam, to the fellow muqtadis, to the guardian angels (hafazah), and to the righteous jinn. The direction of intention depends on where the imam stands relative to the follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the silent intention of the follower during the final salam. The ruling is that it is recommended (sunnah) to intend the listed parties.
The intention does not affect the validity of the salam; it is a recommended act for greater reward.
2
List the intended parties
The text mentions four groups: the imam, the congregation (qawm, meaning male followers), the guardian angels (hafazah), and the righteous jinn (salih al-jinn).
The inclusion of angels and jinn highlights the unseen audience of the salam.
3
Determine the direction of intention based on imam's position
If the imam is to the follower's right, intend him when turning right; if to the left, intend when turning left; if directly in front, intend in both salams (right and left).
The athar of Hammad explains this in detail.
4
Analyze the evidence
The primary proof is the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub commanding to respond to the imam and to exchange salam among the congregation. The second evidence is the athar of Hammad providing positional guidance.
Both proofs are zanni (probable) in transmission but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The follower should silently intend these parties when saying the two salams (to the right and left). The specific intention for the imam follows his actual position.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position; there is no noted intra-Hanafi dispute.
