Translation: (440) [49] The muqtadi (follower) should intend his imam to whichever side his imam is, and if he is in front, he should intend him in both salams, along with the congregation, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn. Explanation: The muqtadi should intend his imam when turning to the side where the imam is; if the imam is exactly in front, he should intend him in both salams. And along with him, he should intend the other muqtadis, that he is saying salam to them, and he should intend the guardian angels and the righteous jinn. Evidence (1): The proof is this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub that he said: The Prophet commanded us to respond to the imam, and to love one another, and that some of us should say salam to others. (Abu Dawud, chapter on responding to the imam, p. 152, no. 1001?; Ibn Majah, chapter on responding to the imam, p. 131, no. 922) This hadith indicates that one should say salam to his imam as well. (2) In the athar: From Hammad that he said: If the imam is on your right, then when you say salam to the right, intend the imam in that; and if he is on your left, when you say salam to the left, intend the imam in that as well; and if he is in front of you, then say salam to him in your heart (silently), then say salam to your right and left. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on responding to the imam, vol. 2, p. 147, no. 3157) This athar indicates that if the imam is on the right, he should intend him on the right, and if on the left, intend him on the left.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage explains the intention of the follower (muqtadi) during the final salam. The follower should intend to return the salam to the imam, to the other muqtadis, to the guardian angels, and to the righteous jinn. The direction of intention depends on the imam's position: if the imam is to the follower's right, he intends him when turning right; if to the left, he intends him when turning left; if directly in front, he intends him in both salams (albeit silently for return). The proofs include: (1) the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub where the Prophet commanded returning salam to the imam and mutual salam among the congregation, and (2) the athar (statement of a tabi'i) of Hammad, which gives specific instructions for different imam positions. This detailed ruling shows the Hanafi concern for precise intention in worship.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): A follower praying behind an imam
قوم (qawm): The congregation of followers (muqtadis) behind the imam
حفظة (hafazah): Guardian angels, meaning the angels recording deeds or protecting
صالح الجن (salih al-jinn): Righteous jinn

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Intend the imam only when turning left

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends that the follower, when saying the final salam, intend the imam (according to his position), the congregation, guardian angels, and righteous jinn.

The Imam's Intention During the Two Salutations
Imam's intention during taslim: men, angels, jinn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of beings the imam should intend during the two salutations and identify the dalil from hadith.

Core Idea
The imam's intention during taslim includes male followers, guardian angels, and righteous jinn.

When the imam concludes the prayer with the two salams (taslimatayn), the intention behind those words matters. This lesson clarifies whom the imam should address: the male muqtadis, the guardian angels, and even the righteous jinn. We will explore the soundest narration and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's intention (niyyah) while performing the two salutations at the end of prayer. The ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) to intend specific beings.
The intention is not fard or wajib; the taslim itself is wajib.
2
Recognize the three intended categories
The imam should intend: (1) the male followers (muqtadis), (2) the guardian angels (al-hafazah), and (3) the righteous jinn (salih al-jinn). This is according to the asahh (soundest) narration.
Women are excluded to avoid fitna, though they may be present.
3
Understand the inclusion of jinn
Righteous jinn are included because they attend the prayer, as mentioned in the explanation. Not all narrations include them; the author opts for the sounder view that includes them.
The Shafi'i school does not require intention for jinn.
4
Examine the proof from hadith
The hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah (RA) states: 'It is sufficient for one of you to place his hand on his thigh and then say salam to his brother on his right and left.' The phrase 'his brother' implies the intention is directed to the fellow worshippers, which includes male muqtadis, angels, and jinn.
This hadith is sunnah ahad, zanni in transmission and meaning.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the imam's intention during the salutations at the end of prayer. The author states that the imam should intend three categories when giving the two salams: the male followers (not women, due to fitna), the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn. This is according to the soundest (asahh) narration. The proof cited is a hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah that mentions saluting the brother on the right and left, implying the intention of the muqtadis. The author also notes that jinn attend the prayer, so they should be included. The commentary follows the author's order, first presenting the ruling, then the explanation, then the proof.

Masbuq Waiting After the Imam's First Salam
Ruling on masbuq waiting after imam's first salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the masbuq waiting after the imam's first salam, explain the reason (sajdah al-sahw), and apply the ruling to a congregational prayer scenario.

Core Idea
The masbuq should wait after the imam's first salam to allow for possible sajdah al-sahw.

In congregational prayer, a latecomer (masbuq) often wonders when to stand up to complete missed rak'ahs. The imam's first salam may be a signal for sajdah al-sahw, not the final exit. This lesson clarifies the recommended waiting period and the evidence from a tabi'i's advice, ensuring the prayer remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the specific action being ruled upon: the masbuq waiting after the imam's first salam. Determine the hukm level from the text: it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
The text uses 'should not stand up immediately' implying recommendation, not obligation.
2
Understand the reason behind the ruling
The imam's first salam may be for sajdah al-sahw. If the masbuq stands immediately, he might miss the required prostration. The waiting ensures he can participate if needed.
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib in Hanafi fiqh; missing it without compensation affects prayer validity.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is an athar from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, a tabi'i, reported in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. He advises waiting 'a little' before standing.
In Hanafi usul, qawl al-tabi'i is a valid proof for non-obligatory acts (thubut and dalala are zanni).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a masbuq who misses one rak'ah. After the imam's first salam, he waits briefly. If the imam immediately performs a second salam, the masbuq stands. If the imam performs sajdah al-sahw, the masbuq joins, then stands.
The waiting period is short; the masbuq should not delay unnecessarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۴۵) وانتظار المسبوق فراغ الامام.
بائیں جانب سلام کرے۔
۲۹۹
ه فصل : في آدابها
فصل في اداب الصلوة
ترجمه : (۴۴۵) [۵۱] مسبوق امام کے فارغ ہونے کا انتظار کرے۔
تشریح : کسی کی رکعت چھوٹ گئی ہو اور وہ مسبوق بن گیا ہو تو امام کے پہلے سلام کے بعد فورا کھڑا نہیں ہونا چاہئے، کیونکہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ امام نے سجدہ سہو کرنے کے لئے یہ سلام کیا ہو، اور مسبوق کو بھی اس میں شرکت کرنی پڑے اس لئے دوسرا سلام کرے تب مسبوق کھڑا ہو۔
وجه : قلت لعطاء تفوتنى ركعة مع الامام فيسلم الامام فأقوم فأقضى أم انتظر ؟ قال : تنتظر قليلا فان حتبس فقم و دعه (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب متى يقوم الرجل منقضی مافاته اذا سلم الامام، ج ثانی ص ۱۴۷ نمبر ۳۱۶) اس قول
تابعی میں ہے کہ مسبوق کو تھوڑا انتظار کرنا چاہئے ۔
(445) And the waiting of the masbuq for the completion of the imam. He should do salam to the left side. Section: On its etiquettes. Section on etiquettes of prayer. Translation: (445) [51] The masbuq should wait for the imam to finish. Explanation: If someone missed a rak'ah and became a masbuq, he should not stand up immediately after the imam's first salam, because it is possible that the imam made that salam in order to perform sajdah al-sahw, and the masbuq would need to participate in that. Therefore, he should [wait until the imam] does the second salam, then the masbuq stands. Evidence: I said to 'Ata': 'I miss a rak'ah with the imam, so the imam says salam, should I stand up and make up [what I missed] or should I wait?' He said: 'Wait a little; if he stops, then stand and leave him.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on when a man stands up to complete what he missed after the imam's salam, vol. 2, p. 147, no. 316) In this statement of a tabi'i, it is stated that the masbuq should wait a little.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the situation of a masbuq (a latecomer who missed one or more rak'ahs of the congregational prayer). The ruling states that after the imam performs the first salam (to the right), the masbuq should not immediately stand up to complete his missed rak'ahs. Instead, he should wait briefly until the imam performs the second salam (to the left). The reason is that the imam may have made the first salam due to an oversight that necessitates sajdah al-sahw; if the masbuq stood up immediately, he might miss the required prostration with the imam. The proof is an athar from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, a tabi'i, reported in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. 'Ata' advises waiting a little after the imam's salam before standing. This waiting period ensures the masbuq can join the imam in sajdah al-sahw if needed. The Hanafi position follows this principle, emphasizing caution to preserve the validity of the prayer.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer, such as omission of a wajib or delay in a rukn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A masbuq should wait after the imam's first salam to allow for possible sajdah al-sahw, ensuring his prayer is complete.

Mustahabbat (Recommended Acts) in Prayer: List and Proofs
List of ten recommended acts with proofs for first two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten mustahabbat of prayer and explain the Hanafi evidence for removing hands from sleeves at takbir and directing the gaze during prayer.

Core Idea
Mustahabbat enhance khushu' but are not obligatory; omitting them does not invalidate prayer.

Prayer has layers of perfection beyond its obligatory elements (fard) and necessary elements (wajib). The Hanafi school identifies a set of recommended acts (mustahabbat) that cultivate humility and focus (khushu'). In this passage, we learn the ten recommended acts and the detailed proofs for the first two: removing hands from sleeves at takbir and fixing the gaze on the place of prostration. Understanding these acts deepens our appreciation of the Prophet's practice and our own prayer experience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that these acts are mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) — recommended, not obligatory. The passage explicitly says omitting them is not harmful.
Mustahabb = reward for doing, no sin for leaving.
2
List the ten acts
Read the list: (1) remove hands from sleeves at takbir; (2) look at place of prostration during qiyam; (3) during ruku' look at back of feet; (4) during sujud look at tip of nose; (5) during qa'dah look at lap; (6) during salam look at shoulders; (7) suppress cough when possible; (8) close mouth when yawning; (9) stand up at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in iqamah; (10) imam starts at 'qad qamat al-salah'.
The pattern: direct the gaze to the appropriate spot for each posture.
3
Analyze the proof for removing hands (first mustahabb)
Two pieces of evidence: (a) Hadith of Wa'il ibn Hajar showing the Prophet took his hands out of his garment before ruku'; by analogy (qiyas), the same should be done at takbir. (b) Athar of Abu Qilabah that he removed his hands from his garment during sujud; again analogized to takbir. The common illa (effective cause) is the need for full raising of hands without obstruction.
The analogy from ruku' and sujud to takbir is a jali (clear) qiyas.
4
Analyze the proof for directing gaze (second mustahabb)
Two evidences: (a) Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim severely prohibiting raising eyes to the sky during prayer, implying gaze should be down. (b) Practice of Muhammad ibn Sirin (narrated in Bayhaqi) to keep gaze on the place of prostration, derived from the revelation of the khushu' verse. The proof establishes that looking at the place of prostration is the recommended norm.
The prohibition of looking around is strong, reinforcing the recommended act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ضروری نوٹ : مستحبات کا مطلب ہے کہ کرے تو بہتر ہے اور نہ کرے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے
ترجمه : (۴۴۶) [۱] تکبیر کے وقت مرد آستین سے اپنے دونوں ہاتھ نکال لیوے۔
تشریح : ہاتھ آستین کے اندر ہوگا تو پورے طور پر نہیں اٹھا سکے گا، اوراللہ کی بڑائی بھی پورے طور پر نہیں ہو سکے گی ، اس لئے اگر ہاتھ آستین کے اندر ہو یا کپڑے کے اندر ہو تو اس کو نکال لے۔
وجه : عن وائل بن حجر انه رأى النبى الله رفع يديه حين دخل في الصلاة كبر ـ وصف همام حيال اذنيه ثم التحف بثوبه ثم وضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى فلما اراد ان يركع اخرج يديه من الثوب ثم رفعهما ) مسلم شریف ، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری بعد تکبیرة الاحرام الخ ص۱۷۰، نمبر ۱۸۹۶/۴۰۱ ابوداود شریف، باب رفع الیدین فی الصلاۃ ، ص ۱۱۳، نمبر ۷۲۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رکوع کے وقت ہاتھ نکالتے تھے ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آستین لمبی ہو تو تکبیر کے وقت ہاتھ آستین سے نکالے۔ (۲) اس قول ان ابا قلابہ کان اذا اسجد خرج ید یہ من ثوبه (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من كان يخرج ید یہ اذا سجد ، ج اول ص ۲۳۹، نمبر ۲۷۴۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ سجدے کے وقت ہاتھ نکالے، اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے تکبیر کے وقت ہاتھ باہر کرے۔ یہ آداب میں سے ہے۔ کم : آستین ۔ ترجمه : (۴۴۷) [۲] اور مصلی قیام کے وقت سجدہ کی جگہ نظر رکھے۔ [۳] اور رکوع کرتے وقت قدم کے ظاہری حصے پر ۔ [۴] اور سجدہ میں ناک کے سرے پر۔ تشریح : اصل قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ نماز پڑھتے وقت ادھر ادھر نہ دیکھے ، اور سجدے کی جگہ پر نظر رکھے تاکہ خشوع خضوع زیادہ سے زیادہ پیدا ہو سکے۔ اس لئے قیام کی حالت میں سجدے کی جگہ پر نظر رکھے، اور رکوع کی حالت میں قدم کے ظاہری حصے پر نظر رکھے۔ اور سجدے کی حالت میں ناک کے سرے پر نگاہ رکھے۔ وجه : (۱) ادھر ادھر نہ دیکھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے. ان انس بن مالک حدثه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما بال
صلى الله
اقوام يرفعون أبصارهم الى السماء في صلاتهم ؟ فاشتد قوله فی ذالک حتی قال لينتهين عن ذالک او
لـتـخـطـفـن ابصارهم ـ ( بخاری شریف، باب رفع البصر الى السماء فی الصلاۃ، ص ۱۲۲، نمبر ۷۵۰ مسلم شریف ، باب انھی عن رفع البصر الى السماء في الصلاة، ص ۱۸۳ نمبر ۹۶۶/۴۲۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں نگاہ ادھر ادھر نہیں کرنی چاہئے ۔ (۲) سجدے کی جگہ پر نظر ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے . عن محمد قال نبئت ان رسول الله الله كان اذا صلى رفع بصره الى السماء فنزلت آية ان لم تكن الذين هم في صلاتهم خاشعون ، فلا ادری ای آیة هي فكان محمد بن سيرين يحب ان لا يجاوز بصره مصلاه - (سنن بیہقی ، باب لا یجاوز بصره موضع سجوده ، ج ثانی ، ص ۴۰۲، نمبر ۳۵۴۱) اس
Section: On the etiquettes of prayer. The mustahabbat (recommended acts) of prayer: (10) ten are these: At takbir the man should take out both his hands from his sleeves. And the praying person should look at the place of prostration during qiyam. During ruku' at the apparent part of the foot. … And during sujud at the tip of the nose. And during qa'dah in his lap. And during salam at the shoulders. … And within capacity, suppress a cough. And when yawning, close the mouth. And stand up at the time of saying 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the iqamah. And when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said, the imam should start the prayer. Thamaratun Najah vol. 1 300 Fasl fi adab al-salah (446) Among its etiquettes is that a man takes out his palms from his sleeves at takbir. (447) And the praying person's looking at the place … Important note: Mustahabbat means that if one does it, it is better, and if one does not do it, there is no harm. Translation: (446) [1] At takbir the man should take out both his hands from his sleeves. Explanation: If the hand is inside the sleeve, he cannot raise it fully, and the glorification of Allah will not be complete. Therefore, if the hand is inside the sleeve or inside the garment, one should take it out. Evidence: From Wa'il ibn Hajar that he saw the Prophet (SAW) raise his hands when he entered the prayer and said Allahu Akbar – Hammam described: parallel to his ears, then he wrapped himself in his garment, then placed his right hand on his left. When he wanted to bow, he took out his hands from the garment and then raised them. (Muslim, chapter on placing right hand on left after takbirat al-ihram etc., p.170, no.1896/401; Abu Dawud, chapter on raising hands in prayer, p.113, no.723). In this hadith it is that he would take out his hands at ruku', from which it is understood that if the sleeve is long, he should take out his hands from the sleeve at takbir. (2) This statement: that Abu Qilabah would when he prostrated take out his hands from his garment (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who would take out their hands when prostrating, vol.1 p.239, no.2740). In this athar it is that he took out his hands at sajdah; by analogy, one should take out the hands at takbir. This is among the etiquettes. (447) [2] And the praying person looks at the place of prostration during qiyam. [3] And during ruku' at the apparent part of the foot. [4] And during sujud at the tip of the nose. Explanation: The basic rule is not to look around while praying, and to keep the gaze on the place of prostration so that khushu' and khudu' can be maximally achieved. Therefore, during qiyam one looks at the place of prostration; during ruku' at the apparent part of the foot; and during sujud at the tip of the nose. Evidence: (1) For not looking around, there is this hadith: Anas ibn Malik reported that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) said: 'What is the matter with people who raise their eyes to the sky during prayer?' And he spoke strongly about that until he said: 'They must cease doing that or their eyesight will be snatched away.' (Bukhari, chapter on raising the eyes to the sky in prayer, p.122, no.750; Muslim, chapter on prohibition of raising the eyes to the sky in prayer, p.183, no.966/428). This hadith indicates that one should not look around in prayer. (2) For looking at the place of prostration, there is this hadith: From Muhammad, he said: I was informed that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) used to raise his gaze to the sky when he prayed, then the verse was revealed – 'unless they are those who are humble in their prayers' – I do not know which verse it was. So Muhammad ibn Sirin liked that one's gaze should not go beyond his place of prostration. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on not letting one's gaze go beyond the place of prostration, vol.2 p.402, no.3541). This...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It lists ten mustahabbat (recommended acts) in prayer, which enhance khushu' but are not obligatory. The list is: (1) at takbir, a man takes his hands out from his sleeves; (2) during qiyam, look at the place of prostration; (3) during ruku', look at the back of the feet; (4) during sujud, look at the tip of the nose; (5) during qa'dah, look at the lap; (6) during salam, look at the shoulders; (7) suppress a cough as much as possible; (8) close the mouth when yawning; (9) stand up when the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-falah' during iqamah; (10) the imam begins when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said. The text then elaborates on the first two with proofs. For the first, the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hajar shows the Prophet (SAW) removing his hands from his garment before ruku', analogically applied to takbir. The athar of Abu Qilabah also shows removing hands at sujud, further supporting the analogy. For the second, the hadith against raising eyes to the sky (from Bukhari and Muslim) establishes the prohibition of looking around, and the practice of Muhammad ibn Sirin (narrated in Bayhaqi) specifies keeping the gaze on the place of prostration. The underlying principle is maximising khushu' by directing the gaze appropriately during each posture. All these are mustahabbat: doing them earns reward, omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
مستحبات (mustahabbat): Recommended acts in prayer; doing them is meritorious, omitting them is not sinful.
خشوع (khushu'): Humility, attentiveness, and calmness in prayer; a desired state enhanced by mustahabbat.
آداب (adab): Etiquettes or recommended conduct; in this context, mustahabbat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on looking at the place of prostration during prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is haram (forbidden).

Key Takeaway
The ten mustahabbat of prayer enhance focus and humility, and their evidence from hadith and qiyas shows the depth of Hanafi fiqh in perfecting worship.

Removing Hands from Sleeves at Takbir: A Recommended Etiquette
Ruling on adab of taking hands out of sleeves during takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hukm of removing hands from sleeves at takbir and identify the evidence (hadith and qiyas) that supports it.

Core Idea
Removing hands from sleeves at takbir is mustahabb—not wajib—to enable full glorification of Allah.

This lesson introduces the first ruling in the section on the etiquettes of prayer (adab al-salah). Many students may think that any action related to the hands in prayer is strictly obligatory. However, the text clarifies that this act is only recommended. Understanding the level of hukm (mustahabb vs. wajib) is essential to avoid unnecessary rigidity or invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, clearly identify the action being ruled upon: a man taking out his hands from his sleeves at the opening takbir. Then note the ruling: it is 'adab' (etiquette) and 'mustahabb' (recommended). This means it is better to do it, but omitting it does not incur sin or require repetition.
2
Locate the primary dalil (evidence)
The text provides two evidences: a hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr showing the Prophet removing his hands at ruku', and an athar of Abu Qilabah removing his hands at prostration. These are not directly about takbir, so the author uses qiyas (analogy) to apply the same rule to takbir.
The hadith is classified as zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
The illa (effective cause) is the need to fully raise the hands for glorification. Since raising hands at takbir and ruku' share this cause, the same recommendation applies to takbir by analogy. This is a clear (jaliyyah) qiyas.
The athar of Abu Qilabah provides additional support but is not necessary for the ruling.
4
Confirm the hukm level and its implications
The text explicitly labels this as 'adab' and 'mustahabbat'. In Hanafi fiqh, this equates to sunnah ghayr muakkadah or mandub. It does not affect the validity of the prayer if omitted. Recognizing this distinction prevents the common error of treating recommend acts as obligatory.

(۴۴۶) من آدابها اخراج الرجل كفيه من كميه عند التكبير

ترجمه : (۴۴۶) [۱] تکبیر کے وقت مرد آستین سے اپنے دونوں ہاتھ نکال لیوے۔
تشریح : ہاتھ آستین کے اندر ہوگا تو پورے طور پر نہیں اٹھا سکے گا، اوراللہ کی بڑائی بھی پورے طور پر نہیں ہو سکے گی ، اس لئے اگر ہاتھ آستین کے اندر ہو یا کپڑے کے اندر ہو تو اس کو نکال لے۔

Chapter on the etiquettes of prayer. (446) Among its etiquettes: a man removes his hands from his sleeves at the time of takbir. Important note: 'mustahabbat' means if one does it, it is better; if one does not, there is no harm. Translation: (446) [1] At the time of takbir, a man should take out both his hands from his sleeves. Explanation: If the hand is inside the sleeve, one cannot raise it completely, and the glorification of Allah will not be complete. Therefore, if the hand is inside the sleeve or inside the cloth, he should take it out. Evidence: From Wa'il ibn Hujr that he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) raise his hands when entering the prayer, he said takbir... (then mention of raising hands at ruku) This hadith indicates that he would take out his hands at the time of ruku, from which it is understood that if the sleeve is long, one should take out the hands from the sleeves at the time of takbir. (2) The statement that Abu Qilabah, when he prostrated, would take his hands out from his garment (Ibn Abi Shaybah)... This athar indicates that he would take out his hands at the time of prostration, and by analogy, one should take out the hands at the time of takbir. This is among the etiquettes. 'Kumm': sleeve.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage begins the section on the etiquettes of prayer (adab al-salah). It first gives a general note that 'mustahabbat' (recommended acts) are those which if performed are better, but omission is not sinful. Then it presents ruling 446: It is mustahabb for a man to take his hands out of his sleeves when raising them for the opening takbir. The commentary explains the wisdom: to enable full raising of the hands and complete expression of Allah's greatness. The author then provides two pieces of evidence: first, a hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud that the Prophet ﷺ took his hands out of his garment when raising them for ruku'; by analogy, the same applies at takbir. Second, an athar from Abu Qilabah who took out his hands during prostration, further supporting the practice. The ruling is explicitly categorized as adab, not wajib.

Key Terms
اداب الصلوة (adab al-salah): Etiquettes of prayer; recommended actions that enhance khushu' and completeness of salah, but are not obligatory.
مستحبات (mustahabbat): Recommended acts; performing them is better, omitting them is not sinful.

Key Takeaway
Removing hands from sleeves at takbir is a recommended etiquette (mustahabb) that enhances glorification but is not required for the prayer's validity.

Where to Look During Prayer: The Adab of the Gaze
Ruling on where to direct the gaze in different postures of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where to look during each posture of prayer and identify the proofs that establish it as mustahabb.

Core Idea
The gaze in prayer follows the posture: prostration spot when standing, back of feet when bowing, tip of nose when prostrating.

This lesson explains the recommended (mustahabb) positions for the worshiper's gaze during the various postures of prayer. Controlling the gaze is a key component of khushu' (heartfelt concentration) and is established by the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the early Muslims. While not obligatory, it greatly enhances the quality of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (directing the gaze in prayer) and its legal category (mustahabb/sunnah ghayr muakkadah). Note that it is a recommended etiquette, not a condition of validity.
The text uses 'ينظر' (looks at) as a recommendation, not a command.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
Find the proofs cited: (1) Hadith from Anas in Bukhari/Muslim warning against raising eyes to the sky, (2) Mursal hadith in Bayhaqi linking the revelation of the khushu' verse, (3) Practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
These are ahad hadith and athar, establishing recommendation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof indicate the ruling? The first prohibits wandering gaze; the second shows the Prophet's practice after revelation; the third shows a tabi'i's preference.
Together they demonstrate it is praiseworthy to restrain the gaze.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school has no internal disagreement on this; it is considered mustahabb. No dispute is mentioned in the text.
Some other schools may have similar or different emphasis, but here it is clear.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that for each posture a specific gaze point is recommended: standing (sajdah place), bowing (back of feet), prostrating (nose tip). Not following this does not invalidate prayer but reduces perfection.
This is from the chapter of adab, not invalidators.

ترجمه : (۴۴۷) [۲] اور مصلی قیام کے وقت سجدہ کی جگہ نظر رکھے۔ [۳] اور رکوع کرتے وقت قدم کے ظاہری حصے پر ۔ [۴] اور سجدہ میں ناک کے سرے پر۔

(447) The worshiper's gaze: when standing, towards the place of prostration; when bowing, towards the back of the foot; when prostrating, towards the tip of the nose. Translation: (447) [2] The worshiper, while standing, looks at the place of prostration. [3] While bowing, looks at the outer part of the foot. [4] While prostrating, looks at the tip of the nose. Explanation: The basic rule is that during prayer one should not look around. Looking at the place of prostration increases khushu' and khudu'. Therefore, while standing, look at the place of prostration; while bowing, look at the upper part of the foot; while prostrating, look at the nose tip. Evidence: (1) Not looking around: hadith from Anas that the Prophet ﷺ said, 'What is the matter with people who raise their eyes to the heaven in prayer?' He spoke strongly until he said, 'They must desist or their eyesight will be snatched away.' (Bukhari, Muslim). (2) For looking at the place of prostration: a mursal hadith that the Prophet used to raise his eyes to heaven until the verse about khushu' was revealed, then he kept his gaze below. (Bayhaqi). (3) From Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that he liked the worshiper not to let his gaze go beyond his place of prostration (Ibn Abi Shaybah).
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This lesson covers the second major adab: directing the gaze during prayer. The author first states the ruling: while standing (qiyam), look at the place of prostration; while bowing (ruku'), look at the back of the feet; while prostrating (sujud), look at the tip of the nose. The explanation emphasizes khushu' (heartfelt humility) and the need to avoid distraction. Three evidences are provided: first, a well-known hadith warning against raising eyes to the sky; second, a mursal hadith about the revelation of the verse on khushu' (which caused the Prophet to lower his gaze); third, the practice of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. The ruling is adab/mustahabb, not wajib.

Key Terms
خشوع (khushu'): Heartfelt humility and concentration in prayer, enhanced by controlling the gaze.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should the worshiper look while bowing (ruku')?
A) At the place of prostration
B) At the back of the feet
C) At the tip of the nose
D) At the lap

Key Takeaway
Directing the gaze according to the prayer posture is a recommended sunnah that enhances khushu', but its absence does not invalidate the prayer.

Gaze During Sitting and Salam in Hanafi Prayer
Ruling with proof for gaze during sitting and salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) positions for the gaze during sitting and salam in Hanafi prayer, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, gaze follows action: lap when sitting, shoulder when salam.

This lesson completes the adab of gaze in prayer. The author specifies where to direct the eyes during the sitting postures (jalsah and tashahhud) and during the salam, emphasizing khushu'. The ruling is mustahabb, supported by a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for sitting
When sitting in prayer (whether jalsah or tashahhud), look at your lap (hijr). This is mustahabb.
The text applies to all sitting postures, not just tashahhud.
2
State the ruling for salam
When turning for salam to the right and left, look at the corresponding shoulder (mankib).
3
Identify the evidence
The hadith from Nasa'i: the Prophet's gaze did not go beyond his pointing finger during tashahhud, indicating his eyes were fixed on his finger near the lap.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Extract the legal principle
The gaze should be directed to the area of the action to maintain concentration (khushu').
This principle also applies to other postures (e.g., looking at the place of sujud while standing).
5
Apply the ruling
The practice is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah). Omitting it does not invalidate prayer, but following it earns reward and enhances khushu'.

Suppressing Cough and Yawning During Prayer
Ruling on adab of controlling cough and yawning during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on suppressing cough and yawning during salah and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Suppressing cough and yawn in prayer is recommended adab, not an obligation.

In prayer, maintaining khushu' is essential. Involuntary actions like coughing and yawning can disrupt focus. This lesson explains the recommended etiquettes for handling these situations, supported by a hadith from Sahih Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
Recognize that coughing and yawning during prayer are involuntary acts. The ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to suppress them, not wajib.
The text mentions both acts, but only yawning has a direct hadith; cough is addressed by general adab.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith from Abu Hurairah (reported by Muslim) states that yawning is from Shaytan and commands suppression. Analyze the imperative 'falyakzim'.
The hadith is ahad, zanni in transmission and indication.
3
Understand the Hanafi interpretation
The Hanafi school interprets the imperative as a recommendation (nadb) because the act is involuntary and suppressing it is a means to avoid imitating Shaytan.
This avoids making the ruling wajib, which would be burdensome for involuntary actions.

This is adab/mustahabb; failure to do so is not sinful but reduces the perfection of prayer.

Standing at Hayya 'ala al-Falah
Ruling on standing during iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommended timing for the congregation to stand during iqamah and distinguish the two Hanafi interpretations.

Core Idea
Stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' – the call to success is the cue to rise.

In congregational prayer, the iqamah signals that prayer is about to begin. But when exactly should the followers stand? This lesson presents the Hanafi view, which ties the moment of standing directly to the phrase 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' (Come to success). We will explore the reasoning and a subtle difference among Hanafi scholars on this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the standing of the congregation before the imam begins the prayer. Determine its legal status (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.).
The ruling here is sunnah ghayr muakkadah, a recommended practice.
2
Locate the specific timing recommended
From the source, find the exact moment the followers should stand: at the phrase 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah' in the iqamah.
This is based on the idea that the mu'adhdhin is calling to prayer, and standing is a response.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
The source mentions two interpretations: one is to stand shortly after the iqamah begins but before 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah'; the other is to stand exactly at that phrase.
Both are present in Hanafi practice, but the latter is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text indicates by 'they say' that the predominant view is to stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah'. Confirm that this is the operative ruling for fatwa.

The author notes that among Hanafis, there are two views: one is to stand after the start of iqamah but before 'Hayya 'ala al-Falah', the other is to stand exactly at that phrase. Looking at Place of Sajdah During Prayer
Ruling on where to look while standing, bowing, and prostrating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where to direct the gaze during standing, bowing, and prostration, and identify the evidence for this sunnah.

Core Idea
The gaze in prayer follows the act: standing – place of sajdah, bowing – back of feet, prostrating – tip of nose.

In the Hanafi school, the placement of the eyes during prayer is not arbitrary—it is a sunnah that aids concentration (khushu). This passage details the recommended gaze for each posture and supports it with a mursal hadith and the practice of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Understanding this etiquette helps you enhance the quality of your salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text describes where to look during three postures: standing, bowing, and prostrating. Determine the hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.).
The ruling is sunnah ghayr muakkadah—recommended but not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a mursal hadith and a saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Identify the type of evidence and its transmission strength.
The dalil is a mursal hadith (zanni al-thubut) and a tabi'i qawl, which together establish a recommended practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the evidence proves the ruling. The phrase 'kan yuhibbu' (he liked) indicates istihbab (recommendation).
The evidence does not use imperative language, so it cannot indicate wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Although the Hanafi school emphasizes this sunnah for khushu, some other schools may hold different positions. Understand that this is a matter of etiquette, not obligation.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih, but the Hanafi position is consistent.

Timing of Standing for Congregational Prayer
Ruling on when followers should stand for the congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on when followers should stand during iqamah, and apply the preferred view with supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Standing at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' is recommended, but earlier standing is also permissible—flexibility is key.

The simple matn 'وَالْقِيَامُ حِينَ قِيلَ' (and standing when it is said) opens a nuanced discussion on the exact moment followers should rise for prayer. The commentary clarifies that the time is linked to the phrase 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the iqamah, but Hanafi scholars have differed on whether to stand exactly at that phrase or from the beginning of iqamah. This lesson unpacks the proofs for both positions and emphasizes that the matter is one of etiquette, not strict obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The ruling concerns the act of standing by the followers (muqtadin) during the iqamah for congregational prayer. Determine what is being ruled upon.
This is a sunnah-related ruling, not fard or wajib.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
The text presents two opinions within the Hanafi school: (1) stand from the start of iqamah until before 'hayya 'ala al-falah', and (2) stand exactly at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. List them clearly.
Both opinions are considered valid; the difference is a matter of preference.
3
Examine the hadith proofs for each
For the first opinion (earlier standing), the text cites hadith from Abu Hurayra and al-Bara' showing companions standing before the Prophet reached his place. For the second opinion (standing exactly at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'), it cites a statement of al-Hasan al-Basri. Compare the strength of these proofs.
The hadith of al-Bara' is particularly strong; it shows standing long before takbir.
4
Understand the preferred view
The text does not decisively prefer one opinion but notes that the first opinion (standing earlier) is more commonly practiced and supported by multiple hadith. Identify which evidence is given more weight.
The command to stand only upon seeing the imam (in the hadith of Abu Qatada) is interpreted as a recommendation for order, not a restriction.
5
Note the emphasis on flexibility
The commentary explicitly states 'These are etiquettes, so no group should be strict about it.' Recognize that the ruling is not rigid; both positions are acceptable.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of facilitating ease in non-obligatory matters.

والقيام حين قيل (۴۵۰) ترجمه : (۴۵۰) (۹) اور تکبیر میں جی علی الفلاح، کہنے کے وقت کھڑا ہو۔ تشریح : امام جب تک نماز پڑھانے کے لئے تیار نہ ہو تکبیر نہ کہے، کیونکہ اس سے مقتدی کو بلا وجہ انتظار کرنا پڑے گا۔ لیکن اگر امام امامت کے لئے تیار ہو اور مصلے پر ہو تو فرماتے ہیں کہ جی علی الفلاح پر مقتدی کھڑے ہو جائیں، کیونکہ موذن نماز کی طرف بلا رہا ہے ۔ ۔ حنفیوں کے یہاں جی علی الفلاح، پر کھڑا ہونے کا دو مطلب لئے ہیں، ایک یہ کہ اقامت شروع ہونے کے بعد جی علی الفلاح، سے پہلے تک کھڑا ہوتا رہے، البتہ اس سے تاخیر نہ کرے، ایک جماعت اسی پر عمل کرتی ہے، اس جماعت کی حدیث نیچے آرہی ہے ۔ دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جی علی الفلاح، سے پہلے کوئی مقتدی کھڑا نہ ہو، ٹھیک جی علی الفلاح، پر ہی کھڑا ہو، اور اس سے تاخیر نہ کرے۔ دوسری جماعت اس طرف گئی ہے۔۔۔ یہ آداب ہیں اس لئے کسی جماعت کو اس پر تشدد نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ وجه : (۱) امام جب تک مصلی پر آنے کے لئے تیار نہ ہو تو اقامت نہ کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة عن ابيه قال قال رسول الله اذا اقيمت الصلوة فلا تقوموا حتى ترونی ۔(بخاری شریف، باب منی لقوم الناس اذا رأوا الامام عند الاقامة؟ ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۶۳۷ / مسلم شریف ، باب متى يقوم الناس للصلاة، ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۳۹۵/۶۰۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام نماز کے لئے تیار ہوتب ہی مقتدی کھڑے ہوں چاہے اقامت کہی جا چکی ہو ۔ (۲) جی علی الفلاح، سے پہلے کھڑا ہوتار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے . عن ابي هريرة ان الصلاة كانت تقام لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيأخذ الناس مصافهم قبل ان يقوم النبى الله مقامه - (مسلم شریف ، باب متى يقوم الناس للصلاة ص ۲۴۵، نمبر ۱۳۶۹/۶۰۵ و ابوداود شریف، باب فی الصلاة تقام ولم يأت الامام بينظر ونحو قعودا ص ۹۰ نمبر ۵۴) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ آپ مصلی پر جاتے اس سے پہلے اقامت کہی جاتی اور لوگ نماز کے لئے کھڑے بھی ہو جاتے ۔ (۳) عن البراء بن عاذب قال كنا نقوم في الصفوف على عهد رسول الله طويلا قبل ان يكبر ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب فی الصلاة تقام ولم يأت الامام بينظر ونحو قعودا ص ۹۰، نمبر ۵۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تکبیر سے بہت پہلے لوگ کھڑے ہو جاتے ۔ (۴) جو حضرات حی علی الصلوۃ پر کھڑے ہونے کے قائل ہیں انکی دلیل یہ قول تابعی ہے . عن الحسن انه كره ان يقوم الامام حتى يقول المؤذن قد قامت الصلوة ( مصنف ابن ابی شيبه ، باب من قال اذا قال المؤذن قد قامت الصلوة فلتقم ، ج اول ص ۳۵۶، نمبر ۴۰۹۹ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قد قامت الصلوۃ ، پر ہی کھڑا ہو۔
And standing when it is said. (450) Translation: (450) (9) And with the takbir, he should stand at the time of saying 'hayya 'ala al-falah'. Explanation: The imam should not say the takbir until he is ready to lead, because otherwise the followers would have to wait unnecessarily. But if the imam is ready and on his prayer mat, they say that the followers should stand at 'hayya 'ala al-falah', because the mu'adhdhin is calling to the prayer. Among Hanafis, there are two meanings of standing at 'hayya 'ala al-falah': one is to stand from the beginning of iqamah until before 'hayya 'ala al-falah', not delaying beyond that; one group acts upon this, their hadith comes below. The second meaning is that no follower should stand before 'hayya 'ala al-falah', but exactly at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' they stand, and do not delay thereafter. Another group takes this position... These are etiquettes, so no group should be strict about it. Evidence: (1) The imam should not say iqamah until he is ready to go to the prayer place; this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father that the Messenger of Allah said, 'When the iqamah is called, do not stand until you see me.' (Bukhari and Muslim) This hadith says that the followers should stand only when the imam is ready, even if iqamah has been said. (2) That one stands before 'hayya 'ala al-falah' is evidenced by this hadith: from Abu Hurayra that the prayer used to be setup for the Messenger of Allah and the people would take their rows before the Prophet stood at his place. (Muslim and Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that iqamah was said before the Prophet went to his place and people would stand for prayer. (3) From al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: We used to stand in rows during the time of the Messenger of Allah for a long time before he said takbir. (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that people would stand long before the takbir. (4) Those who advocate standing at 'hayya 'ala al-salah' have as proof the statement of the tabi'i: from al-Hasan that he disliked the imam standing until the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah'. This athar says to stand at 'qad qamat al-salah'.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This is a detailed discussion on when the followers (muqtadin) should stand for congregational prayer. The matn says simply to stand when 'it is said' (i.e., during iqamah). The commentary explains that the proper time is at 'hayya 'ala al-falah', but there are two opinions among Hanafis: first, to stand from the start of iqamah until before that phrase; second, to stand exactly at that phrase. The strongest opinion, based on multiple hadith, is that followers may stand before the imam appears, as long as they are not causing disturbance. However, the text emphasizes that these are etiquettes and not to be made a cause of strictness. The hadith cited show various practices: some indicate standing when seeing the imam, others show standing before the imam comes. All are permissible as long as khushu' is maintained.

Key Terms
حي على الفلاح (hayya 'ala al-falah): A phrase in the iqamah meaning 'come to success'.
مقتدي (muqtadī): Follower in the congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what is the ruling on when followers should stand for congregational prayer?
A) They must stand exactly at 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
B) They must stand only when they see the imam.
C) They may stand at 'hayya 'ala al-falah' or earlier; both are acceptable.
D) They must stand at the beginning of the iqamah.

Key Takeaway
The timing for followers to stand during iqamah is a matter of adab with two valid Hanafi opinions; flexibility is recommended to maintain unity.

Imam's Takbir at the End of Iqamah
Ruling on when the imam should begin the prayer with takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred timing for the imam's takbir and cite the primary evidence from hadith and the practice of the tabi'i.

Core Idea
The imam should say takbir when the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah' — this is the sunnah, though other timings are permissible.

This lesson resolves a practical question in congregational prayer: when exactly should the imam commence with takbirat al-ihram? Through hadith and the guidance of early scholars, the preferred moment is identified as the phrase 'qad qamat al-salah'. Let us examine the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the preferred timing for the imam's takbir according to the Hanafi text.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proofs cited: hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith demonstrate the preferred time? The Prophet rose and said takbir when Bilal said 'qad qamat al-salah'.
This establishes a direct prophetic practice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Ibrahim al-Nakha'i indicates flexibility—any timing during the iqamah is permissible, but his own practice was at 'qad qamat'.
Shows that other timings are allowed but not optimal.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred view is that the imam should begin at 'qad qamat al-salah', combining the Prophet's action and the preferred practice of the tabi'i.
This becomes the mufta bihi.

ترجمه : (۴۵۱) [۱۰] اور قد قامت الصلوۃ کہنے کے وقت امام نماز شروع کرے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عبد الله بن ابی اوفى قال كان اذا قال بلال قد قامت الصلوة نهض رسول الله فكبر. (سنن بیہقی، باب من زعم انه يكبر قبل فراغ الموذن من الاقامة، ج ثانی، ص ۳۵، نمبر ۲۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قد قامت الصلوۃ کے وقت حضور تکبیر کہتے ۔ (۲) سألت ابراهيم متى يكبر الامام ؟ اذا فرغ المؤذن او قبل ان يفرغ ؟ قال ای ذالک فعلت فلا بأس ، قال و اخبرني الاعمش عن ابراهيم انه كان يكبر حين يقول المؤذن قد قامت الصلاة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب متی يكبر الامام؟ ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۸، نمبر ۵۵۳/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی الامام متی يكبر اذا قال المؤذن قد قامت الصلاة، ج اول ص ۳۵۵ نمبر ۴۰۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ کبھی بھی تکبیر کہے کوئی بات نہیں ہے، البتہ ادب یہ ہے کہ قد قامت الصلوۃ ، کے وقت امام تکبیر کہے۔ (۳) عن انس قال اقيمت الصلاة و رسول الله
Translation: (451) [10] And the imam should start the prayer at the time of 'qad qamat al-salah'. Evidence: (1) From Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: When Bilal said 'qad qamat al-salah', the Messenger of Allah rose and said takbir. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This hadith states that at the time of 'qad qamat al-salah', the Prophet said takbir. (2) I asked Ibrahim: When does the imam say takbir? When the mu'adhdhin finishes or before he finishes? He said: whichever you do, there is no problem. He said: And al-A'mash informed me from Ibrahim that he used to say takbir when the mu'adhdhin said 'qad qamat al-salah'. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) This statement of a tabi'i indicates that saying takbir at any time is fine, but the etiquette is that the imam says takbir at the time of 'qad qamat al-salah'. (3) From Anas: The iqamah was said and the Messenger of Allah... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This lesson determines the preferred time for the imam to begin the prayer by saying takbir. The established sunnah from multiple sources is that the imam should start when the mu'adhdhin reaches 'qad qamat al-salah'. The first proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa directly showing this practice of the Prophet. The second proof is a statement from the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who first gives flexibility but then indicates his own practice was to say takbir at 'qad qamat al-salah'. The commentary emphasizes that this is the recommended etiquette (adab). The third hadith from Anas is cut off in the text but likely similar. Thus, while other timings are permissible, the best practice is to start at that phrase.

Key Terms
قد قامت الصلوة (qad qamat al-salah): A phrase in the iqamah meaning 'the prayer has been established'.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The initial takbir that begins the prayer; referred to as 'takbir' in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the imam say the takbir to begin the prayer according to the Hanafi text?
A) At the beginning of iqamah
B) When the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-falah'
C) When the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah'
D) After the mu'adhdhin finishes the iqamah completely

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is for the imam to say takbir at the moment the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah', though other timings are permissible.

When to Stand During Iqamah: Etiquette and Flexibility
Discusses differing opinions on when to stand for congregational prayer during the iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended timing for the imam and muqtadi to stand during iqamah, and identify the evidence supporting the preferred Hanafi position.

Core Idea
The timing of standing during iqamah is a matter of sunnah, not obligation; flexibility is emphasized.

Congregational prayer begins with the iqamah, but when exactly should the followers stand? This lesson examines the differing opinions among early scholars and the proofs they cite. The Hanafi school recommends that the imam start at 'qad qamat al-salah', while the muqtadi may stand at 'hayya ala al-falah', with ample flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being discussed (standing during iqamah) and classify its hukm: is it obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible?
The passage treats this as a matter of adab (etiquette), not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith and athar cited. The passage quotes several: the hadith 'When the iqamah is said, do not stand until you see me', hadith of standing early, and statements of tabi'in.
Multiple proofs are presented for different timings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each proof supports a specific timing. For example, the imperative 'la taqumu' suggests not standing early, but other hadith show the Companions standing before the Prophet.
The author reconciles by classifying the differences as sunnah variations.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the views: standing at 'hayya ala al-salah', at 'qad qamat al-salah', or at the imam's arrival. The passage presents these as legitimate differences of opinion.
The Hanafi school opts for qad qamat al-salah for the imam.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the author prefers 'qad qamat al-salah' for the imam: based on multiple hadith, including the practice of the Prophet when Bilal gave the iqamah.
The mufta bihi is that the imam begins at qad qamat al-salah.

فصل في اداب الصلوة
حی علی الفلاح (۴۵۱) و شروع الامام مذ قيل قد قامت الصلوة. آرہی ہے ۔ دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جی علی الفلاح، سے پہلے کوئی مقتدی کھڑا نہ ہو، ٹھیک جی علی الفلاح، پر ہی کھڑا ہو، اور اس سے
تاخیر نہ کرے۔ دوسری جماعت اس طرف گئی ہے۔۔۔ یہ آداب ہیں اس لئے کسی جماعت کو اس پر تشد دنہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ وجه : (۱) امام جب تک مصلی پر آنے کے لئے تیار نہ ہو تو اقامت نہ کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة عن ابيه قال قال رسول الله الله اذا اقيمت الصلاة فلا تقوموا حتى ترونی ۔(بخاری شریف، باب منی لقوم الناس اذا ر وا الامام عند الاقامة ؟ ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۶۳۷ / مسلم شریف ، باب متى يقوم الناس للصلاة، ص ۲۴۴، نمبر ۱۳۹۵/۶۰۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام نماز کے لئے تیار ہوتب ہی مقتدی کھڑے ہوں چاہے اقامت کہی جا چکی ہو ۔ (۲) جی علی الفلاح، سے پہلے کھڑا ہوتار ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے . عن ابي هريرة ان الصلاة كانت تقام لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيأخذ الناس مصافهم قبل ان يقوم النبى الله مقامه - (مسلم شریف ، باب متى يقوم الناس للصلاة ص ۲۴۵، نمبر ۱۳۶۹/۶۰۵ را بوداود شریف، باب فی الصلاة تقام ولم يأت الامام بینظر و نہ قعودا ص ۹۰ نمبر (۵۴) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ آپ مصلی پر جاتے اس سے پہلے اقامت کہی جاتی اور لوگ نماز کے لئے کھڑے بھی ہو جاتے ۔ (۳) عن البراء بن عاذب قال كنا نقوم في الصفوف
صلہ الل
على عهد رسول الله لا طويلا قبل ان يكبر ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب فی الصلاة تقام ولم يأت الامام بینظر و نه قعودا ص ۹۰، نمبر ۵۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تکبیر سے بہت پہلے لوگ کھڑے ہو جاتے ۔ (۴) جو حضرات حی علی الصلوۃ پر کھڑے ہونے کے قائل ہیں انکی دلیل یہ قول تابعی ہے . عن الحسن انه كره ان يقوم الامام حتى يقول المؤذن قد قامت الصلوة ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ، باب من قال اذا قال المؤذن قد قامت الصلوة فلتقم ، ج اول ص ۳۵۶، نمبر ۴۰۹۹ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قد قامت الصلوۃ ، پر ہی کھڑا ہو۔
ترجمه : (۴۵۱) [۱۰] اور قد قامت الصلوۃ کہنے کے وقت امام نماز شروع کرے۔
وجه : (۱) عن عبد الله بن ابی اوفى قال كان اذا قال بلال قد قامت الصلوة نهض رسول الله الله فكبر. (سن بیہقی ، باب من زعم انہ یکبر قبل فراغ الموذن من الاقامة ، ج ثانی، ص ۳۵، نمبر ۷ ۲۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قد قامت الصلوۃ کے وقت حضور تکبیر کہتے ۔ (۲) سألت ابراهيم متى يكبر الامام ؟ اذا فرغ المؤذن او قبل ان يفرغ ؟ قال ای ذالک فـعـلـت فلا بأس ، قال و اخبرني الاعمش عن ابراهيم انه كان يكبر حين يقول المؤذن قد قامت الصلاة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب متنی یکبر الامام؟ ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۸، نمبر ۵۵۳/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی الامام متی یکبر اذا قال المؤذن قد قامت الصلاة ، ج اول ص ۳۵۵ نمبر ۴۰۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ کبھی بھی تکبیر کہے کوئی بات نہیں ہے،

(2) Standing before 'hayya ala al-falah' is allowed; proof from hadith... (3) Hadith that they used to stand in rows for a long time before takbir... (4) Those who hold standing at 'hayya ala al-salah' use the saying of a tabi'i... Translation: (451) [10] The imam starts prayer when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said. Proof: (1) Hadith that when Bilal said 'qad qamat al-salah', the Prophet rose and said takbir... (2) Ibrahim was asked when the imam should say takbir; he said it doesn't matter, but it is proper to say takbir when the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah'... (3) Hadith that the iqamah was said and the Prophet was in a corner of the mosque and did not stand until the people had fallen asleep... this hadith indicates that the takbir was said a considerable time after the iqamah.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof discussing the proper etiquettes of standing for congregational prayer during the iqamah. The author presents multiple views and proofs from hadith and the sayings of tabi'in. The preferred Hanafi position is that the muqtadi may stand at 'hayya ala al-falah' or later, but it is recommended to stand when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said for the imam to start. The proofs include hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and others. The passage shows flexibility and discourages strictness. The imam should begin the takbir at 'qad qamat al-salah' as indicated by the practice of the Prophet and the statements of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Key Terms
اقامت (iqamah): The second call to prayer consisting of similar phrases as adhan but with 'qad qamat al-salah' added twice.
مقتدی (muqtadi): Follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
حی علی الفلاح (hayya ala al-falah): A phrase in the adhan and iqamah meaning 'come to success'.
قد قامت الصلوة (qad qamat al-salah): The phrase in the iqamah meaning 'the prayer has been established'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it recommended for the imam to begin the takbir?
A) At 'hayya ala al-salah'
B) At 'qad qamat al-salah'
C) When the muqtadi are all standing
D) After the iqamah is complete

Key Takeaway
Standing at 'qad qamat al-salah' is recommended for the imam, but other timings are permissible without sin.

The Opening Takbir: Fard but Flexible in Wording
Describes the opening actions of prayer: raising hands, takbir, and validity of any pure dhikr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the opening takbir and explain why any pure dhikr suffices for validity, citing the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is fard, but any pure dhikr of Allah suffices — the Quranic proof allows flexibility.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah details the initial actions of prayer. While the sunnah is to say 'Allahu Akbar', the Hanafi school permits any pure remembrance of Allah (dhikr) for the opening takbir. This ruling is derived from Quranic verses that emphasize magnifying Allah through any form of praise. Understanding this flexibility helps avoid unnecessary strictness and ensures the prayer's validity even if the specific phrase is not recited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is fard (obligatory). Determine what exactly is fard: the act of starting prayer with a dhikr, not necessarily the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar'.
The text explicitly says 'تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہے' (the opening takbir is fard).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two Quranic verses: 'وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّىٰ' (and mention the name of his Lord and pray) and 'وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ' (and your Lord magnify). Identify that these are the primary proofs.
A third hadith is mentioned but cut off in this excerpt.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each verse proves the ruling. The first verse indicates that any mention of Allah's name before prayer is sufficient. The second shows that the objective is magnification (takbir), which can be achieved by any word of praise, not only the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar'.
The Hanafi principle: the general command (amm) is understood as inclusive.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require the exact phrase 'Allahu Akbar' for the opening takbir. Understand that this difference stems from how they interpret the same verses.
The Hanafi position is that any pure dhikr (like 'Subhanallah') is valid.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that saying 'Allahu Akbar' is best, but other phrases like 'Subhanallah' suffice. This is based on the Quran's generality and the principle that the essence is remembrance of Allah.
The author does not give a separate preference; the text itself presents this as the ruling.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof detailing the initial actions of prayer. The author states that a man should remove his hands from his sleeves, raise them to the level of his ears, and say the takbir with intention, avoiding prolongation of the vowel in 'Allah' because it could change the meaning to a question implying disbelief. The takbir is fard (obligatory). However, if one says any dhikr that is pure praise of Allah without supplication, like 'Subhanallah', the prayer is still valid because the essence is the remembrance of Allah as indicated by the Quranic verses. The author notes that most of these rulings have been discussed earlier in sections on fard, wajib, sunan, and adab of prayer, so proofs are only given for new issues. The proof for (453) is from Quran and a hadith that is cut off in this excerpt.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbirat al-ihram): The opening takbir that makes the prayer begin and prohibits worldly actions.
مد (madd): Prolongation of the vowel sound; in 'Allah', prolonging the initial 'a' can turn it into an interrogative 'a-Allah' meaning 'Is Allah?' which is problematic.

How a Man Enters Prayer: Raising Hands and Takbir
Ruling on the opening actions of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required physical actions for a man entering prayer and explain why prolonging the takbir's vowel invalidates the act.

Core Idea
A man must raise his hands to his ears and say 'Allahu Akbar' without prolongation; prolonging the vowel changes the meaning to disbelief.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah details the initial steps a man performs when entering salah (prayer). The sequence—removing hands from sleeves, raising them to the ears, and uttering the opening takbir with intention—is outlined with a crucial caution against elongating the vowel in 'Allah'. This lesson breaks down these actions and their juristic significance, drawing from Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequential actions
List the actions a man performs in order: (1) remove hands from sleeves, (2) raise hands to ears, (3) say 'Allahu Akbar' with intention, (4) avoid prolongation (mad).
2
Classify each action in Hanafi fiqh
Based on standard Hanafi rulings, tag each action: removing hands = adab (propriety), raising hands = sunnah, saying takbir = fard (obligatory), intention = fard (pillar of prayer), avoiding prolongation = condition for validity.
The passage itself does not assign these categories; they are inferred from known Hanafi principles.
3
Understand the prohibition of mad
Prolonging the alif in 'Allah' (Āllah) turns it into an interrogative (Ā-llah? meaning 'Is Allah?'), which changes the intended meaning and renders the takbir invalid, leading to disbelief (kufr).
This is a unique Hanafi caution; other schools may not emphasize it as severely.
4
Apply ruling to common scenarios
Consider a man who raises his hands only to his chest or says 'Allaahu Akbar' with a slight prolongation. According to the passage, the hand position may reduce reward but the takbir is still valid if pronounced correctly without excessive mad.
Raising to ears is sunnah; slight deviation does not invalidate, but intentional mad does.

Section on the composition of prayer. Section: On the manner of composing prayer. (452) When a man intends to enter the prayer, he takes out his two hands from his sleeves, then raises them to the level of his ears, then says Allahu Akbar without prolongation, with intention. ... this hadith says that after the iqamah, the takbir was said after a sufficient delay. Section: On the explanation of the manner of prayer. Important note: Most of the issues in this section have already passed in the obligations of prayer, obligations of prayer, sunnahs of prayer, and etiquettes of prayer, and their evidence has also passed there. Therefore, their evidence will not be repeated here; otherwise the book would become very thick. Yes, those issues that have not passed, their evidence will be mentioned here. Translation: (452) When a man intends to enter the prayer, first he takes out his hands from his sleeves, then raises both hands to the level of his ears, then with intention says 'Allahu Akbar' without prolongation. Commentary: The arrangement of prayer for men and women is almost the same; only where there is a difference, it will be mentioned. When a man intends to pray, he takes his hands out of the sleeves; this is a propriety. He raises both hands to the level of the ears, then says the takbir while intending the prayer. However, there should be no prolongation in the takbir because if he prolongs the alif of Allah, it becomes an interrogative, and the meaning becomes 'Is Allah great?' and that would necessitate disbelief. Therefore, he should not prolong. 'Kumm': sleeve. 'Hidha'': opposite, facing.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the section on the composition of prayer. It describes the opening actions for a man entering prayer. The author first states the ruling: when a man intends to pray, he must take his hands out of his sleeves, raise them to the level of his ears, and say 'Allahu Akbar' without prolongation, with intention. The commentary explains that this is the proper etiquette, and the takbir must not be elongated because changing the pronunciation of 'Allah' to 'A-llah' could turn it into a question, which would be disbelief. The hadith cited refers to a narration about the takbir being said after a delay from the iqamah, but it is not the primary proof for this ruling. The note explains that many issues have already been covered with their proofs in earlier sections, so only new issues will have proofs given.

تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and prohibits actions outside prayer.
مد (mad): Prolongation of the vowel sound in the pronunciation of 'Allahu Akbar'.

Validity of Opening Takbir with Any Pure Dhikr
Ruling that the opening takbir is valid with any pure remembrance of Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of the opening takbir with any pure dhikr, identify the condition of pure praise, and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is valid with any pure remembrance of Allah; magnification, not specific words, is what matters.

This lesson addresses a common question: Must the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) be the exact phrase 'Allahu Akbar'? According to the Hanafi school, any pure dhikr of Allah suffices as long as it expresses magnification. We will examine the evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and the ruling of the Companions (athar).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling and Its Condition
Identify the legal rule: the opening takbir is fard, and it is valid with any pure dhikr of Allah (e.g., 'Subhan Allah') but not with a supplication (e.g., 'Allahumma ighfir li').
The condition is 'khāliṣ' (pure) — the phrase must be purely praise, not a request.
2
Locate the First Proof (Quran 87:15)
Find the verse 'wa dhakra isma rabbihi faṣallā' (And mentions the name of his Lord and prays). This indicates that any mention of Allah's name suffices before prayer.
The verse does not specify 'Allahu Akbar'; it uses the general 'ism' (name).
3
Locate the Second Proof (Quran 74:3)
Find the verse 'wa rabbaka fakabbir' (And your Lord magnify). The imperative 'kabbir' means magnify, which can be done with any expression of magnification.
The root k-b-r implies exalting, not a specific formula.
4
Locate the Hadith and Athar Proofs
Identify the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet used the takbir when starting night prayer. Also, the athar from al-Sha'bi: 'With whichever of Allah's names you open the prayer, it suffices you.'
These show the prophetic practice and a Companion's explicit ruling.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i Position
The Shafi'i school requires the specific words 'Allahu Akbar'. The Hanafi position is more flexible based on the general proofs.
The practical consequence: a person who says 'Subhan Allah' with intention of takbir has validly started prayer in the Hanafi school.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ا
۳۰۴
فصل في تركيب الصلوة
(۴۵۴) وبالفارسية ان عـجـز عـن الـعـربية وان قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية ولا قراء ته بها في كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ۔ (ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷، نمبر ۲۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحریمہ کے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ اس لئے کسی بھی کلمات سے تعظیم کرنا کافی ہوگا۔ (۴) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال : بأى أسماء الله افتتحت الصلوة أجزاک ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ما سجزی من افتتاح الصلوة ، ج اول، ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۲۴۶۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اللہ کے کسی نام سے بھی تکبیر شروع کرے گا تو تکبیر ہو جائے گی۔
(453) And the commencement (of prayer) is valid with every pure remembrance of Allah, such as 'Subhan Allah'. Translation: (453) And it is valid to start the prayer with every pure dhikr of Allah, like 'Subhan Allah'. Commentary: The opening takbir is fard; for it, saying 'Allahu Akbar' is better. But if he says the opening takbir with any dhikr that contains pure remembrance of Allah, not supplication, then it also becomes the opening takbir. For example, if he says 'Subhan Allah', the opening takbir will be valid. And if it is a supplication like 'Allahumma ighfir li', then it will not be considered takbir. Proofs: (1) In the verse: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' (Surah al-A'la, 87:15). From this verse, it is understood that before prayer, one may utter any name of Allah, whether it is the takbir or any other word of magnification. (2) In the verse: 'And your Lord magnify' (Surah al-Muddaththir, 74:3). From this verse also, it is understood that the main objective is to magnify Allah, regardless of the specific word. (3) In the hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: ... The Messenger of Allah, when he stood for prayer at night, said the takbir. (Tirmidhi, chapter on what to say at the opening of prayer, p.57, no.242) This hadith indicates that the takbir is said at the time of the opening. Therefore, magnifying with any words is sufficient. (4) In the athar: from al-Sha'bi, he said: 'With whichever of Allah's names you open the prayer, it will suffice you.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on what suffices for opening prayer, vol.1, p.215, no.2464) This athar indicates that if one starts the takbir with any name of Allah, the takbir will be valid.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author states that the opening takbir can be performed with any pure dhikr of Allah, not necessarily 'Allahu Akbar'. The commentary explains that this is valid only if the dhikr is purely praise, not a supplication. Four proofs are provided: two Quranic verses (87:15 and 74:3) show that mentioning Allah's name or magnifying Him is sufficient. A hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri confirms that the Prophet used the takbir when starting prayer. An athar from al-Sha'bi explicitly allows opening with any of Allah's names. The Hanafi position is thus that the intention of magnifying Allah is crucial; the specific wording is secondary.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
ذکر خالص (dhikr khalis): A phrase that is purely praise of Allah without any element of supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which phrase WOULD NOT be valid as an opening takbir?
A) Subhan Allah
B) Allahu Akbar
C) Allahumma ighfir li
D) La ilaha illa Allah

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) is valid with any pure dhikr of Allah; the essential element is magnification, not a specific wording.

Salah — Prayer
