Using Farsi for Takbir and Recitation in Prayer
Ruling on using Farsi for takbir and recitation when unable to speak Arabic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on using translation for takbir and Quranic recitation in prayer, and identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi requires Arabic recitation in prayer when capable, despite Abu Hanifa's permission to use translation.

The proper performance of salah requires recitation of the Quran and the takbir in Arabic. But what if a person cannot speak Arabic? This passage from the Hanafi tradition addresses that very question—and goes deeper into a dispute among the school's founders when a person actually can speak Arabic. The ruling hinges on the nature of the Quran: is it essence (meaning) or form (Arabic wording)?

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
Determine the agreed-upon ruling when the person is unable to speak Arabic (عاجز عن العربية). The text states that if one cannot say the takbir or recite in Arabic, using Farsi is permissible and the prayer is valid.
This applies to genuine incapacity, not mere lack of fluency.
2
Locate the point of dispute
Recognize the disagreement arises when the person is able to speak Arabic (عربی آتی ہو). The text reports a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
The dispute is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that conveying the meaning in another language fulfills the obligation. His proofs: (1) previous scriptures (Torah, Gospel, Scrolls) were in non-Arabic languages and were recited in prayer; (2) Quranic verses (26:196, 87:19) indicate that the Quran existed in those books; and (3) a hadith states that certain surahs were given from earlier revelations. Thus, the Arabic wording is not essential for fulfilling the obligation.
Abu Hanifa still considers it sinful to abandon the sunnah of Arabic.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn insist that the Quran is defined as the combination of meaning and Arabic wording. Mere translation does not qualify as Quranic recitation. Their principle is that 'the name Quran is given to the combination of meaning and wording.' Therefore, recitation in any language other than Arabic does not discharge the duty when one is capable of Arabic.
The text mentions that 'the correct narration' supports the Sahibayn, indicating the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The text states 'the correct narration is that reciting in Farsi is also not valid' (صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ فارسی میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت کا ترجمہ کر کے قرآت کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے). This reveals that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view. Practically, if a person who knows Arabic recites a translation, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The Shafi'i school also requires Arabic; only extreme incapacity permits translation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۵۴) و بالفارسية ان عـجـز عـن الـعـربية وان قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية ولا قراء ته بها في
كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ۔ (ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷، نمبر ۲۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحریمہ کے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ اس لئے کسی بھی کلمات سے تعظیم کرنا کافی ہوگا۔
تشریح : اگر عربی میں تکبیر بھی نہیں کہ سکتا ہو تو فارسی میں تکبیر کہ لے اور بڑائی بیان کر لے تب بھی نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح عربی نہیں آتی ہو تو فارسی میں قرآت کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ یہ مجبور ہے۔ لیکن اگر عربی آتی ہو تو فارسی میں تکبیر کہنا درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ
یہ مجبور نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ فارسی میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت کا ترجمہ کر کے قرآت کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
اصول : عربی اچھی نہ آتی ہوتب تو بالا تفاق نماز ہو جائے گی ۔ لیکن اگر عربی اچھی آتی ہو تو اختلاف ہے کہ یہ سب ہو جائے گی یا نہیں ۔ اختلاف کا مدار اس بات پر ہے کہ آیت کا معنی کسی دوسری زبان میں ادا کر دیا جائے تو آیت کی ادا ئیگی ہوگی یا نہیں ! امام ابو
حنیفہ کے نزدیک دوسری زبان میں معنی ادا کر دیا جائے تو ادا ئیگی ہو جائے گی البتہ سنت متوارثہ کی مخالفت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عربی زبان کی اہمیت ضرور ہے لیکن آیت کا معنی اصل ہے جو کسی بھی زبان میں ادا ہو جائے تو کافی ہے (۲) کیونکہ بہت سی سورتیں دوسری کتا ہیں ، تو رات اور انجیل اور صحف ابراہیم میں تھیں جو عربی کے علاوہ دوسری زبان میں تھیں اور اس امت کے لوگ اسی کو اپنی نماز میں پڑھتے تھے جسکا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ دوسری زبان میں سورت پڑھ دینا جائز ہے۔اس آیت میں اسکا ذکر ہے۔ و انه لفی زیر الاولین ( آیت ۱۹۶ ، سورۃ الشعراء ۲۶) اس آیت میں ہے کہ آیت پہلی کتابوں میں تھی ، (۲) اس آیت میں بھی ہے کہ قرآن پچھلی کتابوں میں تھا۔ ان هذا لفى الصحف الاولى صحف ابراهیم و موسی . (آیت ۱۹ سورۃ الاعلی ۸۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ قرآن پچھلی کتابوں میں تھا (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عـن مـعـقـل بـن يسار قال : قال صلى الله رسول الله عله : .... و انى أعطيت سورة البقرة من الذكر الاول و أعطيت طه ، و طواسين ،و الحوامين من الواح موسى و اعطيت فاتحة الكتاب من تحت العرش - مستدرک للحاکم ، باب ذکر فضائل سور و آی متفرقه ، ج اول ، ص ۷ ۷۵ نمبر ۷ (۲۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ یہ سورتیں پہلی کتابوں میں تھیں۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ وہ دوسری زبان میں ہی ہوگی اسلئے دوسری زبان میں آیت پڑھنا جائز ہوگا۔ صاحبین کا اصول یہ ہے کہ معنی کے ساتھ عربی کے الفاظ بھی ضروری ہیں، انکے یہاں معنی اور لفظ دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام قرآن ہے۔
Translation: (454) And in Persian if one is unable to speak Arabic, but if he is able, his starting (prayer) in Persian is not valid, nor is his recitation in Persian. The Messenger of Allah, when he stood for prayer at night, said the takbir. (Tirmidhi, chapter on what to say at the opening of prayer, p.57, no.242) From this hadith, it is understood that the takbir is said at the time of the opening. Therefore, magnifying with any words is sufficient. Commentary: If one cannot even say the takbir in Arabic, then he may say the takbir in Persian and express magnification; then the prayer will still be valid. Similarly, if one does not know Arabic, recitation in Persian is permissible because he is compelled. But if he knows Arabic, saying the takbir in Persian is not correct, because he is not compelled. Similarly, the correct narration is that reciting Surah al-Fatiha and other surahs by translating them into Persian is also not valid. Principle: If one does not know Arabic well, then by agreement the prayer will be valid. But if he knows Arabic well, there is disagreement whether it will all be valid or not. The difference revolves around whether conveying the meaning of a verse in another language constitutes conveying the verse. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the meaning is conveyed in another language, the verse is conveyed, though he will be sinful for opposing the inherited sunnah. Proofs: (1) The reason is that the Arabic language certainly has importance, but the meaning of the verse is the essence; if it is conveyed in any language, it is sufficient. (2) Because many surahs were in other books—the Torah, the Gospel, and the Scrolls of Abraham—which were in languages other than Arabic, and the people of this nation used to recite them in their prayers. This means that reciting a surah in another language is permissible. This is mentioned in the verse: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' (Surah al-Shu'ara, 26:196). This verse indicates that the Quran was in the previous books. (3) Also in the verse: 'Indeed this is in the former scriptures, the scriptures of Abraham and Moses' (Surah al-A'la, 87:19). This verse indicates that the Quran was in the previous books. (4) In the hadith: from Ma'qil ibn Yasar, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: '... and I was given Surah al-Baqarah from the first remembrance, and I was given Ta-Ha, the Tawasin, and the Hawamim from the tablets of Moses, and I was given the Opening of the Book from beneath the Throne.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim, chapter on virtues of various surahs and verses, vol.1, p.75, no.208) This hadith indicates that these surahs were in the previous books. And it is obvious that they were in other languages, so reciting a verse in another language is permissible. The principle of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that along with the meaning, the Arabic words are also necessary; according to them, the name 'Quran' is given to the combination of meaning and wording.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the use of non-Arabic (Farsi) for the opening takbir and Quranic recitation in prayer when one is able to speak Arabic. The ruling initially states that if one is unable to speak Arabic, Farsi may be used; but if able, it is not valid. The commentary clarifies that the inability refers to actual incapacity, not mere difficulty. A key dispute arises over whether reciting the Quran in translation suffices. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that conveying the meaning in another language fulfills the obligation, though one may be sinful for abandoning the sunnah. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require both the Arabic wording and the meaning, as the Quran is defined by its specific Arabic expression. The text provides proofs from the Quran and hadith showing that previous scriptures were in non-Arabic languages, and those were recited in prayer by earlier communities. However, the Sahibayn's position is stated without full rebuttal, leaving the reader to note the difference.

Key Terms
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Refers to the two chief disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
قرآت (qira'ah): The recitation of Quranic verses during the prayer, specifically in the standing position.
عجز (ajz): Inability or incapacity to perform an act.
مجبور (majbur): Compelled; one who has no choice but to do a certain act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in this passage, what is the ruling if a person who knows Arabic recites the meaning of Surah al-Fatiha in Farsi during prayer?
A) The prayer is valid and recommended.
B) The prayer is valid but sinful.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The prayer is valid if the intention is correct.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires Quranic recitation in Arabic when one is capable; translation is only permitted for those genuinely unable to speak Arabic.

Reciting Takbir and Quran in Persian: The Hanafi Intra-Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting takbir and Quran in Persian when capable of Arabic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn's positions on reciting the takbir and Quran in Persian in prayer, identify their respective proofs, and explain the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Reciting meaning in another language fulfills recitation, but sin remains; the correct view invalidates the prayer if capable of Arabic.

The composition of prayer includes recitation of the Quran and the opening takbir. What if a person who knows Arabic recites these in Persian? Imam Abu Hanifa and his leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. Their dispute hinges on whether the Quran is defined by meaning alone or by both words and meaning. This lesson unpacks their arguments and identifies the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of disagreement
The dispute centers on whether a person capable of Arabic may validly begin the prayer (say the takbir) or recite the Quran in Persian translation. If unable, all agree it is permissible.
The text explicitly states if unable, Persian is allowed by consensus.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his proofs
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that reciting the meaning in another language fulfills the obligation, so the prayer is valid. However, the person is sinful for abandoning the sunnah. His proofs include: (1) meaning is primary, (2) previous scriptures in non-Arabic languages were recited by earlier nations, (3) a hadith that surahs were given from previous books, and (4) an athar that any of Allah's names suffices for the takbir.
The meaning-based definition of Quran allows translation to convey the verse.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proofs
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that reciting in Persian when capable invalidates the prayer because the Quran is both its Arabic words and its meaning. Their proof includes Quranic verses emphasizing an Arabic Quran and the requirement of tartil (proper recitation).
For them, translation does not constitute qira'ah.
4
Locate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a capable person recites in Persian, Abu Hanifa says the prayer must be repeated (since it is sinful but valid?) Actually, he says valid but sinful, so no need to repeat; Sahibayn say it is invalid and must be repeated. The text states 'correct narration' supports Sahibayn.
The mufta bihi is Sahibayn's view: the prayer is invalid.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text explicitly says 'correct narration' is that reciting in Persian is not valid. Later Hanafi fatwa works adopt the Sahibayn's position when the person is capable of Arabic.
This is the operative ruling for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تركيب الصلوة
(٤٥٤) وبالفارسية ان عجز عن العربية وان قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية ولا قراءته بها في كان رسول الله ﷺ اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر. (ترمذی شریف، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۵۷، نمبر ۲۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تحریمہ کے وقت تکبیر کہے۔ اس لئے کسی بھی کلمات سے تعظیم کرنا کافی ہوگا۔ (٤) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال : بأى أسماء الله افتتحت الصلوة أجزاک. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ما سجزی من افتتاح الصلوة، ج اول، ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۲۴۶۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اللہ کے کسی نام سے بھی تکبیر شروع کرے گا تو تکبیر ہو جائے گی۔
ترجمه : (٤٥٤) اور عربی سے عاجز ہو تو فارسی میں کہے۔ اور اگر قادر ہو عربی پر تو نہیں صحیح ہے اس کا شروع کرنا فارسی میں۔ اور اسی طرح صحیح روایت کے موافق نہیں صحیح ہے اس کی قرآت کرنا فارسی میں۔
تشریح : اگر عربی میں تکبیر بھی نہیں کہ سکتا ہو تو فارسی میں تکبیر کہ لے اور بڑائی بیان کر لے تب بھی نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح عربی نہیں آتی ہو تو فارسی میں قرآت کرنا جائز ہے، کیونکہ یہ مجبور ہے۔ لیکن اگر عربی آتی ہو تو فارسی میں تکبیر کہنا درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ مجبور نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح صحیح روایت یہ ہے کہ فارسی میں سورہ فاتحہ اور سورت کا ترجمہ کر کے قرآت کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
اصول : عربی اچھی نہ آتی ہو تب تو بالاتفاق نماز ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن اگر عربی اچھی آتی ہو تو اختلاف ہے کہ یہ سب ہو جائے گی یا نہیں۔ اختلاف کا مدار اس بات پر ہے کہ آیت کا معنی کسی دوسری زبان میں ادا کر دیا جائے تو آیت کی ادائیگی ہوگی یا نہیں! امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دوسری زبان میں معنی ادا کر دیا جائے تو ادائیگی ہو جائے گی البتہ سنت متوارثہ کی مخالفت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عربی زبان کی اہمیت ضرور ہے لیکن آیت کا معنی اصل ہے جو کسی بھی زبان میں ادا ہو جائے تو کافی ہے (۲) کیونکہ بہت سی سورتیں دوسری کتا ہیں، تو رات اور انجیل اور صحف ابراہیم میں تھیں جو عربی کے علاوہ دوسری زبان میں تھیں اور اس امت کے لوگ اسی کو اپنی نماز میں پڑھتے تھے جسکا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ دوسری زبان میں سورت پڑھ دینا جائز ہے۔ اس آیت میں اسکا ذکر ہے۔ و إنه لفي زبر الأولين (آیت ۱۹۶، سورۃ الشعراء ۲۶) اس آیت میں ہے کہ آیت پہلی کتابوں میں تھی، (۲) اس آیت میں بھی ہے کہ قرآن پچھلی کتابوں میں تھا۔ إن هذا لفي الصحف الأولى صحف إبراهيم وموسى. (آیت ۱۹ سورۃ الأعلى ۸۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ قرآن پچھلی کتابوں میں تھا (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن معقل بن يسار قال : قال صلى الله رسول الله عليه : .... و إني أعطيت سورة البقرة من الذكر الأول و أعطيت طه، و طواسين، و الحوامين من ألواح موسى و أعطيت فاتحة الكتاب من تحت العرش - مستدرک للحاکم، باب ذکر فضائل سور و آی متفرقه، ج اول، ص ۷۷۵ نمبر ۷ (۲۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ یہ سورتیں پہلی کتابوں میں تھیں۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ وہ دوسری زبان میں ہی ہوگی اس لئے دوسری زبان میں آیت پڑھنا جائز ہوگا۔
صاحبین کا اصول یہ ہے کہ معنی کے ساتھ عربی کے الفاظ بھی ضروری ہیں، انکے یہاں معنی اور لفظ دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام قرآن ہے۔
Section on the composition of prayer. (454) And in Persian if he is unable to recite Arabic, and if he is able, his commencing in Persian is not valid, nor is his recitation in it. [Hadith:] 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood for prayer at night, he said the takbir.' (Tirmidhi) From this hadith it is understood that at the time of tahrimah one says the takbir. Therefore, glorification with any words suffices. (4) There is an athar from al-Sha'bi: 'by whichever of Allah's names you open the prayer, it suffices you.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This athar states that whichever of Allah's names one uses to begin the takbir, the takbir is valid. Translation: (454) If he is unable to recite in Arabic, he may say it in Persian. But if he is capable of Arabic, his commencing in Persian is not valid, and similarly, according to the correct narration, his reciting the Quran in Persian is not valid. Explanation: If he cannot even say the takbir in Arabic, he may say the takbir in Persian and express glorification, and the prayer will still be valid. Similarly, if he does not know Arabic, reciting the Quran in Persian is permissible because he is compelled. But if he knows Arabic, saying the takbir in Persian is not correct because he is not compelled. Similarly, the correct narration is that reciting the translation of Surah al-Fatihah and other surahs in Persian is also not correct. Principle: If one does not know Arabic well, then by consensus the prayer is valid. But if one knows Arabic well, there is disagreement whether it will all be valid or not. The point of disagreement is whether conveying the meaning of a verse in another language constitutes recitation of the verse. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, if the meaning is conveyed in another language, the recitation is valid, but he will be sinful for opposing the inherited sunnah. Proof: (1) The reason is that although the Arabic language has importance, the meaning of the verse is fundamental, so if it is conveyed in any language, it suffices. (2) Because many surahs were in other books—the Torah, the Gospel, and the Scriptures of Ibrahim—which were in languages other than Arabic, and the people of this nation used to recite them in their prayers, meaning that reciting a surah in another language is permissible. There is mention of this in the verse: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' (26:196). This verse states that the verse was in previous books. Also this verse: 'Indeed this is in the former scriptures, the scriptures of Ibrahim and Musa' (87:18-19). This verse states that the Quran was in previous books. (3) There is a hadith from Ma'qil ibn Yasar: 'I was given Surah al-Baqarah from the first remembrance, and I was given Ta-Ha, the Ta-Sins, and the Ha-Mims from the tablets of Musa, and I was given the Opening of the Book from beneath the Throne.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim) This hadith states that these surahs were in previous books, and obviously they were in another language, so reciting a verse in another language is permissible. The principle of the Sahibayn is that along with the meaning, the Arabic words are also necessary; in their view, the name 'Quran' is given to the combination of both meaning and words.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the section on the composition of prayer. The text begins by stating the ruling (454) that if a person is unable to recite Arabic, they may say the takbir and recite the Quran in Persian. However, if they are capable of Arabic, it is not valid to commence the prayer in Persian or recite the Quran in translation. The commentary then explains that if one cannot even say the takbir in Arabic, saying it in Persian suffices. If one does not know Arabic, reciting in Persian is permissible due to necessity. But if one knows Arabic, the correct narration is that Persian recitation is not valid. The principle is that there is consensus when one does not know Arabic, but there is disagreement when one knows Arabic. The point of contention is whether conveying the meaning in another language fulfills the recitation of the verse. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it does, but the person is sinful for opposing the inherited sunnah. The text then provides proofs for Abu Hanifa's position: (1) The meaning is primary; (2) Previous scriptures were in non-Arabic languages and the early Muslims recited them; (3) A hadith indicates that surahs existed in previous books in other languages. Finally, the principle of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is presented: that both the Arabic words and meaning together constitute the Quran, so reciting only the meaning in another language is not valid. This passage shows the methodological difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding the definition of Quranic recitation. The relied-upon position for fatwa is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi works generally adopt the view of the Sahibayn when the person is capable of Arabic.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
معنی اور لفظ دونوں کا مجموعہ (ma'na wa lafz donon ka majmu'ah): The combined entity of meaning and wording; Sahibayn define Quran as both.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'correct narration' in the text, what is the ruling if a person who knows Arabic recites the Quran in Persian translation during prayer?
A) The prayer is valid but the person is sinful.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid and there is no sin.
D) The prayer is valid only if the takbir is also in Persian.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that reciting the Quran in translation during prayer when capable of Arabic invalidates the prayer; the prayer is valid only in cases of inability.

Hand Placement After Tahrimah: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on hand placement after takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement after the opening takbir, identify its hukm level, and apply it correctly in prayer.

Core Idea
Placing hands under navel immediately after takbir is sunnah muakkadah, not fard.

This lesson examines the precise manner of hand placement (wadh' al-yadayn) after the opening takbir in Hanafi prayer. The source text provides the ruling that the right hand should be placed on the left under the navel without delay, supported by the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr. Understanding this ruling ensures you correctly follow the sunnah without overstepping its legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the action described: placing the right hand on the left after the opening takbir. Note that the text calls it 'al-asahh' (the most correct) and that it is a sunnah act.
The ruling is not fard or wajib; it is a confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing the Prophet's action. Read the hadith carefully to identify the sequence: takbir, then hand placement.
The dalil is ahad (single narration) but sahih.
3
Note the immediacy requirement
The phrase 'بلا مهلة' (without delay) indicates that the hand placement should be right after the takbir. There should be no noticeable pause.
Delaying intentionaly loses the sunnah.
4
Note the location
The text specifies 'تحت سرته' (under his navel). This is the Hanafi position, distinct from other schools.
Abu Yusuf differed, but the mufta bihi is under the navel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاصح. (٤٥٥) ثم وضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته عقب التحريمة بلا مهلة.
تشریح : تکبیر تحریمہ کے بعد تحریمہ باندھنے میں دیر نہ کرے، بلکہ فورا ناف کے نیچے دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ کے اوپر رکھے، اور ثناء پڑھے.
وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تکبیر کے بعد فورا ہاتھ باندھے۔ عن وائل بن حجر انه رأى النبي ﷺ رفع يديه حين دخل في الصلاة كبر - وصف همام حيال اذنيه ـ ثم التحف بثوبه ثم وضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى. (مسلم شریف، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری ص ۱۷۰ نمبر ۸۹۶/۴۰)
The most correct. (455) Then he places his right hand on his left under his navel immediately after the tahrimah without delay.
Explanation: After the takbir tahrimah, he should not delay in binding the tahrimah, but immediately place his right hand over his left under the navel and recite the thana.
Proof: In this hadith it is that after the takbir he immediately folds his hands. From Wa'il ibn Hujr: 'He saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) raise his hands when he entered into prayer and said the takbir... then he wrapped himself in his garment and placed his right hand on his left.' (Muslim, Book of Prayer, Chapter on Placing the Right Hand on the Left, hadith no. 896/40)
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the manner of hand placement in prayer. The text states the most correct (al-asahh) position that after the opening takbir (tahrimah), one should immediately place the right hand on the left under the navel without delay. The explanation clarifies that the binding of the hands should occur right after the takbir, not with a pause. The proof is a hadith from Wa'il ibn Hujr describing the Prophet's (peace be upon him) action. The phrase 'under the navel' reflects the Hanafi position, which differs from some other schools that place hands on the chest. The command 'without delay' emphasizes that there should be no gap between the takbir and the hand placement. This is a sunnah act of the prayer, not a fard; if omitted, the prayer is still valid but the sunnah is missed.

Key Terms
تحریہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes prayer begin and prohibits worldly actions.
وضع یدین (wadh' al-yadayn): Placing the right hand on the left after takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should a person place their hands after the opening takbir?
A) Under the navel.
B) On the chest.
C) On the navel.
D) At the sides.

Key Takeaway
Placing the right hand on the left under the navel immediately after the opening takbir is a confirmed sunnah in Hanafi prayer, not a fard.

The Opening Supplication (Thana): Ruling and Wording
Ruling on reciting the opening supplication (thana) in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the thana and state its ruling in the Hanafi school as a sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Thana is a sunnah muakkadah opening supplication after takbir; omitting it does not invalidate prayer.

This lesson presents the exact wording of the opening supplication (thana) and clarifies its legal status in the Hanafi school. The thana is a recommended act, not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that every praying person recites the thana at the beginning. Identify that this act is the opening supplication (thana) and that the Hanafi ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
Sunnah muakkadah means confirmed sunnah - regularly practiced by the Prophet.
2
Memorize the wording
Learn the exact Arabic text: سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك. This is the prescribed wording.
This supplication is also known as Subhanaka Allahumma.
3
Understand the timing
It is recited after the opening takbir and before seeking refuge (ta'awwudh). It is only recited in the first rak'ah.
If a follower joins late, they may still recite it if they catch the imam before recitation begins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤٥٦) مستفتحا وهو ان يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك.
ترجمه: (٤٥٦) ثناء پڑھے: سبحانك اللهم و بحمدك و تبارك اسمك و تعالی جدك ولا إله غيرک ہر ایک نمازی شروع میں ثنا پڑھے۔
(456) Opening with the supplication, which is: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakas-muka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.'
Translation: (456) Recite the thana: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakas-muka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.' Every praying person recites the thana at the beginning.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This is a ruling statement prescribing the opening supplication (thana) in prayer. The text gives the exact wording: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' and states that every person praying should recite it at the beginning. The thana is recited after the takbir and before the ta'awwudh and basmalah. According to the Hanafi school, the thana is sunnah for both the imam and the follower. It is recited in the first rak'ah only. If the follower joins the prayer late, they may recite thana if they catch the imam before he begins recitation. The wording provided is the most common and is considered the authentic version transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication recited after the takbir in prayer, praising Allah.
سبحانك اللهم (Subhanaka Allahumma): The specific wording of the thana, meaning 'Glory be to You, O Allah.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting the thana (Subhanaka Allahumma) at the beginning of prayer?
A) Wajib, and if omitted the prayer must be repeated.
B) Sunnah muakkadah, and if omitted the prayer is valid without compensation.
C) Fard, and if omitted the prayer is invalid.
D) Makruh, and it is better not to recite it.

Key Takeaway
Thana is a sunnah muakkadah; its wording is specified, and every worshipper should recite it at the start of prayer.

Definition of Quran and Ruling on Reciting Translation in Prayer
Dispute on Quran's definition and translation ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the definition of Quran and apply the ruling on reciting translation in prayer for Arabic and non-Arabic speakers.

Core Idea
The Quran is the Arabic words and meaning together; translation in prayer is invalid for Arabic speakers but valid if unable.

This lesson explores a fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute: what exactly is the Quran? Is it the meaning alone, or the Arabic words and meaning together? The answer directly affects the validity of prayer when one recites a translation instead of the Arabic text. We will examine the proofs of the majority view (Sahibayn) and understand the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'Quran' is the meaning (ma'na). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is the combination of Arabic words and meaning.
This difference stems from the definition of the term 'Quran'.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proofs
Three proofs are given: verses calling Quran 'Arabic', the command to recite with tartil (which requires Arabic), and the hadith of seven ahruf limiting recitation to Arabic dialects.
These proofs strengthen the Sahibayn's position that the Arabic wording is essential.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: For a person who knows Arabic, reciting a translation in prayer invalidates it according to the Sahibayn, while Abu Hanifa would allow it. For a non-Arabic speaker, necessity allows translation.
This difference matters in real-life prayer for non-Arabic speakers.
4
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: reciting translation is not permissible if one can recite Arabic. If one cannot, it is allowed.
This is based on the strength of the dalil and the majority of later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه : (١) انکی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آیت میں عربی الفاظ کو قرآن کہا ہے، آیت یہ ہے۔ انا أنزلناه قرآنا عربيا لعلكم تعقلون ( آیت ٢ ، سورۃ یوسف (١٢) ، و كذالك أنزلناه قرآنا عربيا و صرفنا فيه من الوعيد - ( آیت ١٣، سورة طه ٢٠) ، انا جعلناه قرآنا عربيا لعلكم تعقلون - ( آیت ٣، سورۃ الزخرف ٤٣) ان آیتوں میں قرآن کو عربی کہا ہے اسلئے عربی لفظ اور معنی دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام قرآن ہے۔ اسلئے جسکو عربی اچھی آتی ہو وہ دوسری زبان میں آیت کا معنی پڑھے گا تو جائز نہیں ہوگا (٢) آیت میں ہے. ورتل القرآن ترتیلا ( آیت ٤ ، سورۃ المزمل ٧٣ ) که قرآن کو ترتیل سے پڑھو اور یہ اسی صورت میں ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ عربی میں ہوا سلئے قرآن عربی الفاظ کا نام ہے۔ (٣) حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے اجازت مانگی تو عرب کے صرف سات لغات میں قرآن پڑھنے کی اجازت دی، اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ انکے علاوہ دوسری زبان میں قرآن پڑھنا جائز نہیں ہوگا ۔ لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابی بن کعب أن النبي الله كان عند أضاة بني غفار قال : فأتاه جبريل عليه السلام فقال : ان الله يأمرك أن تقرأ أمتك القرآن على حرف .... ان الله يأمرك أن تقرأ أمتك القرآن على سبعة احرف ، فأيما حرف قرأوا عليه ، فقد أصابوا - ( مسلم شریف ، باب بیان آن القرآن انزل علی سبعة أحرف و بیان معناها،ص ١٣٢٩، نمبر ١٩٠٦/٨٢ر بخاری شریف ، باب انزل القرآن علی سبعة أحرف ،ص ١٨٩٥، نمبر ٤٩٩١ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عرب کے سات لغات پر ہی پڑھنا جائز ہوگا ، اسکے علاوہ پر نہیں۔
اصول : امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک معنی کا نام قرآن ہے۔۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک عربی عبارت اور معنی دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام قرآن ہے۔۔ البتہ اگر عربی نہیں آتی ہو تو اب مجبوری ہے اسلئے دوسری زبان میں آیت کا معنی پڑھ دے تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔
Proof: (1) His evidence is that in the verse the Arabic words are called Quran. The verse is: 'Indeed, We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran that you might understand.' (Yusuf 12:2) And similarly: 'And thus We have sent it down as an Arabic Quran and have diversified therein the warnings.' (Ta-Ha 20:113) And: 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran that you might understand.' (Az-Zukhruf 43:3) In these verses, Quran is called Arabic, so the name Quran applies to the combination of both Arabic words and meaning. Therefore, for one who knows Arabic well, if he recites the meaning of a verse in another language it will not be permissible. (2) In the verse: 'And recite the Quran with measured recitation.' (Al-Muzzammil 73:4) That you recite the Quran with tartil, and this can only be if it is in Arabic, therefore Quran is the name of the Arabic words. (3) In the hadith, when he asked permission, he only allowed recitation in the seven Arabic dialects. From this it is understood that reciting in other than these languages is not permissible. The portion of the long hadith is: From Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Prophet was at the pond of Banu Ghifar. He said: Jibril came to him and said: 'Allah commands you to recite the Quran to your nation in one dialect... Allah commands you to recite the Quran to your nation in seven dialects; whichever dialect they recite, they are correct.' (Muslim, chapter on statement that the Quran was revealed in seven dialects and explanation of its meaning, p.1329, no.1906/82r; Bukhari, chapter on the revelation of the Quran in seven dialects, p.1895, no.4991) From this hadith it is understood that reciting in only the seven Arabic dialects is permissible, not in other languages.
Principle: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'Quran' is the name of the meaning. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), 'Quran' is the name of the combination of both the Arabic expression and the meaning. However, if one does not know Arabic, then there is necessity, so if he recites the meaning of the verse in another language, the prayer will be valid.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the definition of the Quran and the ruling on reciting its translation in prayer. The author presents three proofs (dalil) that the Quran is the Arabic words themselves, not just the meaning. The proofs are: (1) Quranic verses calling it 'Arabic Quran', (2) the command to recite it with tartil, which requires its Arabic form, and (3) the hadith of seven ahruf limiting recitation to Arabic dialects. These proofs support the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) that the Quran is both the Arabic words and the meaning. Then the author states the usul (principle): Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'Quran' is the meaning (ma'na), while the Sahibayn hold it is the combination of Arabic expression and meaning. The practical difference is: for those who know Arabic, reciting the translation in prayer is not valid according to the Sahibayn, but Abu Hanifa allows it if one does not know Arabic due to necessity (however, his position is that ma'na is Quran, so translation would be considered Quran in meaning). The text notes that if one does not know Arabic, necessity permits reciting the meaning in another language. This ikhtilaf impacts the validity of prayer for non-Arabic speakers.

Key Terms
قرآن (Qur'an): This text debates whether the term refers to the Arabic words, the meaning, or both.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), what is the definition of Quran?
A) Only the meaning (ma'na)
B) Only the Arabic words
C) The combination of Arabic words and meanings
D) Any translation that conveys the message

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that the Quran is the Arabic words and meaning together, making translation in prayer invalid for those who know Arabic but valid for those who cannot.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Placing Hands and Reciting Thana After Takbir: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
States the sunnah of hand placement and thana after takbir with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnah actions after takbir and identify their proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
After takbir, place right hand on left under navel and recite thana — emphasized sunnah, not fard.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the rulings for the initial moments after the takbirat al-tahrimah. The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice, teaches that the worshiper should immediately fold the hands and recite the opening supplication (thana). These acts are sunnah mu'akkadah, meaning they are highly recommended but not obligatory. The passage provides direct hadith evidence for each action and clarifies that the follower (muqtadi) also recites thana.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states two actions: (1) placing right hand on left under navel after takbir without delay, and (2) reciting thana. Both are ruled as sunnah mu'akkadah.
The Urdu commentary emphasizes 'immediately' (بلا مهلة) for hand placement.
2
Locate the dalil for hand placement
The author cites the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr (Muslim) describing the Prophet’s practice: he raised his hands, said takbir, then placed his right hand on left.
This is a fi'l (action) of the Prophet, indicating sunnah.
3
Locate the dalil for thana
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood) reports that the Prophet recited 'Subhanakallahumma...' after takbir when standing for night prayer.
This establishes the specific wording of thana.
4
Understand the follower's recitation of thana
The commentary explains that the follower recites thana himself, unlike Fatiha where the imam's recitation suffices. Thana is a separate sunnah for each worshiper.
This addresses a common misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تركيب الصلوة الاصح. (٤٥٥) ثم وضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته عقب التحريمة بلا مهلة (٤٥٦) مستفتحا وهو ان يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا اله غيرك
ترجمه : (٤٥٥) پھر تحریمہ کے بعد بلا تاخیر داہنا ہاتھ بائیں ہاتھ پر ناف کے نیچے رکھے۔ تشریح : تکبیر تحریمہ کے بعد تحریمہ باندھنے میں دیر نہ کرے، بلکہ فورا ناف کے نیچے دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ کے اوپر رکھے، اور ثناء پڑھے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تکبیر کے بعد فورا ہاتھ باند ھے۔ عن وائل بن حجر انه رأى النبي عل رفع يديه حين دخل في الصلاة كبر - وصف همام حيال اذنيه ـ ثم التحف بثوبه ثم وضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى. (مسلم شریف ، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری ص ١٧٠ نمبر ٨٩٦/٤٠)
ترجمه : (٤٥٦) ثناء پڑھے : سبحانك اللهم و بحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالی جدک ولا اله غیرک ہر ایک نمازی شروع میں ثنا پڑھے۔
تشریح : تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد سبحانک الخ پڑھے، اور یہ مقتدی بھی پڑھے، کیونکہ یہ قرآت کی طرح نہیں ہے کہ امام کی قرآت مقتدی کی قرآت شمار ہو۔ وجه (١) یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ثم يـقـول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالی جدک ولا اله غیرک. (ترمذی شریف، باب ما يقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ، ص ١٥٧، نمبر ٢٤٢ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسجانک ،ص ١٢١ نمبر ٧٧٥)
Chapter on the Composition of Prayer. The most correct view. (455) Then he places his right hand on his left under his navel immediately after the takbir without delay. (456) Opening with the supplication which is that he says: 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghairuk.' (455) Then after the takbir, without delay, place the right hand on the left hand under the navel. Explanation: After the takbirat al-tahrimah, do not delay in folding the hands; rather immediately place the right hand over the left under the navel and recite thana. Proof: In this hadith: that after the takbir, immediately fold the hands. From Wa'il ibn Hujr: that he saw the Prophet raise his hands when entering prayer, say the takbir - and described them parallel to his ears - then he wrapped himself in his garment, then placed his right hand on his left. (Muslim, chapter on placing right hand on left, p.170, no.896/40) (456) Recite thana: 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghairuk.' Every worshiper recites thana at the beginning. Explanation: After folding the hands, recite 'Subhanaka...' and the follower also recites it because it is not like recitation where the imam's recitation suffices for the follower. Proof: (1) This hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: 'When the Messenger of Allah would stand for prayer at night, he would say the takbir, then say: Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghairuk.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on what to say at opening of prayer, p.157, no.242; Abu Dawood, chapter on those who saw opening with Subhanak, p.121, no.775)
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the sunnah actions immediately following the takbirat al-tahrimah. It is a ruling_with_proof type: the author first states the ruling in the matn (the base text) and then provides hadith evidence. The first ruling (455) is that the worshiper should place his right hand on his left hand under the navel without delay after the takbir. The Hanafi school considers this sunnah mu'akkadah. The proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr, which reports that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did this. The second ruling (456) is that the worshiper then recites the thana (opening supplication): 'Subhanakallahumma...'. The commentary clarifies that the follower (muqtadi) also recites this thana, unlike the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah, because thana is a separate sunnah and not part of the imam's recitation that suffices. The proof for thana is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited thana after takbir. Both actions are from the sunnah and are recommended for all worshipers in every prayer.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir that makes the prayer begin and prohibits worldly actions.
ثناء (thana'): The opening supplication 'Subhanakallahumma...' recited after takbir.
مستفتحا (mustaftihan): Opening the prayer with this supplication, i.e., thana.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when should a worshiper place his right hand on his left during prayer?
A) Before the takbirat al-tahrimah
B) Immediately after the takbirat al-tahrimah without delay
C) After reciting thana
D) Only in the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
After takbir, it is sunnah to place right hand on left under navel and recite thana; the follower also recites thana.
